Intercourse After 'Arafah: Expiation, Not Invalidation
Specifies expiation for intercourse after 'Arafah but before shaving; Hanafi position with proof and inter-madhhab dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intercourse after 'Arafah and distinguish it from the position of al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad.

Core Idea
Intercourse after 'Arafah does not invalidate Hajj but requires a badanah; the act enjoys a higher expiation while preserving the Hajj.

What happens if a pilgrim in ihram has intercourse after the essential standing at 'Arafah but before shaving? The Hanafi school makes a key distinction: the Hajj remains valid, yet a heavy expiation is due. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof from Ibn 'Abbas, and the inter-madhhab dispute with those who hold the Hajj invalid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the specific scenario? Intercourse after wuquf at 'Arafah and before tahallul (shaving or stoning). What does the Hanafi school say?
The act is a violation of ihram, but the timing matters.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof is cited? A narration from Ibn 'Abbas and a general hadith about completion of Hajj.
The hadith 'Whoever stands at 'Arafah, his Hajj is complete' is interpreted as safety from invalidation.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
How does the proof support the ruling? The term 'complete' is metaphorical; the Hajj is not literally complete because tawaf al-ziyarah remains. Thus the meaning is that the Hajj is not ruined.
Hanafi usul: zahir is not taken literally here due to context.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Which schools disagree? Al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad say it invalidates. Their proof is qiyas with intercourse before 'Arafah.
The common factor claimed is that both occur before full tahallul.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response and thamarah
How does the Hanafi school rebut the analogy? The completion hadith overrides the qiyas. The practical difference: Hanafi says Hajj valid, expiation badanah; others say Hajj invalid, must be made up plus expiation.
Thamarah al-khilaf: whether the pilgrim must repeat Hajj.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبدنة لو بعده [ أي جامع بعد الوقوف بعرفة . (ط)] عطف على "شاة" أي لو جامع بعد الوقوف قبل الحلق تجب بدنة، كذا روي عن ابن عباس اما، ولا يعرف ذلك إلا سماعاً، ولأنه أعلى الارتفاقات فتغلظ موجبه، ولو كان قارناً فعليه بدنة لحجه وشاة لعمرته، وقوله: "ولا فساد" أي لم يفسد الحج مطلقاً سواء كان قبل الرمي أو بعده؛ لقوله عليك: من وقف بعرفة فقد تم حجه، وحقيقة التمام غير مراد لبقاء طواف الزيارة، وهو ركن، فتعليق التمام الذمة المشقة حكماً بالأمن من الفساد بفراغ عن الواجب، وقال الشافعي: إذا جامع قبل الرمي يفسد، وبه قال مالك وأحمد اعتباراً بالجماع قبل الوقوف، والجامع أن كلا منهما قبل التحلل. [رمز الحقائق: ١٧٤/١] ولا فساد: لحجه سواء كان قبل الرمي أو بعده (ط)
And a badanah if after it [i.e., if he has intercourse after standing at 'Arafah]. This is a conjunction to 'a ram', i.e., if he has intercourse after standing and before shaving, a badanah is obligatory. Thus it is narrated from Ibn 'Abbas, may Allah be pleased with him, and it is not known except by hearing, and because it is the highest form of indulgence so its obligation is made heavy. And if he is a qarin (performing Hajj and 'Umrah together), then upon him is a badanah for his Hajj and a ram for his 'Umrah. And His statement: 'And no invalidation' means that the Hajj is not invalidated at all, whether before the stoning or after it, due to his statement: 'Whoever stands at 'Arafah, his Hajj is complete.' But the reality of completion is not intended because the tawaf al-ziyarah remains, and it is a pillar. So the attachment of completion to the guarantee of difficulty is a legal ruling of safety from invalidation, having finished the obligatory. And al-Shafi'i said: If he has intercourse before the stoning, it invalidates, and Malik and Ahmad also said that, drawing analogy to intercourse before standing at 'Arafah, and the common factor is that both are before tahallul (release from ihram). And there is no invalidation: for his Hajj, whether before stoning or after.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This section addresses a specific scenario: if a person in ihram has intercourse after the essential rite of standing at 'Arafah but before shaving the head (the first tahallul). According to the Hanafi school, this does not invalidate the Hajj, because the standing at 'Arafah is the major pillar; once performed, the Hajj is fundamentally complete, though certain obligations remain (like tawaf al-ziyarah). However, because the person violated the sanctity of ihram at a stage when the prohibitions are lighter, a badanah (camel) is obligatory as expiation. This ruling is attributed to Ibn 'Abbas and is based on the principle that the higher the form of indulgence (the closer to the end of ihram), the heavier the expiation. The text contrasts this with the view of al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad, who hold that intercourse before the stoning of Jamarat on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah invalidates the Hajj entirely, drawing an analogy with intercourse before 'Arafah. The Hanafi response is that the completion of Hajj is metaphorically stated by the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) meaning safety from total loss, not literal completion. The dispute centers on whether the state of tahallul (partial release) has begun.

Key Terms
قارن (qarin): Someone who performs Hajj and 'Umrah combined in a single state of ihram.
لا فساد (la fasad): The Hajj is not invalidated; it remains valid.
بدنة (badanah): A camel offered as sacrifice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a person has intercourse after standing at 'Arafah but before shaving?
A) Hajj is invalidated and must be made up.
B) Hajj is not invalidated but a ram is obligatory.
C) Hajj is not invalidated but a badanah is obligatory.
D) Hajj remains valid with no expiation.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school teaches that intercourse after 'Arafah does not invalidate Hajj but requires a badanah as expiation, distinguishing the stage of Hajj completion from total nullification.

Intercourse After Shaving But Before Tawaf al-Ziyarah
Continues rulings on intercourse at different Hajj stages, specifying the penalty after partial release.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the expiation for intercourse after shaving and before tawaf al-ziyarah and explain why it differs from intercourse before shaving.

Core Idea
Partial ihram means lighter expiation: a ram, not a camel.

In the previous lesson, we learned that intercourse before the first tahallul (shaving) invalidates Hajj and requires a camel. Now we examine a different stage: after shaving but before performing tawaf al-ziyarah. At this point, the pilgrim has partially exited ihram—only sexual relations remain prohibited. The Hanafi school rules that such intercourse requires a ram as expiation, not a camel, because the offense is against a weakened ihram. Understanding this gradation clarifies the legal reasoning behind expiation amounts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Stage of Ihram
Determine whether the pilgrim has performed shaving (halq) or trimming (taqsir) but not yet completed tawaf al-ziyarah. This is the partial release stage.
Shaving is the first act of tahallul; after it, only sexual relations remain forbidden.
2
State the Ruling for Intercourse
If intercourse occurs at this stage, a ram (shah) is wajib as expiation. The Hajj is valid but deficient.
3
Contrast with Full Release
If intercourse occurs after completing all or most (≥4 circuits) of tawaf al-ziyarah, no expiation is required because full release has been achieved.
The threshold for 'most' is four circuits out of seven.
4
Understand the Legal Cause (Ta'lil)
The lighter penalty is based on the principle that the ihram is 'deficient'—only sexual prohibitions remain. The offense is less severe, so a smaller expiation suffices.
This illustrates the Hanafi method of gradation (tadarruj) in penalties.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو جامع بعد الحلق [عطف على ما فيه وجوب الشاة أي تجب عليه شاة إن جامع. (ع)] أي تجب شاة إن جامع بعد الحلق، قيد به؛ لأن الخروج عن الإحرام إنما يكون بالحلق أو التقصير ، ولزوم الشاة بناء على أنه جناية على إحرام ناقص؛ لأنه لم يبق محرما إلا في حق النساء، فخفت الجناية فاكتفى بالشاة، والمراد بعد الحلق قبل طواف الزيارة كله أو أكثره، فإنه لو جامع بعد ما طاف للزيارة كله أو أكثره لا شيء عليه؛ لأنه خرج من إحرامه وحلت له النساء أيضاً. (مسكين) الحلق: قبل طواف الزيارة كله أو أكثره لخفة الجناية لوجود الحل في حق غير النساء فلو بعد ما طاف كله أو أكثره فلا شيء عليه. (ط،ع)
Or he has intercourse after shaving [This is a conjunction to that which has the obligation of a ram; i.e., a ram is obligatory upon him if he has intercourse after shaving. He specified it because exiting from ihram is only by shaving or trimming. And the obligation of a ram is based on it being an offense against a deficient ihram, because he remains in ihram only with respect to women, so the offense became light, so a ram suffices. And what is meant is after shaving and before all or most of tawaf al-ziyarah. If he has intercourse after performing all or most of tawaf al-ziyarah, then nothing is upon him because he has exited his ihram and women become permissible for him.]
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This ruling covers the scenario of intercourse after the first tahallul (shaving or trimming hair) but before completing tawaf al-ziyarah. At this stage, the pilgrim has partially exited ihram: all prohibitions are lifted except for sexual relations with one's spouse. Therefore, if intercourse occurs, it is a less severe violation, and the expiation is a ram (shah), not a badanah. If the person has already performed all or most of tawaf al-ziyarah (defined as four or more circuits), then full release is achieved, and no expiation is required. The reasoning is based on the principle of gradation: as the ihram weakens, the penalty lightens.

Key Terms
شاة (shah): A ram or goat (a small livestock sacrifice) for expiation.
الحلق (al-halq): Shaving the head, which is the first act of tahallul (partial release from ihram).
طواف الزيارة (tawaf al-ziyarah): The obligatory tawaf of the Ka'bah performed after stoning and shaving, also called tawaf al-ifadah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the expiation for intercourse after shaving but before completing most of tawaf al-ziyarah?
A) A camel (badanah)
B) A ram (shah)
C) Nothing
D) A cow

Key Takeaway
Intercourse after shaving but before tawaf al-ziyarah requires a ram; after most of tawaf, no expiation.

Intercourse in 'Umrah: Rulings on Validity and Expiation
Covers the ruling for intercourse during 'Umrah at different stages

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for intercourse in 'Umrah before and after completing most tawaf and explain the difference in expiation compared to Hajj.

Core Idea
In 'Umrah, intercourse before completing four circuits invalidates; after, it does not; a ram is always due.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi rulings on intercourse during 'Umrah. Since 'Umrah is a sunnah while Hajj is fard, the rulings differ in terms of invalidation and expiation. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the ahkam of pilgrimage and avoiding common errors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
We are ruling on intercourse during 'Umrah. The ruling is divided into two scenarios: before performing most tawaf (less than four circuits) and after most tawaf (four or more).
Most tawaf is defined as four circuits out of seven.
2
Apply the ruling for the two scenarios
If intercourse occurs before four circuits, the 'Umrah is invalidated and must be made up, and a ram (shah) is wajib. If after four circuits, the 'Umrah remains valid but a ram is still obligatory.
This is analogous to the ruling in Hajj, where intercourse before 'Arafah invalidates but after does not.
3
Analyze the dalil and talil (evidence and reasoning)
The Hanafi proof is qiyas based on the rank of 'Umrah. Since 'Umrah is sunnah, the expiation is lighter (ram) compared to Hajj (badanah). The tawaf is the pillar of 'Umrah; its majority stands for the whole.
The Shafi'i position is presented and rebutted: they treat 'Umrah as fard, requiring badanah and invalidation in both cases.
4
Note the dispute and its practical consequence
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is that Hanafis require a ram and only invalidate before most tawaf, while Shafi'is require a badanah and invalidate always.
The Hanafi response emphasizes the lower rank of 'Umrah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو في العمرة قبل أن يطوف الأكثر ، وتفسد ويمضي ويقضي ، أو بعد طواف الأكثر وهو أربعة أشواط العمرة بذلك. ولا فساد، وجماعُ النّاسي كالعامد. أو طاف للركن محدثا، لعمرته لوجود أكثرها في الحج والعمرة. أي في حالة الحدث. أو في العمرة: أي يلزمه شاة أيضاً لو جامع في العمرة. (ع) تفسد أي العمرة؛ لوقوع الجماع قبل الإتيان بركنها أي الطواف، فصار كالجماع قبل الوقوف في الحج. (فتح) ويمضي فيها كمن لم يفسد. (ط) أو بعد طواف أي تجب عليه شاة أيضاً إن جامع في العمرة بعد الطواف (ع) ولا فساد: وقال الشافعي: تفسد في الوجهين، أي فيما إذا جامع المعتمر قبل أن يطوف الأكثر أو بعده، وعليه بدنة اعتباراً بالحج؛ إذ العمرة فرض عنده كالحج، ولنا: أنها سنة فكانت أحط رتبة منه فتجب الشاة فيها، والبدنة في الحج إظهاراً للتفاوت بينهما، وطواف العمرة ركن فصار كالوقوف بعرفة، وأكثره يقوم مقام كله تبيين الحقائق: ٣٦٨/٢] (فتح)
Or in 'Umrah before he has performed most of the tawaf, and it invalidates, and he continues and makes it up. Or after the majority of tawaf, which is four circuits, of 'Umrah therein, and no invalidation. And the intercourse of the forgetful is like the intentional. Or if he performs the tawaf of the pillar while in a state of minor impurity, for his 'Umrah due to the existence of most of it in Hajj and 'Umrah. i.e., in a state of hadath. Or in 'Umrah: i.e., a ram is also obligatory upon him if he has intercourse in 'Umrah. It invalidates, i.e., the 'Umrah, because intercourse occurred before performing its pillar, i.e., the tawaf, so it becomes like intercourse before standing at 'Arafah in Hajj. And he continues in it like one who did not invalidate. Or after tawaf, i.e., a ram is also obligatory upon him if he has intercourse in 'Umrah after the tawaf, and no invalidation. And al-Shafi'i said: It invalidates in both cases, i.e., when the performer of 'Umrah has intercourse before he has performed most of the tawaf or after it, and upon him is a badanah, by analogy to Hajj, since 'Umrah is a fard in his view like Hajj. And we [Hanafis say]: it is a sunnah, so it is of a lower rank, so a ram is obligatory in it, and the badanah in Hajj is to show the difference between them. And the tawaf of 'Umrah is a pillar, so it becomes like standing at 'Arafah, and its majority takes the place of the whole.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This section addresses intercourse during 'Umrah. Since 'Umrah is of a lower rank than Hajj (sunnah vs. fard), the expiation is a ram (shah) whether the intercourse occurs before or after performing most of the tawaf. However, the ruling on validity differs: if intercourse occurs before performing most tawaf (i.e., before completing four circuits), the 'Umrah is invalidated and must be made up. If after most tawaf, it remains valid. This is analogous to the ruling in Hajj, where intercourse before 'Arafah invalidates but after does not. The dispute with al-Shafi'i is noted: he equates 'Umrah to Hajj in both rank and expiation, requiring a badanah and ruling invalidation in both cases. The Hanafi response is that 'Umrah is sunnah, hence lighter expiation; the tawaf is its main pillar, and performing most of it is like completing it.

Key Terms
الأكثر (al-akthar): The majority of tawaf, which is four circuits out of seven.
العمرة (al-'umrah): A ritual visit to Makkah including tawaf and sa'y, considered sunnah in Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafis, if a person has intercourse in 'Umrah after completing four circuits of tawaf, what is the ruling?
A) 'Umrah is invalidated, must make up, and a badanah is due.
B) 'Umrah is invalidated, must make up, and a ram is due.
C) 'Umrah is not invalidated, and a ram is due.
D) 'Umrah is not invalidated, and no expiation is due.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the ruling for intercourse in 'Umrah depends on the stage of tawaf, with a ram as expiation but invalidation only before completing the majority.

Forgetful Intercourse During Ihram: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Discusses the ruling of intercourse out of forgetfulness, ignorance, or coercion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on forgetful intercourse during ihram and distinguish it from the Shafi'i position, applying the principle of 'irtifaq' and the analogy with prayer.

Core Idea
Forgetfulness does not excuse invalidation of ihram because indulgence is present, but it removes sin.

This lesson addresses a critical distinction in Hanafi fiqh: while forgetfulness may remove sin, it does not necessarily remove the legal consequences of an act. The source text examines intercourse during ihram by a forgetful person, and contrasts the Hanafi view with that of Imam al-Shafi'i. Understanding this ruling requires grasping the Hanafi concept of 'irtifaq' (indulgence) and the reminding nature of ihram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
State that forgetful intercourse invalidates ihram, requiring make-up and expiation, but no sin.
This is the mufta bihi position from Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position
State that forgetful intercourse does not invalidate ihram; it is excused like in fasting.
Shafi'i bases this on qiyas with fasting.
3
Follow the Shafi'i dalil
Understand the analogy: just as forgetting breaks the fast without invalidating or requiring expiation, so too with ihram.
Qiyas with fasting is the core of the Shafi'i argument.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Examine the Hanafi rebuttal: ihram resembles prayer (constant reminder), not fasting (no reminder), so forgetfulness does not excuse.
The reminding nature of ihram is key to the Hanafi distinction.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: Hanafi requires make-up and expiation; Shafi'i does not invalidate.
This difference affects pilgrims in real life.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجماع الناسي: وكذا المخطي والجاهل؛ لاستواء الكل في الارتفاق وقال الشافعي: لا يفسد جماع الناسي، وكذا الخلاف في جماع المكرهة والنائمة هو يقول: إن فعله لم يقع جناية لعدم الحظر مع العذر فشابه الصوم حيث لا تلزمه الكفارة بالفطر في رمضان مكرهاً ولنا أن الفساد باعتبار معنى الارتفاق في الإحرام ارتفاقا مخصوصا وهو الجماع، وهذا لا ينعدم بعوارض النسيان وغيره فيقع جناية، ولا تفسد الصوم بالجماع والأكل أنهما يفوتان ركن الصوم وهو الإمساك؛ لأن هنا هيئة المحرم وحالات الإحرام مذكرة له كما أن الكلام ناسيا يفسد الصلاة بناء على أن هيئة الصلاة مذكرة بخلاف الصوم؛ لأنه ليس فيه هيئة مذكرة فاعتبر النسيان فيه عذرا. (عيني، مستخلص كالعامد في غير الإثم من الأحكام؛ لاستوائهما في الارتفاق، وكذا جماع النائمة والمكرهة مفسد خلافاً للشافعي. (ط،ع)
And the intercourse of the forgetful: and likewise the mistaken and the ignorant; because all are equal in indulgence. And al-Shafi'i said: The intercourse of the forgetful does not invalidate. Similarly, the disagreement applies to the intercourse of the coerced and the sleeping woman. He says: his action did not constitute an offense because prohibition is absent due to the excuse, so it resembles fasting where the expiation for breaking the fast in Ramadan under coercion is not obligatory. And we [Hanafis say]: invalidation is based on the meaning of indulgence in ihram, a specific indulgence which is intercourse, and this is not nullified by incidental forgetfulness etc., so it constitutes an offense. And fasting is not invalidated by intercourse and eating because they destroy the essence of fasting, which is abstention; but here, the state of the person in ihram and the conditions of ihram serve as a reminder for him, just as speaking forgetfully invalidates prayer because the state of prayer is a reminder, unlike fasting, because it has no reminding state, so forgetfulness is considered an excuse in fasting.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage resolves the issue of intercourse committed out of forgetfulness, ignorance, or mistake during ihram. According to the Hanafi school, such acts still invalidate the Hajj or 'Umrah, because the essence of the violation—indulgence in sexual relations—is present. The forgetful person is treated the same as the intentional one regarding the obligation to continue, make up, and offer expiation; however, no sin is recorded because the intention was absent. The text contrasts this with al-Shafi'i's view, who holds that forgetfulness removes the invalidation, drawing an analogy with fasting under coercion where expiation is not required. The Hanafi response distinguishes ihram from fasting: ihram has a 'reminding' nature (the special clothing and prohibitions are constant reminders), similar to prayer, where forgetful speech invalidates. Fasting lacks such a reminding quality, so forgetfulness is excused. The same ruling applies to the coerced person and the sleeping woman: if intercourse occurs, the ihram is invalidated, contrary to al-Shafi'i.

Key Terms
الناسي (al-nasi): One who forgets that they are in ihram and performs intercourse.
ارتفاق (irtifaq): Indulgence or benefit; the pleasure derived from an act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafis, what is the ruling if a person in ihram forgetfully has intercourse?
A) His ihram is not invalidated, and no expiation is required.
B) His ihram is invalidated, and he must make up and offer expiation, but no sin.
C) His ihram is invalidated, and he must make up and offer expiation, and he incurs sin.
D) His ihram is not invalidated, but he must offer expiation.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, forgetful intercourse during ihram invalidates the pilgrimage and requires expiation, but no sin is recorded, because the indulgence (irtifaq) is present and ihram serves as a constant reminder.

Ruling on Performing Tawaf with Impurity
Discusses the expiation for performing tawaf al-ziyarah with impurity and explains the Hanafi vs Shafi'i difference.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing tawaf al-ziyarah in a state of impurity and explain the expiation required for minor and major impurity.

Core Idea
Tawaf with impurity is valid but deficient – a ram for hadath, a camel for janabah.

This passage addresses an important Hajj issue: what happens if a pilgrim performs the obligatory tawaf al-ziyarah without ritual purity? The Hanafi school takes a pragmatic view – the tawaf counts, but the pilgrim must pay an expiation (dam) for the deficiency. The passage explains the rulings for both minor impurity (hadath) and major impurity (janabah), contrasting the Hanafi view with that of Imam al-Shafi'i, who requires purity for tawaf to be valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the two types of impurity
The act is tawaf al-ziyarah (the essential tawaf of Hajj). The passage distinguishes between minor impurity (hadath) and major impurity (janabah). Determine which expiation applies for each.
Hadath includes being without wudu; janabah requires ghusl.
2
State the Hanafi ruling for each case
For hadath: a ram (shah) is wajib. For janabah: a badanah (camel) is wajib. The tawaf itself is valid (yu'taddu bihi) but deficient.
The expiation is wajib, not sunnah or optional.
3
Identify the Hanafi primary proof (dalil)
The Quranic verse (al-Hajj 29) 'And let them circumambulate the Ancient House' is absolute and contains no condition of purity. Adding purity would be an addition to the text (ziyadah), which is akin to abrogation (naskh).
The verse is qat'i al-thubut but zanni al-dalalah.
4
Analyze the opposing proof and the Hanafi response
The Shafi'i school cites the hadith 'Tawaf around the House is a prayer,' implying purity is a condition. The Hanafi response argues that the hadith is a solitary report (khabar wahid) and cannot abrogate the Quran. Moreover, the comparison is only in reward, not in rulings, as evidenced by differences like walking and talking not invalidating tawaf.
The Hanafi response uses a linguistic and usul argument.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Hanafi: tawaf valid, expiation wajib. Shafi'i: tawaf invalid, must be repeated. This affects the pilgrim's Hajj: Hanafi allows completion without repeating tawaf but requires sacrifice; Shafi'i requires repeating the tawaf, which may be difficult after leaving Makkah.
The difference is significant in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(ع)] لما فرغ من باب الجناية على الإحرام ذكر الجناية على الطواف الذي هو بعد الإحرام، وقيد الطواف بالمحدث؛ لأن الطواف مع المائعة مكروه فقط، وقوله: "وبدنة لو جنبا روي ذلك عن ابن عباس هما؛ ولأن الجنابة أغلظ الحدث فغلظ من موجبها إظهارا للتفاوت، ويعتد بهذا الطواف عندنا وعند الشافعي: لا يعتد به أصلا؛ لقوله، علية: "الطواف بالبيت صلاة" فيكون من شرطه الطهارة. ولنا قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلْيَطَّوَّفُوا بِالْبَيْتِ الْعَتِيقِ (الحج:٢٩) من غير قيد بالطهارة، فاشتراط الطهارة فيه يكون زيادة على النص، وهي نسخ فلا تثبت بخبر الواحد، والمراد بالحديث تشبيه الطواف بالصلاة في الثواب دون الحكم، ألا ترى أن المشي والانحراف عن القبلة والكلام لا يفسد الطواف ويفسد الصلاة، ثم قيل عندنا الطهارة سنة، والصحيح أنها واجبة. (عيني فتح للركن أي لأجله وهو طواف الزيارة. (ع)
Or he performed the tawaf of the pillar, etc. [This is a conjunction to that which has the obligation of a ram, i.e., a ram is obligatory if he performs tawaf in a state of impurity.] When he finished the section on offenses against ihram, he mentioned offenses against tawaf, which comes after ihram. He restricted tawaf to that with impurity because tawaf with non-fluid impurity is only makruh. And his statement: 'And a badanah if he is in a state of janabah'; this is narrated from Ibn 'Abbas, because janabah is the severer impurity, so its obligation is made heavy to show the difference. And this tawaf is considered valid according to us [Hanafis], whereas according to al-Shafi'i: it is not considered at all, due to his statement: 'Tawaf around the House is a prayer', so purity is a condition. And we [Hanafis] rely on the verse: 'And let them circumambulate the Ancient House' (al-Hajj 29) without any condition of purity. So stipulating purity would be an addition to the text, which would be abrogation, and that cannot be established by a solitary report. The intended meaning of the hadith is to liken tawaf to prayer in reward, not in ruling. Do you not see that walking, turning away from the qiblah, and talking do not invalidate tawaf, whereas they invalidate prayer? Then it is said in our school that purity is sunnah, but the correct view is that it is wajib.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage covers the violation of performing tawaf al-ziyarah while in a state of impurity. According to the Hanafi school, tawaf is valid even without purity, but expiation is required: a ram if in minor impurity (hadath), and a badanah if in major impurity (janabah). The text cites Ibn 'Abbas for the janabah ruling. The proof is the Quranic verse (al-Hajj 29) which commands tawaf without mentioning purity. The hadith 'Tawaf is prayer' is interpreted as a comparison in reward, not in legal conditions, because walking, talking, etc., do not break tawaf as they do prayer. Therefore, purity is not a condition of validity but a wajib requirement. The passage also notes the disagreement with al-Shafi'i, who considers purity a condition and does not count the tawaf at all. Some Hanafi scholars say purity is sunnah, but the mu'tamad (correct view) is that it is wajib (hence the expiation).

Key Terms
محدث (muhdith): One who is in a state of minor impurity (without wudu) or major impurity (janabah).
جنب (junub): One in need of ritual bath (ghusl) due to sexual activity or seminal discharge.
يعتد به (yu'taddu bihi): It is considered (valid) as a fulfillment of the required tawaf.

B) A badanah (camel)
C) Nothing; the tawaf is invalid and must be repeated.
D) Sadaqah (charity)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits tawaf without purity, requiring an animal sacrifice as compensation, balancing textual evidence with practical facilitation.

Intercourse in Umrah: Invalidation and Penalty
Ruling on invalidation of Umrah by intercourse and forgetful intercourse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intercourse in Umrah before and after most tawaf, and explain why forgetful intercourse invalidates like intentional.

Core Idea
Intercourse before most tawaf invalidates Umrah; after most tawaf it does not, but a shah is due.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a crucial issue in Umrah: when does sexual intercourse invalidate the pilgrimage? The answer depends on whether it occurs before or after completing most of the tawaf, and it also covers the case of forgetfulness. The Hanafi school distinguishes between Umrah and Hajj due to the difference in their legal status (sunnah vs. fard). Let's explore the rulings and the madhhab dispute with al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The passage covers three cases: intercourse before most tawaf, after most tawaf, and forgetful intercourse. Identify each and the ruling attached.
Most tawaf is defined as four circuits in Umrah.
2
State the Hanafi position for each
For before most tawaf: Umrah invalidated, must complete and repeat. After most tawaf: valid but a sheep (shah) is due. Forgetful: same as intentional in invalidation.
Forgetful person is not sinful but the act still invalidates.
3
Identify the Shafi'i opposing view
Al-Shafi'i holds that Umrah is invalidated in both before and after, and requires a camel (badanah). Forgetful intercourse does not invalidate.
This stems from considering Umrah as fard like Hajj.
4
Analyze the Hanafi proof and rebuttal
The Hanafi proof: Umrah is sunnah (lower rank) so penalty is lighter; analogy to Hajj is not exact. For forgetfulness: ihram is a constant reminder, so forgetfulness is not an excuse, unlike fasting.
The key distinction is the 'constant reminder' nature of ihram.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi allows Umrah to continue after most tawaf with a shah; Shafi'i invalidates entirely requiring a camel. For forgetfulness, Hanafi invalidates, Shafi'i does not.
This affects whether the Umrah must be repeated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Or in Umrah before he circumambulates the majority, it becomes invalid and he proceeds and makes up; or after circumambulating the majority, which is four circuits in Umrah, there is no invalidation. And intercourse of the forgetful is like the intentional. Or he circumambulated for the pillar in a state of hadath... The commentary explains the rulings and disputes with al-Shafi'i.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq deals with the invalidation of Umrah due to sexual intercourse. It states that if intercourse occurs before completing most of the tawaf (four circuits), the Umrah is invalidated and must be completed and repeated. If after most of the tawaf, the Umrah remains valid but a sheep (shah) is due. The author then discusses the case of a forgetful person, equating it to the intentional in terms of invalidation but not sin. A dispute with al-Shafi'i is presented: al-Shafi'i holds that Umrah is invalidated in both cases and requires a camel, as he considers Umrah obligatory like Hajj. The Hanafi response is that Umrah is a sunnah, so a lighter penalty (shah) suffices. For forgetfulness, the Hanafi argument is that the state of ihram is a constant reminder, unlike fasting, so forgetfulness does not excuse the invalidation.

Key Terms
العمرة (al-‘umrah): The minor pilgrimage, considered sunnah mu’akkadah in Hanafi school as per this text.
الجماع (al-jimā‘): Sexual intercourse, a prohibited act in ihram that may invalidate the pilgrimage.
الناسي (al-nāsī): One who forgets they are in ihram and commits prohibited acts; ruling as intentional in invalidation.

C) 'Umrah is not invalidated but requires a shah (sheep).
D) 'Umrah is not invalidated and nothing is required.

Key Takeaway
In Umrah, intercourse before most tawaf invalidates the pilgrimage; after most tawaf it does not invalidate but requires a shah; forgetfulness does not excuse invalidation.

Tawaf with Hadath and Janabah: Ruling, Penalty, and Proof
Ruling on validity and penalty for tawaf with impurity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tawaf performed in a state of impurity, identify the required compensation for minor and major impurity, and explain the Hanafi proof against the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Purification is not a condition for tawaf; it is valid but deficient, requiring compensation: badanah for janabah, sadaqah for hadath.

The tawaf (circumambulation) around the Kaaba is a central ritual of Hajj. A common question concerns its validity if performed without proper purification. The Hanafi school offers a detailed ruling distinguishing between minor and major impurity, and provides specific compensation. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its evidence, and the dispute with other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of impurity
Distinguish between hadath (minor impurity, e.g., breaking wudu) and janabah (major impurity requiring ghusl). These are the only two states of impurity that affect tawaf; other impurities (e.g., najasah on garment) are treated separately.
The text specifies that tawaf with flowing impurity (mā'i'a) is only makruh, not discussed here.
2
State the penalty for each
For janabah: a badanah (camel) and repetition of the tawaf (wajib). For hadath: sadaqah (half a sa' of wheat per circuit) and repetition recommended (mandub).
If repeated during the days of nahr (sacrifice), the penalty is waived.
3
Understand the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on timing
If tawaf in janabah is repeated after the days of nahr, Abu Hanifa requires a dam (sheep), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say nothing is due. The text prefers the two companions' view for hadath (repetition recommended) but for janabah repetition is obligatory.
The mufta bihi position is that repetition is wajib for janabah and mandub for hadath.
4
Analyze the proof from Quran and hadith
The Hanafi proof rests on Quran 22:29 ('...and let them circumambulate the Ancient House') which does not mention purity. The hadith 'Tawaf is prayer' is interpreted as a metaphor for reward, not a legal analogy. Requiring purification would be an addition to the Quran, which cannot be established by a single hadith (khabar wahid).
The Shafi'i school uses the same hadith to require purification as a condition.
5
Compare with the Shafi'i position
Shafi'i: tawaf without purification is invalid and must be repeated, no compensation. Hanafi: valid but deficient, with compensation. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is whether the pilgrim must simply pay compensation or repeat the tawaf entirely.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi in the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو طاف للركن إلخ [عطف على ما فيه وجوب الشاة أي تجب شاة إن طاف. (ع)] لما فرغ من باب الجناية على الإحرام ذكر الجناية على الطواف الذي هو بعد الإحرام، وقيد الطواف بالمحدث؛ لأن الطواف مع المائعة مكروه فقط، وقوله: 'وبدنة لو جنبا روي ذلك عن ابن عباس هما؛ ولأن الجنابة أغلظ الحدث فغلظ موجبها إظهارا للتفاوت، ويعتد بهذا الطواف عندنا وعند الشافعي: لا يعتد به أصلا؛ لقوله، عليه: 'الطواف بالبيت صلاة' فيكون من شرطه الطهارة. ولنا قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلْيَطَّوَّفُوا بِالْبَيْتِ الْعَتِيقِ (الحج:٢٩) من غير قيد بالطهارة، فاشتراط الطهارة فيه يكون زيادة على النص، وهي نسخ فلا تثبت بخبر الواحد، والمراد بالحديث تشبيه الطواف بالصلاة في الثواب دون الحكم، ألا ترى أن المشي والانحراف عن القبلة والكلام لا يفسد الطواف ويفسد الصلاة، ثم قيل عندنا الطهارة سنة، والصحيح أنها واجبة. (عيني فتح للركن أي لأجله وهو طواف الزيارة. (ع)] الواو بمعنى 'أو'؛ لأن الواجب ليس خصوص الدم، بل إما هو أو الإعادة ما دام بمكة، ولا ذبح عليه في الصورتين أي الحدث والجنابة، وهو محمول على ما إذا أعاده في أيام النحر، والإعادة أفضل، وفي بعض النسخ:' عليه أن يعيد'، والأصح أن يعيد في الحدث ندباً وفي الجنابة وجوباً؛ لكمال الجناية فيها وقصورها في الحدث، ثم إن أعاده وقد طافه محدثاً لا دم عليه ولو بعد أيام النحر، فإن أعاده وقد طافه جنباً في أيام النحر لا شيء عليه؛ لأنه أعاده في وقته، وإن أعاده بعد أيام النحر يجب دم عند أبي حنيفة؛ للتأخير عن أيام النحر، وعندهما: لا يجب شيء، ولو رجع إلى أهله وقد طافه جنباً عليه أن يعود ويعيد بإحرام جديد؛ لأن الطواف الأول معتد به في حق التحليل وليس أن يدخل مكة بغير إحرام فيلزمه إحرام جديد لدخول مكة، وقيل: يعود بذلك الإحرام، وإن لم يعد وبعث بدنة جاز إلا أن الأفضل أن يعود، وفي 'المحيط': بعث الدم أفضل؛ لأن الطواف وقع معتداً به، وفيه نفع الفقراء، ولو رجع إلى أهله وقد طافه محدثاً إن عاد وطاف جاز، وإن بعث بالشاة فهو الأفضل؛ لنفع الفقراء وتخفيف الجناية. (فتح، مسكين) وصدقة لو محدثاً: الصدقة نصف صاع من الحنطة لكل شوط، وقوله: 'للقدوم والصدر' وكذا لكل طواف هو تطوع جبراً لما دخله من النقص بترك الطهارة، وهو وإن وجب بالشروع إلا أنه اكتفى فيه بالصدقة إظهاراً لدنو رتبته عن الواجب بإيجابه تعالى، وإنما وجبت الصدقة بطواف الصدر محدثاً دون الدم؛ إظهاراً للتفاوت بينه وبين طواف الزيارة، وعن أبي حنيفة في طواف الصدر محدثاً شاة؛ لأن ما وجب بإيجابه تعالى أقوى من ما وجب بالشروع، ولو طاف للصدر جنبا فعليه شاة؛ لأنه نقص كثير، ثم هو دون طواف الزيارة، فيكتفي بالشاة، فإن أعاده طاهراً شيء عليه. (مسكين، فتح للقدوم أي لطواف القدوم وهو سنة لكنه صار واجباً بالشروع. (مسكين) والصدر وهو واجب ولكنه أدنى من طواف الزيارة، وكذا في كل طواف هو تطوع. (مسكين)
Or he circumambulated for the pillar... When he finished the chapter on violations of ihram, he mentioned violations concerning tawaf... He restricted tawaf to one with hadath... a camel (badanah) if he is in janabah... and he repeats it. Commentary
This passage discusses tawaf performed in a state of impurity. It begins by specifying that the discussion concerns tawaf with minor impurity (hadath) and major impurity (janabah). The ruling is that while tawaf is not invalidated by impurity, it requires compensation: a camel (badanah) and repetition for janabah, and a sadaqah (half a sa' of wheat per circuit) for hadath. The text then engages a dispute with al-Shafi'i, who considers purification a condition for validity based on the hadith 'Tawaf is prayer.' The Hanafi response is that the Quranic command (22:29) does not mention purity, so requiring it would be an addition that cannot be established by a single hadith. The hadith is interpreted as metaphorical. The passage also details that if one repeats the tawaf during the days of sacrifice, the penalty is waived; if after, Abu Hanifa requires a dam, while the two companions disagree. If the person has already returned home, he must return with a new ihram for janabah, or may send compensation.

Key Terms
الطواف (al-ṭawāf): Circumambulation around the Kaaba; the obligatory tawaf is tawaf al-ziyarah.
الحدث (al-ḥadath): Minor ritual impurity (e.g., breaking wudu); its state during tawaf requires sadaqah per circuit.
الجنابة (al-janābah): Major ritual impurity requiring ghusl; tawaf in this state requires badanah and repetition.
البدنة (al-badanah): A camel offered as expiation for violating ihram, specifically for tawaf in janabah.
الصدقة (al-ṣadaqah): Here, half a sa' of wheat per circuit as compensation for tawaf with hadath.

A) He must give sadaqah (half sa' per circuit).
B) He must sacrifice a badanah (camel) and repeat the tawaf.
C) He must give a shah (sheep) only.
D) The tawaf is invalid and he must repeat it without any sacrifice.

Key Takeaway
Tawaf with impurity is valid in the Hanafi school but requires compensation; purification is wajib, not a condition.

Leaving Parts of the Obligatory Tawaf
Ruling on leaving less than half vs more than half of the obligatory tawaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for leaving less than half vs more than half of the obligatory tawaf and identify the consequence of each.

Core Idea
Leaving 1-2 circuits of tawaf al-ziyarah requires a shah; leaving 4+ circuits invalidates the tawaf and the pilgrim remains in ihram.

This lesson clarifies the Hanafi ruling on a pilgrim who omits some circuits of the obligatory tawaf (tawaf al-ziyarah). The key is the threshold of half: leaving a small part is compensable by a sacrifice, while leaving a majority makes the tawaf void and keeps the pilgrim in ihram. The distinction is based on whether the deficiency is minor or major.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its parts
Tawaf al-ziyarah consists of 7 circuits. In Hanafi, the first 4 circuits are the rukn (pillar) and the remaining 3 are wajib. Determine how many circuits the pilgrim omitted.
The ruling distinguishes between omission of less than half (1-2 circuits) and more than half (4 or more circuits) of the rukn portion.
2
Classify the omission as minor or major
If the omitted circuits are 1 or 2, the deficiency is considered minor (less than half of the rukn). If 4 or more are omitted, it is major (more than half of the rukn).
The text defines 'more than half' as 4 circuits and above.
3
Apply the ruling for minor omission
For 1-2 circuits omitted, the pilgrim owes one shah (sheep) as compensation. He may send the shah even if he has returned home; he does not need to return to Makkah.
This is because the deficiency is minor and can be patched with blood (dam).
4
Apply the ruling for major omission
For 4 or more circuits omitted, the tawaf is considered not performed. The pilgrim remains in ihram indefinitely, prohibited from women, until he completes the tawaf. If he returns home, he must go back with the same ihram.
The majority (akthar) has the legal status of the whole, so omitting it is like performing no tawaf at all.
5
Note the exception regarding tawaf al-sadr
The ruling on leaving less than half applies only if the pilgrim has not performed tawaf al-sadr (farewell tawaf). If he has, the deficiency is handled differently (sadaqah or dam).
This is a subtle detail not fully elaborated in the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو ترك أقل إلخ [عطف على ما فيه وجوب الشاة أي تجب شاة إن ترك. (ط)] أي ترك شوطاً أو شوطين أو من طواف الزيارة فعليه شاة؛ لأن النقصان يسير، فينجر بالدم كما في النقصان بسبب الحدث، ولو رجع إلى أهله جاز أن لا يعود ويبعث شاة، ثم هذا الترك لا يتصور إلا إذا لم يكن طاف للصدر، أما إذا طاف له انتقل إلى طواف الزيارة ما يكمله، ثم ينظر في الباقي من الصدر إن كان أقله لزمه صدقة وإلا فدم. (فتح) ولو ترك أكثره إلخ [ أي أكثر طواف الركن وهو أربعة أشواط فصاعداً. (ع)] لأن للأكثر حكم الكل فصار كأن لم يطف أصلاً. [تبيين الحقائق: ۳۷۰/۲] وقوله: 'بقي محرماً' أي . النساء دائماً ومستمراً حتى يطوف للزيارة. (فتح) محرماً: أبدا عن النساء حتى يطوفه، وإن رجع إلى أهله فعليه أن يعود بذلك الإحرام. (ط)
Or he left less [than half, i.e., 1 or 2 circuits from tawaf al-ziyarah], so a shah is due; because the deficiency is minor. If he returned to his family, it is permissible not to return and send a shah. This leaving is only conceivable if he has not performed tawaf al-sadr. And if he left more [than half, i.e., 4 or more circuits], he remains in ihram indefinitely until he performs the tawaf.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This section addresses the case where a pilgrim leaves out some circuits of the obligatory tawaf (tawaf al-ziyarah). If he leaves one or two circuits (less than half), a shah (sheep) is required as the deficiency is minor. He may pay it even if he has returned home. However, if he leaves three circuits (which is the majority, i.e., more than half), he remains in ihram and is prohibited from women until he completes the tawaf. If he returns home, he must go back with the same ihram. The text distinguishes between leaving less than half (one or two circuits) and more than half (three or more circuits). The rule is that the majority (three circuits) has the status of the whole, so omitting it is like not having performed the tawaf at all.

Key Terms
طواف الركن (ṭawāf al-rukn): The obligatory tawaf of Hajj, also called tawaf al-ziyarah; consists of 7 circuits, of which 4 are considered the rukn (pillar) and 3 are wajib.
الشوط (al-shawṭ): One complete circuit around the Kaaba.
الأقل والأكثر (al-aqall wa al-akthar): Here, less than half means 1-2 circuits (of the rukn portion); more than half means 4+ circuits (of the rukn portion).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He must return and complete the tawaf, no penalty.
B) He must return and complete, and also pay a shah.
C) He can send a shah and be free from ihram.
D) He remains in ihram until he completes the tawaf.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, leaving 1-2 circuits of tawaf al-ziyarah requires a shah, while leaving 4 or more circuits invalidates the tawaf and the pilgrim remains in ihram until completing it.

Ruling for Tawaf al-Ziyarah in Janabah or Hadath
States expiation and repetition for tawaf in impurity with intra-Hanafi difference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the expiation required for tawaf al-ziyarah performed while junub and hadath, and identify the intra-Hanafi difference regarding repetition after the days of nahr.

Core Idea
Tawaf in impurity is valid but requires expiation: a badanah for janabah, a sadaqah for hadath.

Tawaf al-ziyarah is a fard of Hajj, but performing it while impure does not invalidate it; rather, expiation and repetition are required. This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq with its commentary clarifies the obligations and differences among Hanafi imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of impurity
Distinguish between janabah (major impurity) and hadath (minor impurity). The passage prescribes a badanah for janabah and a sadaqah for hadath for the tawafs of arrival and departure.
2
Understand the general rule of expiation
The obligation is either to repeat the tawaf in a pure state or to offer a blood sacrifice. The waw in the matn means 'or' because the specific sacrifice is not required; the choice is between repetition or sacrifice while still in Makkah.
3
Recognize the time sensitivity
If the repetition occurs during the days of nahr (10th to 13th of Dhul Hijjah), no additional dam is due. If repetition is delayed after the days of nahr, Abu Hanifa holds a dam is obligatory due to the delay; the Sahibayn hold nothing is due.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Analyze the scenario of returning home
If the pilgrim returns home without repeating tawaf after janabah, he must go back to Makkah with a new ihram and repeat, or he may send a badanah. For hadath, it is permissible to return and tawaf or send a shah.
The text from Al-Muhit prefers sending the blood sacrifice as it benefits the poor.
5
Apply the preferred view
The later authorities (Al-Muhit, Fath al-Qadir) consider sending the sacrifice as better than returning, because the tawaf is considered valid and the poor benefit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بدنة لو جنباً ويعيده، وصدقة لو محدثاً للقدوم والصدر أو ترك أقل طواف أي تجب بدنة أي طاف جنباً الركن، ولو ترك أكثره بقي محرماً طاف وهو ثلاثة أشواط فأقل ويعيده [ أي يجب عليه الطواف في الجنابة والحدث جميعاً؛ ليأتي به على وجه الكمال. (ع)] الواو بمعنى "أو"؛ لأن الواجب ليس خصوص الدم، بل إما هو أو الإعادة ما دام بمكة، ولا ذبح عليه في الصورتين أي الحدث والجنابة، وهو محمول على ما إذا أعاده في أيام النحر، والإعادة أفضل، وفي بعض النسخ:" عليه أن يعيد"، والأصح أن يعيد في الحدث ندباً وفي الجنابة وجوباً؛ لكمال الجناية فيها وقصورها في الحدث، ثم إن أعاده وقد طافه محدثاً لا دم عليه ولو بعد أيام النحر، فإن أعاده وقد طافه جنباً في أيام النحر لا شيء عليه؛ لأنه أعاده في وقته، وإن أعاده بعد أيام النحر يجب دم عند أبي حنيفة؛ للتأخير عن أيام النحر، وعندهما: لا يجب شيء، ولو رجع إلى أهله وقد طافه جنباً عليه أن يعود ويعيد بإحرام جديد؛ لأن الطواف الأول معتد به في حق التحليل وليس أن يدخل مكة بغير إحرام فيلزمه إحرام جديد لدخول مكة، وقيل: يعود بذلك الإحرام، وإن لم يعد وبعث بدنة جاز إلا أن الأفضل أن يعود، وفي "المحيط": بعث الدم أفضل؛ لأن الطواف وقع معتداً به، وفيه نفع الفقراء، ولو رجع إلى أهله وقد طافه محدثاً إن عاد وطاف جاز، وإن بعث بالشاة فهو الأفضل؛ لنفع الفقراء وتخفيف الجناية.
A badanah is due if he performed tawaf while junub and he should repeat it; and a sadaqah is due if he performed tawaf while in a state of hadath for the tawaf of arrival and departure, or if he left out a small part of tawaf. That is, a badanah is due if he performed tawaf al-rukn while junub. And if he left out most of it, he remains in ihram. He performed tawaf consisting of three circuits or less and should repeat it. [It is obligatory for him to perform tawaf in both states of janabah and hadath, so that he performs it perfectly.] The waw is in the sense of 'or', because the obligation is not specifically the blood sacrifice, but either it or the repetition as long as he is in Makkah. There is no slaughter upon him in both cases, i.e., hadath and janabah, and this is interpreted as when he repeats it during the days of nahr. Repetition is better. In some copies: 'upon him to repeat.' The most correct is that he repeats in hadath as a recommendation, and in janabah as an obligation, because the offense is greater in janabah and lesser in hadath. Then if he repeats after having performed tawaf while in hadath, there is no dam upon him even if after the days of nahr. If he repeats after having performed tawaf while junub during the days of nahr, nothing is due because he repeated in its time. If he repeats after the days of nahr, a dam is obligatory according to Abu Hanifah due to the delay beyond the days of nahr, while according to them (the two companions) nothing is due. If he returns to his family after having performed tawaf while junub, he must go back and repeat with a new ihram, because the first tawaf is valid for the purpose of tahlil, and he cannot enter Makkah without ihram, so a new ihram for entering Makkah is necessary. It is said: he returns with that same ihram. If he does not return but sends a badanah, it is permissible, but the better is to return. In Al-Muhit: Sending the blood is better because the tawaf is considered valid and it benefits the poor. If he returns to his family after having performed tawaf while in hadath, if he returns and performs tawaf, it is permissible, and if he sends a shah, that is better for benefitting the poor and lightening the offense.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling for tawaf al-ziyarah performed while in a state of major impurity (janabah) or minor impurity (hadath). The matn states that a badanah is due for janabah, and a sadaqah for hadath for the tawafs of arrival and departure. The commentary explains that the obligation is either to repeat the tawaf in a pure state or to offer a blood sacrifice, as long as one is in Makkah. Repetition is better. There is an intra-Hanafi difference: if one repeats the tawaf after the days of nahr, Abu Hanifa holds that a dam is due for the delay, while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that nothing is due. The text also discusses the scenario of returning home without repeating: one must go back and repeat with a new ihram, though it is permissible to send a badanah. The preference according to Al-Muhit is to send the blood sacrifice because it benefits the poor and the tawaf is considered valid.

Key Terms
بدنة (badanah): A camel or cow slaughtered as an expiatory sacrifice in Hajj.
جنب (junub): A state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.
محدث (muhdith): A state of minor ritual impurity without wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He must return to Makkah with a new ihram and repeat the tawaf, or send a badanah.
B) He must repeat the tawaf with a new ihram but cannot send a badanah.
C) He is free from any obligation once he returns home.
D) He must sacrifice a shah as expiation.

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-ziyarah performed in impurity is valid but requires expiation and repetition; the Hanafi school has an internal difference on the necessity of dam for delayed repetition.

Sadaqah for Tawaf with Hadath and Missing Parts of Tawaf al-Ziyarah
Details sadaqah for hadath and shah for missing ziyarah circuits.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the expiation (sadaqah or shah) for tawaf performed in a state of hadath and for missing one or two circuits of tawaf al-ziyarah, and identify the intra-Hanafi difference regarding tawaf al-sadr.

Core Idea
Voluntary tawafs with hadath require only half a sa' per circuit; missing part of the obligatory ziyarah tawaf requires a shah.

This lesson clarifies the expiations for two common hajj defects: performing tawaf without wudu (hadath) and omitting a small portion of tawaf al-ziyarah. The rulings distinguish between voluntary tawafs (like qudum and sadr) and the obligatory ziyarah tawaf. An important intra-Hanafi difference exists regarding tawaf al-sadr with hadath.

Guided Path
1
Classify the Tawaf
Identify which tawaf was affected: tawaf al-qudum (arrival), tawaf al-sadr (farewell), any voluntary tawaf, or tawaf al-ziyarah (obligatory). The expiation depends on the type.
2
Identify the Defect
Determine the specific defect: was the tawaf performed while in hadath (minor impurity) or junub (major impurity)? Or was one or two circuits of tawaf al-ziyarah missed?
3
Apply the Appropriate Expiation
For hadath in any voluntary tawaf (including qudum and sadr according to the two companions): sadaqah of half a sa' of wheat per circuit. For hadath in tawaf al-sadr according to Abu Hanifa: one shah. For junub in tawaf al-sadr: one shah. For missing one or two circuits of tawaf al-ziyarah: one shah.
The text notes that the sadaqah is due because the tawaf became obligatory by commencement but its rank is lower than one made obligatory by Allah's command.
4
Consider Interaction with Tawaf al-Sadr
If tawaf al-sadr has been performed, it can complete the missing circuits of tawaf al-ziyarah. Then examine the remainder of tawaf al-sadr: if it is less than three circuits, sadaqah is due; otherwise a shah is due.
This nuance prevents double expiation when the two tawafs are combined.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And the sadaqah if he performed tawaf while in hadath: the sadaqah is half a sa' of wheat for each circuit. And his saying: 'for the tawaf of arrival and departure' and likewise for every tawaf that is voluntary, as a compensation for the deficiency that occurred by abandoning purity. And even though it became obligatory by commencing, it is sufficient with sadaqah to show that its rank is lower than that which is obligatory by Allah's command. The sadaqah is due for performing tawaf al-sadr while in hadath instead of a dam, to show the difference between it and tawaf al-ziyarah. According to Abu Hanifah, for tawaf al-sadr while in hadath, a shah is due, because what is made obligatory by Allah's command is stronger than what is made obligatory by commencing. And if he performed tawaf al-sadr while junub, a shah is due because the deficiency is great, but it is less than tawaf al-ziyarah, so a shah is sufficient. If he repeats it while pure, nothing is due. (Miskin, Fath) For the arrival tawaf, it is sunnah but became obligatory by commencing. And the departure tawaf is obligatory but lower in rank than tawaf al-ziyarah. Likewise, every voluntary tawaf becomes obligatory by commencing. Or if he left out a small part, etc. [It is connected to what involves the obligation of a shah, i.e., a shah is due if he left out] meaning if he left out one or two circuits of tawaf al-ziyarah, a shah is due because the deficiency is small, so it is compensated by a dam just like the deficiency due to hadath. And if he returns to his family, it is permissible not to return and to send a shah. This omission is only conceivable if he had not performed tawaf al-sadr; but if he had performed it, then what is transferred to tawaf al-ziyarah completes it. Then one looks at the remainder of the sadr tawaf; if it is less, sadaqah is due, otherwise a dam.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage elaborates on the sadaqah required for performing tawaf while in a state of minor impurity (hadath), especially for the tawafs of arrival (qudum) and departure (sadr). The sadaqah is half a sa' of wheat per circuit. The commentator clarifies that these tawafs are sunnah in origin but become obligatory once commenced. The sadaqah serves as compensation for the deficiency of missing purity. For tawaf al-sadr performed with hadath, Abu Hanifa actually requires a shah (sheep) rather than sadaqah, because the obligation by Allah's command is stronger. For performing tawaf al-sadr while junub, a shah is also due. The passage also covers missing a small part of tawaf al-ziyarah (one or two circuits): a shah is due. If one returns home, it is permissible to send a shah rather than return. The ruling depends on whether tawaf al-sadr has been performed, as it can complete tawaf al-ziyarah if previously performed.

Key Terms
صدقة (sadaqah): A charity of half a sa' of wheat per circuit for tawaf performed while in hadath.
صاع (sa'): A measure of volume; half a sa' of wheat is approximately 1.5-2 kg.
طواف الصدر (tawaf al-sadr): The farewell tawaf performed when leaving Makkah after Hajj.
شاة (shah): A sheep or goat sacrificed as expiation (dam).

Voluntary tawafs performed without wudu require sadaqah per circuit; missing a small part of tawaf al-ziyarah requires a shah; tawaf al-sadr with hadath has an intra-Hanafi difference between sadaqah and shah.

Expiation for Omissions and Violations in Tawaf al-Sadr
Rulings for tawaf al-sadr expiation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the expiation required for missing most or part of tawaf al-sadr, for performing it while junub, and for combined violations between tawaf al-ziyarah and tawaf al-sadr, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Missing most of tawaf al-sadr requires a dam; missing a little requires sadaqah per circuit; combining violations multiplies the dam with ikhtilaf.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explained by the commentator, details the expiation for leaving out parts of tawaf al-sadr (the farewell tawaf) or performing it in a state of impurity. It also covers complex scenarios where tawaf al-ziyarah and tawaf al-sadr are performed with violations, leading to multiple dam and a notable intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions regarding the count.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage addresses tawaf al-sadr, a wajib act of Hajj. Determine that missing most of it or performing it junub incurs a shah (dam), while missing a little incurs sadaqah per circuit.
Terms: shah (sheep) vs sadaqah (charity per half sa' per circuit)
2
Understand the logic for missing most vs. little
The commentary explains that 'the majority has the ruling of the whole' – so missing most of the circuits is like missing the entire tawaf, hence dam. Missing a few circuits is less severe, so only sadaqah.
3
Analyze combined scenarios
When tawaf al-ziyarah is performed junub and tawaf al-sadr is performed in hadath in the last days of tashriq, multiple dam may be due. Follow the passage's reasoning: dam for leaving tawaf al-sadr, dam for delaying tawaf al-ziyarah beyond the days of nahr, and dam for hadath in tawaf al-sadr.
4
Distinguish the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Hanifa holds that three dam are due (one for each violation), while the Sahibayn hold that two dam are due (since delaying tawaf al-sadr beyond days of nahr does not incur an additional dam according to them). Note the practical difference in sacrifice obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو ترك أكثر الصدر أو طافه جنباً، وصدقة بترك أقله، أو طاف للركن محدثاً، أي الصدر أي في حالة الجنابة أقل طواف الصدر وللصدر طاهراً في آخر أيام التشريق، ودمان لو طاف للركن جنُبا ، . أي وطاف للصدر أي يجب طواف الزيارة في أيامه أو ترك أكثر الصدر: [ أي تجب شاة أيضاً إن ترك أكثر طواف الصدر؛ لأنه واجب، وعليه إعادته ما دام بمكة. (ط،ع)] أما وجوب الدم بترك أكثره فلأنه بتركه يجب الدم، فكذا بترك أكثره؛ لأن للأكثر حكم الكل، وأما بالطواف جنباً، فلأنه نقص كبير لكنه يؤمر بالإعادة ما دام بمكة. (فتح) وصدقة بترك أقله أي تجب صدقة بترك أقل أشواط الصدر ، لكل شوط صدقة، فإن كان المتروك شوطاً فنصف صاع، وإن كان شوطين فصاع، وإن كان ثلاثة فصاع ونصف لكل مسكين نصف صاع. (فتح) أو طاف: أي تجب شاة اتفاقاً إن طاف. (ع) للركن محدثا وللصدر طاهرا قيد به إشارة إلى أنه لو طاف في أيام النحر لا يلزمه دم، يعني أن طواف الصدر في أيام النحر ينتقل إلى طواف الزيارة، فسقط الدم الواجب بالحدث لوقوع طواف الزيارة في أيام النحر مع الطهارة، وبقي طواف الصدر، فيأتي به ما دام بمكة بخلاف ما لو كان طواف الصدر في آخر أيام التشريق وقد طاف للركن محدثاً حيث لا ينتقل إليه طواف الصدر لعدم الفائت؛ لأنه إذا سقط دم الحدث وجب دم التأخير بطواف الزيارة، ولأن إعادة طواف الزيارة بسبب الحدث غير واجب، وطواف الصدر واجب، فالواجب لا ينتقل إلى غير الواجب. الصدر محدثاً، وقيد بقوله: "طاهراً"؛ لأنه لو طاف للصدر محدثاً يلزمه دمان عند أبي حنيفة دم لطواف الزيارة محدثاً، ودم لطواف وفي رواية دم ،وصدقة وهو الموافق لكلام المصنف بقوله: "وصدقة لو طاف محدثاً للقدوم والصدر"، أما إذا كان جنباً في طواف الزيارة في أيامه مع طوافه للصدر محدثاً في آخر أيام التشريق فيلزمه ثلاثة دماء عنده: دم لترك طواف الصدر، ودم لتأخيره عن أيام النحر، ودم لكونه طاف محدثاً، وعندهما: دمان؛ لأن التأخير عندهما لا ا يوجب الدم. (فتح) التشريق: فلو طافه في أيام النحر لا يلزمه دم، ولو طافه محدثا يلزمه دمان في رواية وفي رواية: دم وصدقة. (ط) ودمان: وجه وجوب الدمين لو طاف للركن جنباً في أيامه وللصدر طاهراً في آخر أيام التشريق؛ لأن طواف الصدر ههنا ينتقل إلى طواف الزيارة لفائدة سقوط البدنة وتلغو نية الصدر؛ لوجوب ترتيب أفعال الحج، فيكون تاركاً لطواف الصدر ومؤخراً لطواف الزيارة عن أيام النحر، فيجب دم بترك الصدر بلا خلاف، ودم عند أبي حنيفة بتأخير طواف الزيارة عن أيام النحر، فيكون دمان عنده ودم واحد عندهما، فإن كان بمكة يأتي هي بطواف الصدر ولا يلزمه إلا دم واحد. رمز الحقائق: ١٧٥/١] (فتح)
Or if he left out most of the sadr tawaf, or performed it while junub, and sadaqah for leaving out a little, or if he performed tawaf al-rukn while in hadath, i.e., the sadr tawaf while in janabah. The least of sadr tawaf, and for the sadr tawaf while pure in the last days of tashriq, and two dam if he performed tawaf al-rukn while junub. That is, and he performed the sadr tawaf, i.e., tawaf al-ziyarah is obligatory in its days. Or if he left out most of the sadr tawaf: [a shah is also due if he left out most of the sadr tawaf, because it is wajib, and he must repeat it as long as he is in Makkah.] As for the obligation of a dam for leaving out most of it, because missing the whole requires a dam, so likewise for missing most, because the majority has the ruling of the whole. And as for performing it while junub, because it is a great deficiency, but he is commanded to repeat as long as he is in Makkah. And sadaqah for leaving out a little: sadaqah is due for leaving out a few circuits of the sadr tawaf, for each circuit a sadaqah. If the omitted is one circuit, half a sa'; if two circuits, one sa'; if three, one and a half sa's. Or he performed: a shah is due by agreement if he performed tawaf al-rukn while in hadath, and for the sadr tawaf while pure, this restriction indicates that if he performed it during the days of nahr, no dam is due. That is, the sadr tawaf during the days of nahr transfers to tawaf al-ziyarah, so the dam due for hadath is dropped because tawaf al-ziyarah occurred in the days of nahr with purity, and the sadr tawaf remains, so he performs it as long as he is in Makkah, unlike if the sadr tawaf was in the last days of tashriq and he performed tawaf al-rukn while in hadath, where the sadr tawaf does not transfer because there is no loss. Because if the dam for hadath is dropped, the dam for delay of tawaf al-ziyarah becomes due, and because repeating tawaf al-ziyarah due to hadath is not obligatory, while the sadr tawaf is obligatory, so an obligatory act does not transfer to a non-obligatory one. The sadr tawaf while in hadath, and he restricted it by saying 'while pure'. Because if he performed the sadr tawaf while in hadath, two dam are due according to Abu Hanifah: a dam for tawaf al-ziyarah while in hadath, and a dam for... and in one narration: a dam and sadaqah, which agrees with the author's statement: 'and sadaqah if he performed tawaf while in hadath for the arrival and departure tawaf.' As for if he was junub in tawaf al-ziyarah during its days while performing the sadr tawaf while in hadath in the last days of tashriq, three dam are due according to him: a dam for leaving the sadr tawaf, a dam for delaying it beyond the days of nahr, and a dam for performing it while in hadath. According to them (the two companions), two dam: because delay does not obligate a dam according to them. So if he performed it in the days of nahr, no dam is due; if he performed it while in hadath, two dam in one narration, and in another: a dam and sadaqah. And two dam: the reason for the obligation of two dam if he performed tawaf al-rukn while junub in its days and the sadr tawaf while pure in the last days of tashriq. Because the sadr tawaf here transfers to tawaf al-ziyarah for the benefit of dropping the badanah, and the intention of sadr is nullified due to the obligation of sequence of Hajj actions. So he becomes one who left the sadr tawaf and delayed tawaf al-ziyarah beyond the days of nahr. Thus a dam is due for leaving the sadr tawaf without dispute, and a dam according to Abu Hanifah for delaying tawaf al-ziyarah beyond the days of nahr, so two dam according to him and one dam according to them. If he is in Makkah, he performs the sadr tawaf and only one dam is due.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage deals with the rulings for tawaf al-sadr (departure tawaf) and combined violations. The matn states that missing most of tawaf al-sadr or performing it while junub requires a shah, while missing a little requires sadaqah per circuit. The commentary explains the logic: the majority has the ruling of the whole. For performing tawaf al-rukn (tawaf al-ziyarah) with hadath while performing sadr tawaf in purity in the last days of tashriq, two dam are due according to Abu Hanifa (one for missing sadr and one for delay of ziyarah), but only one according to the two companions. There is also a scenario with three dam: if one is junub in tawaf al-ziyarah and hadath in sadr tawaf in the last days of tashriq, Abu Hanifa says three dam, the two companions say two. The passage also discusses the transfer of sadr tawaf to ziyarah if performed in the days of nahr, which can drop some penalties.

Key Terms
طواف الصدر (tawaf al-sadr): The farewell tawaf performed when leaving Makkah after completing Hajj rites.
دم (dam): A blood sacrifice (sheep) required as expiation for certain violations in Hajj.
أيام التشريق (ayyam al-tashriq): The 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul-Hijjah, days of staying in Mina and performing rites.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Sadaqah per circuit
B) A shah (sheep)
C) A badanah (camel)
D) No expiation

Key Takeaway
Missing most of tawaf al-sadr or performing it junub requires a dam; missing a little requires sadaqah; combined violations lead to multiple dam with an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Compensation for Deficiencies in Farewell Tawaf
Compensation rules for farewell tawaf deficiencies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the compensation required for leaving most or part of the farewell tawaf and for performing it in a state of impurity.

Core Idea
Leaving most of farewell tawaf requires a sheep; leaving less requires charity per circuit.

The farewell tawaf (tawaf al-sadr) is a wajib act in Hajj. If a pilgrim omits it or performs it improperly, compensation is due. This passage explains the rulings for various deficiencies: leaving most of the tawaf, leaving a few circuits, and performing it while junub or in minor impurity. Understanding these compensations ensures one can fulfill the Hajj obligations correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the deficiency
Determine what aspect of farewell tawaf is deficient: leaving most circuits, leaving a few circuits, or performing it while impure.
The text distinguishes between 'most' (akthar) and 'less' (aqall) in terms of circuits left.
2
Apply the compensation rule
Based on the deficiency, apply the required compensation: a sheep (shah) for leaving most or for impurity, or charity (sadaqah) per circuit for leaving less.
The amount of charity: 1/2 sa' per circuit, up to 1.5 sa' for three circuits.
3
Check for repetition
If the deficiency is due to impurity or leaving most, the pilgrim must repeat the tawaf as long as he is still in Makkah.
Repetition is not required for leaving a few circuits; only charity is due.
4
Note the unanimous ruling for impurity in visit tawaf
If one performs the visit tawaf (rukn) while in minor impurity, a sheep is due unanimously, and the farewell tawaf if pure transfers to it.
This is a distinct ruling mentioned in the text.

Source Text

أو ترك أكثر الصدر أو طافه جنباً، وصدقة بترك أقله، أو طاف للركن محدثاً، أي الصدر أي في حالة الجنابة أقل طواف الصدر وللصدر طاهراً في آخر أيام التشريق، ودمان لو طاف للركن جنُبا .
أي وطاف للصدر أي يجب طواف الزيارة في أيامه
أو ترك أكثر الصدر: [ أي تجب شاة أيضاً إن ترك أكثر طواف الصدر؛ لأنه واجب، وعليه إعادته ما دام بمكة. (ط،ع)] أما وجوب الدم بترك أكثره فلأنه بتركه يجب الدم، فكذا بترك أكثره؛ لأن للأكثر حكم الكل، وأما بالطواف جنباً، فلأنه نقص كبير لكنه يؤمر بالإعادة ما دام بمكة. (فتح) وصدقة بترك أقله أي تجب صدقة بترك أقل أشواط الصدر ، لكل شوط صدقة، فإن كان المتروك شوطاً فنصف صاع، وإن كان شوطين فصاع، وإن كان ثلاثة فصاع ونصف لكل مسكين نصف صاع. (فتح) أو طاف: أي تجب شاة اتفاقاً إن طاف. (ع) للركن محدثا وللصدر طاهرا قيد به إشارة إلى أنه لو طاف في أيام النحر لا يلزمه دم، يعني أن طواف الصدر في أيام النحر ينتقل إلى طواف الزيارة، فسقط الدم الواجب بالحدث لوقوع طواف الزيارة في أيام النحر مع الطهارة، وبقي طواف الصدر، فيأتي به ما دام بمكة بخلاف ما لو كان طواف الصدر في آخر أيام التشريق وقد طاف للركن محدثاً حيث لا ينتقل إليه طواف الصدر لعدم الفائت؛ لأنه إذا سقط دم الحدث وجب دم التأخير بطواف الزيارة، ولأن إعادة طواف الزيارة بسبب الحدث غير واجب، وطواف الصدر واجب، فالواجب لا ينتقل إلى غير الواجب.
الصدر محدثاً، وقيد بقوله: "طاهراً"؛ لأنه لو طاف للصدر محدثاً يلزمه دمان عند أبي حنيفة دم لطواف الزيارة محدثاً، ودم لطواف وفي رواية دم ،وصدقة وهو الموافق لكلام المصنف بقوله: "وصدقة لو طاف محدثاً للقدوم والصدر"، أما إذا كان جنباً في طواف الزيارة في أيامه مع طوافه للصدر محدثاً في آخر أيام التشريق فيلزمه ثلاثة دماء عنده: دم لترك طواف الصدر، ودم لتأخيره عن أيام النحر، ودم لكونه طاف ،محدثاً، وعندهما: دمان؛ لأن التأخير عندهما لا ا يوجب الدم. (فتح) التشريق: فلو طافه في أيام النحر لا يلزمه ،دم، ولو طافه محدثا يلزمه دمان في رواية وفي رواية: دم وصدقة. (ط) ودمان: وجه وجوب الدمين لو طاف للركن جنباً في أيامه وللصدر طاهراً في آخر أيام التشريق؛ لأن طواف الصدر ههنا ينتقل إلى طواف الزيارة لفائدة سقوط البدنة وتلغو نية الصدر؛ لوجوب ترتيب أفعال الحج، فيكون تاركاً لطواف الصدر ومؤخراً لطواف الزيارة عن أيام النحر، فيجب دم بترك الصدر بلا خلاف، ودم عند أبي حنيفة بتأخير طواف الزيارة عن أيام النحر، فيكون دمان عنده ودم واحد عندهما، فإن كان بمكة يأتي بطواف الصدر ولا يلزمه إلا دم واحد.
Or he leaves most of the farewell tawaf or performs it while junub, and charity for leaving less than that, or performs the visit tawaf while in a state of minor impurity, meaning the farewell tawaf when in major impurity, the minimum of farewell tawaf, and for the farewell tawaf while pure at the end of the days of Tashriq, and two blood offerings if he performed the visit tawaf while junub. And he performed the farewell tawaf, meaning the visit tawaf must be performed in its days. Or leaves most of the farewell tawaf: a sheep is obligatory if he leaves most of the farewell tawaf because it is wajib, and he must repeat it as long as he is in Makkah. As for the obligation of blood for leaving most of it, because by leaving it blood is obligatory, so similarly by leaving most of it, because the majority has the ruling of the whole. And for performing tawaf while junub, because it is a major deficiency, but he is instructed to repeat it as long as he is in Makkah. And charity for leaving less than that: charity is obligatory for leaving fewer circuits of farewell tawaf, for each circuit charity: if the left is one circuit, then half a sa'; if two circuits, then one sa'; if three, then one and a half sa', for each poor person half a sa'. Or he performs tawaf: a sheep is obligatory unanimously if he performs tawaf for the visit while in minor impurity and for the farewell while pure, restricted to indicate that if he performed tawaf during the days of sacrifice, no blood is required, meaning that the farewell tawaf during the days of sacrifice transfers to the visit tawaf, so the blood obligatory due to minor impurity drops because the visit tawaf occurred in the days of sacrifice with purity, and the farewell tawaf remains, so he performs it as long as he is in Makkah, contrary to if the farewell tawaf is at the end of the days of Tashriq and he performed the visit tawaf while impure, where the farewell tawaf does not transfer to it because there is no lost element; because when the blood for minor impurity drops, the blood for delay of the visit tawaf becomes obligatory, and because repeating the visit tawaf due to impurity is not wajib, and the farewell tawaf is wajib, so the wajib does not transfer to the non-wajib. He said: the farewell tawaf while impure, and he restricted by saying 'while pure'; because if he performs the farewell tawaf while impure, two bloods are required according to Abu Hanifa: one blood for the visit tawaf while impure, and one blood for the farewell tawaf? and in one narration: one blood and charity, and this is in agreement with the author's statement: 'and charity if he performs tawaf for arrival and farewell while impure'. But if he is junub in the visit tawaf during its days along with his farewell tawaf while impure at the end of the days of Tashriq, then three bloods are required according to him: one blood for leaving farewell tawaf, one for delaying it from the days of sacrifice, and one for performing tawaf while impure. According to them (the two companions): two bloods; because delay according to them does not necessitate blood. And two bloods: the justification for the obligation of two bloods if he performed the visit tawaf while junub during its days and the farewell tawaf while pure at the end of the days of Tashriq, because the farewell tawaf here transfers to the visit tawaf for the benefit of dropping the camel, and the intention of farewell is invalid due to the obligation of order of Hajj actions, so he becomes one who left the farewell tawaf and delayed the visit tawaf from the days of sacrifice. So one blood is obligatory for leaving farewell tawaf without dispute, and one blood according to Abu Hanifa for delaying the visit tawaf from the days of sacrifice, so according to him there are two bloods, and according to them one blood. If he is in Makkah, he performs the farewell tawaf and only one blood is required of him.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn (base text) regarding the rulings of compensation (dam and sadaqah) for deficiencies in the farewell tawaf (tawaf al-sadr) and the visit tawaf (tawaf al-ziyarah). The author first addresses the case of leaving most of the farewell tawaf. He states that leaving most of it requires a sheep (shah), and the person must repeat the tawaf as long as he is in Makkah. The reasoning is that the majority has the ruling of the whole, and because leaving the entire farewell tawaf would require blood, leaving most of it similarly requires blood. Then he discusses performing tawaf while in a state of major impurity (junub): it is a major deficiency, but he is instructed to repeat it. For leaving less than half (less than most), charity (sadaqah) is given per circuit: half a sa' for one circuit, one sa' for two, one and a half for three. Then the passage moves to a scenario where one performs the visit tawaf while in minor impurity (hadath) and the farewell tawaf while pure at the end of the days of Tashriq. The commentary explains that if the farewell tawaf is performed during the days of sacrifice (i.e., the days of tashriq), it transfers to the visit tawaf, so no blood is required for impurity. But if it is at the end of the days of tashriq, a different ruling applies. A key intra-Hanafi dispute is presented: according to Abu Hanifa, if one performs the farewell tawaf while impure, two bloods are required (one for the visit tawaf performed while impure and one for the farewell?), whereas according to a narration it is one blood and charity. The commentary also presents a scenario where one is junub during the visit tawaf and impure during the farewell tawaf: Abu Hanifa says three bloods, while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say two bloods because they do not consider delay of the visit tawaf to require a separate blood. The passage concludes that if the person is in Makkah, he should perform the farewell tawaf and only one blood is required.

Key Terms
طواف الصدر (tawaf al-sadr): The farewell tawaf performed after completing Hajj rituals before leaving Makkah. It is wajib according to the Hanafi school.
طواف الزيارة (tawaf al-ziyarah): The visit tawaf performed on the day of sacrifice (10th of Dhul Hijjah) or during the days of Tashriq. It is a rukn of Hajj.
دم (dam): A blood offering (sacrifice of a sheep) required as compensation for missing a wajib or committing a forbidden act during Hajj/Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) A sheep
B) Charity of one sa'
C) No compensation
D) A camel

Key Takeaway
Compensation for deficiencies in farewell tawaf varies by severity: leaving most requires a sheep, leaving a few circuits requires charity per circuit, and impurity requires both a sheep and repetition.
