The penalty for killing game and wounding it. Section: If a muhrim kills game or guides the killer to it, then he must pay the penalty, the muhrim is prohibited from game whether he is muhrim or not. Section: In explanation of the penalty for killing game. [Reference: Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1/177] Because the offense against ihram in game is a different type from the previous types of offenses, he presented it in a separate section due to the difference in type, and combined it with what preceded in one chapter due to the unity in genus. (Fath) A muhrim who is sane, adult, whether free or slave, intentional or mistaken. (T) Game: game is the animal that resists with its legs or wings, wild by original creation. So sheep and cattle are domestic animals, and chickens, ducks, and domesticated deer are not game. It is two types: land game, which is born and dwells on land, and sea game, which is born and dwells in water; because birth is the origin, and being afterward is incidental, so the origin is considered. Sea game is permissible for the non-muhrim and the muhrim, so he may hunt all of it. For indeed, sea game was made permissible for the muhrim by His statement: 'Permitted to you is the game of the sea' (5:96). And land game is forbidden for the muhrim except what the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, ordered to be killed, which is what generally begins with harm. (Fath, Miskin) So he must pay the penalty due to His statement: 'And whoever kills it among you intentionally, then a penalty equivalent to what he killed from the cattle' (5:95). That is, if a muhrim kills game or the killer guides to it, he must pay the penalty, whether the killing was after knowledge of the prohibition or before, whether the game was from the Haram or outside it, whether intentionally or forgetful, directly or indirectly if he was transgressive therein, such as setting a net for game or digging a pit for it and the game perishes, he is liable. And if he sets up a tent himself and it catches on it and dies, or digs a pit for water or for an animal whose killing is permissible like a wolf and it perishes therein, there is nothing upon him. But if he kills game in the Haram, it should be that he has two penalties: one for ihram and the other for the Haram, except that only one penalty is required upon him because the sanctity of ihram is stronger; for the muhrim is not permitted to hunt in the outside or the Haram, so the stronger subsumed the weaker. As for the obligation of penalty for killing, it is due to His statement: 'And do not kill game while you are in ihram, and whoever kills it among you...' (5:95). As for guiding, it is based on what was narrated in the hadith of Abu Qatada: 'Did you guide? Did you indicate? Did you help?' They said, 'No.' He said, 'Then eat.' The way of adhering to it is that if guiding had no effect on prohibition, there would be no benefit in the question. And qiyas is that the penalty should not be obligatory on the guide, and this is what al-Shafi'i adopted, because the penalty is attached to killing, and guiding is not killing, so it resembles a non-muhrim guiding a non-muhrim. But the evidence against it is the hadith of Abu Qatada. Then know that there are five conditions for the obligation of penalty on the muhrim guide: First: The guided person takes the game while the guide is muhrim; if the guide exits ihram before the taking, then no penalty upon him. Second: The guided person should not be aware of the location of the game; if he knew, the penalty is not obligatory on the guide. Third: The guided person confirms the guide in the guidance, i.e., he does not deny him; even if he denies him and takes the game by the guidance of another muhrim, the penalty is on the second, not the first. Fourth: The killing is connected to the guidance. Fifth: The game does not escape; if it escapes from its place and is taken from another place, nothing is on the guide. (Miskin, Fath)
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage is a section on the penalty for a muhrim who kills game or guides someone to kill it. It begins by stating the general ruling: both the killer and the guide are liable. The commentary then defines 'sayd' as wild animals that are untamed by nature, excluding domestic animals and those that have become tame. It classifies game into land and sea, noting that sea game is permissible even for the muhrim, based on Quran 5:96. The penalty for killing land game is derived from Quran 5:95. The text also clarifies that if a muhrim kills game in the Haram, only one penalty is due because the sanctity of ihram is stronger. The guide's liability is established through the hadith of Abu Qatada, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) asked about guiding and helping, implying that guiding has legal effect. The Shafi'i objection based on qiyas (that guiding is not killing) is rebutted by the hadith. Then five specific conditions are given for the guide's liability: (1) the guide must still be in ihram when the game is taken; (2) the guided person was unaware of the game's location; (3) the guided person confirms the guide's direction; (4) the killing is directly connected to the guidance; (5) the game does not escape before capture. These conditions show that the Hanafi school carefully delimits the guide's liability.

Key Terms
صيد (sayd): Wild animals that are inherently untamed; excludes domestic animals and tame ones.
دال (dall): A person who guides or points out the location of game to the hunter.
جزاء (jaza'): The penalty or compensation for killing game while in ihram.
محرم (muhrim): A person in the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT a condition for the guide's liability?
A) The guide is still in Ihram when the game is taken
B) The guided person was unaware of the game's location
C) The guided person confirms the guide's direction
D) The guide personally kills the game

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school makes a muhrim guide liable for the penalty only when five precise conditions are met, and this ruling is based on the hadith of Abu Qatada overriding the Shafi'i qiyas.

Nature of the Penalty for Killing Game: Mithl vs. Qimah
Discusses whether penalty is similar animal or market value, with dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the Hanafi position (value) and the opposing position (similar animal) regarding the penalty for killing game in ihram, and apply the Hanafi ruling to determine the penalty for any game.

Core Idea
The Hanafi penalty for killing game is its market value, not a similar domestic animal.

This lesson explores a key dispute in the fiqh of Hajj: what does Allah mean by 'a penalty equivalent to what he killed from the cattle' (Quran 5:95)? Does 'equivalent' mean a physically similar domestic animal, as Muhammad al-Shaybani and al-Shafi'i argue, or does it mean the market value, as Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold? Understanding this dispute will sharpen your ability to interpret legal texts and appreciate how different usul principles lead to different rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the two positions
State the disagreement: Is the penalty a similar animal (mithl suwari) or market value (qimah)? Note which scholars take each side.
2
Examine the proof of Muhammad and al-Shafi'i
Look at the literal meaning of Quran 5:95 and the practice of the Companions (camel for ostrich, cow for wild donkey, etc.). Understand why they insist on a physical counterpart.
3
Examine the proof of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
Note their reinterpretation of 'mithl': they argue that a physical match is impossible even within the same species (no two cows are exactly alike), so the true equivalent is value. Consider their use of Quran 2:194 and analogy with property damage.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Companions' examples
The Hanafis say those were mere estimations (taqdir), not obligations of the exact animal. Also, the verse is general for all game, and only value can cover all game universally.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
For a specific case (e.g., killing a deer), the Hanafi ruling is to pay its market value, while the other school requires a sheep. This shows the real-world impact.

في ك وهو قيمة الصيد بتقويم عدلين في مقتله أو أقرب موضع منه، فيشتري بها هدياً، أي الجزاء أي في أقرب أي القاتل وذبحه إن بلغت هدياً، أو طعاماً وتصدق به كالفطرة أو صام عن طعام كل ومعنى إن شاء بالحرم قیمته إن شاء يشتري بها أي بالطعام إن شاء بالقيمة أي عن نصف كل صاع اتحاد قيمة الصيد: الأصل في اعتبار قيمة الصيد اعتبار الزمان والمكان، وهو الأصح والمراد تقويمه باعتبار حالته الخلقية، وأما حالته الكسبية بالتعليم فغير معتبرة في التقويم للكفارة، بخلاف التقويم للضمان للمالك، وتعتبر القيمة من حيث كونه صيداً لا من حيث ما زاد بالصنعة فيه، وقال محمد والشافعي الجزاء ما يشبه الصيد في المنظر إن كان له نظير من النعم؛ لقوله تعالى: فَجَزَاء مِثْلُ مَا قَتَلَ مِنَ النَّعَم الله (المائدة : ٩٥) تقديره: فعليه جزاء من النعم مثل المقتول، فمن قال : إنه مثله من الدراهم فقد خالف النص، ولهذا أو جبت الصحابة النظير - أي المثل في الصورة - حتى يجب في النعامة ،بدنة، وفي الحمار الوحشي بقرة، وفي الظبي شاة، وفي الأرنب عناق، وفي ما لا نظير له كالعصفور يكون مضموناً بالقيمة، ولأبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف أن الواجب هو المثل، والمثل المطلق هو المثل صورة فعند تعذره يعتبر المثل معنى والمثل صورة بلا معنى لا يعتبر شرعاً. ولهذا لو أتلف مال إنسان وجب مثله إن كان مثلياً وإلا فقيمته حتى لو أتلف دابة لا يجب عليه دابة مثلها مع ا الجنس؛ لاختلاف المعاني، فما ظنك مع اختلاف الجنس، فإذا لم تكن البقرة مثلاً للبقرة فكيف تكون مثلاً للحمار الوحشي، وإذا تعذر الجنس صورة ومعنى وجب حمله على المثل معنى وهو القيمة؛ إما لكونه معهوداً في الشرع، أو لكونه مراداً بالإجماع فيما لا نظير له، فلا يكون النظير مراداً؛ لأن اللفظ الواحد لا يتناول موضعين مختلفين، ولأن قوله تعالى: ﴿ولا تَقْتُلُوا الصَّيْدَ وَأَنْتُمْ حُرُم (المائدة: ٩٥) عام لجميع الصيد، والضمير في قوله: ﴿وَمَنْ قَتَلَهُ مِنْكُمْ عائد إليه، فوجب أن يكون "المثل" في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَنْ قَتَلَهُ مِنْكُمْ مُتَعَمِّداً فَجَزَاءً مِثْلُ مَا قَتَلَ مِنَ النَّعَمِ ﴾ (المائدة: ٩٥) مثلا للكل، وليس لنا مثل يعم الكل إلا القيمة، والمراد بالنعم الصيد؛ لأن اسم النعم يطلق على الوحشي، والمراد بما روي عن الصحابة: التقدير دون إيجاب العين، ولأن في قوله تعالى: ﴿فَاعْتَدُوا عَلَيْهِ بِمِثْلِ مَا اعْتَدَى عَلَيْكُمْ﴾ (البقرة:١٩٤) هذا "المثل" في الآية: القيمة في الضمان بالإجماع، فكذا في هذا. (فتح) بتقويم: متعلق بمحذوف أي قيمة مقومة بتقويم رجلين عدلين والمراد بالعدل من له معرفة وبصارة بقيمة الصيد، لا العدل في باب الشهادة. (فتح) مقتله بفتح الميم أي في موضع قتل فيه الصيد. (ع ) موضع منه: أي المقتل إن كان في برية لا يباع فيها الصيد. (ع) هدياً من إبل وبقر وغنم وهو رواية الكرخي، واختارها المراد من من صاحب الهداية لما ورد من أمره عليها بقتل الذئب والفأرة والحدأة والغراب، رواه ابن أبي شيبة. (فتح) كالفطرة : فيعطي كل مسكين ولو ذميا نصف صاع من بر أو صاعا من تمر أو شعير، ولا يجوز أقل من ذلك. (ط) أو صام إلخ: [إن شاء قوم المقتول طعاما ثم صام. (ط)] الخيار لقاتل الصيد في أن يجعل قيمته هدياً يجزئ في الأضحية من إبل وبقر وغنم ويذبحه في الحرم، والمراد من الكعبة في الآية: الحرم، عبر عنه بأشرفه، أو يجعلها طعاماً ويتصدق به كما في صدقة الفطرة، أو يقومه طعاماً ثم يصوم مكان طعام كل مسكين يوما، وعن محمد والشافعي: =
In K, and it is the value of the game by the valuation of two just men at its place of killing or the nearest location to it, so that he may buy a sacrificial animal with it, meaning the penalty, meaning at the nearest, meaning the killer, and slaughter it if it reaches the value of a sacrificial animal, or food and give it in charity like zakat al-fitr, or fast instead of food for each, meaning if he wishes, at the Haram its value, if he wishes, he buys with it, meaning with the food if he wishes, with the value, meaning for every half sa'. Unity of the value of game: The principle in considering the value of the game is consideration of time and place, and this is the most correct. And what is meant is its valuation considering its natural state; as for its acquired state through training, it is not considered in the valuation for expiation, unlike valuation for compensation to the owner. And the value is considered from the aspect of it being game, not from what increased by craftsmanship. And Muhammad and al-Shafi'i said: The penalty is what resembles the game in appearance if it has a counterpart from the cattle; due to His statement: 'Then a penalty equivalent to what he killed from the cattle' (5:95). Its interpretation: He owes a penalty from the cattle like the killed one. So whoever says it is like it in dirhams has contradicted the text. For this reason, the Companions obligated the counterpart - i.e., the likeness in form - so that a camel is required for an ostrich, a cow for a wild donkey, a sheep for a deer, a young goat for a hare, and for what has no counterpart like a sparrow, it is guaranteed by value. And Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that what is obligatory is the equivalent (mithl), and the absolute equivalent is the equivalent in form. So when that is impossible, the equivalent in meaning is considered, and an equivalent in form without meaning is not considered legally. For this reason, if someone destroys another's property, its equivalent is obligatory if it is of a standard type, otherwise its value. So if he destroys an animal, he is not obligated to give a similar animal even within the same species, because of difference in qualities. So what do you think of different species? So if a cow is not a match for a cow, how can it be a match for a wild donkey? And when the species is impossible both in form and meaning, it must be carried to the equivalent in meaning, which is value; either because it is customary in the law, or because it is intended by consensus for what has no counterpart. So the counterpart is not intended, because a single word does not cover two different contexts. And because His statement: 'And do not kill game while you are in ihram' (5:95) is general for all game, and the pronoun in 'And whoever kills it among you' refers back to it, so it is necessary that 'the equivalent' in His statement 'And whoever kills it among you intentionally, then a penalty equivalent to what he killed from the cattle' (5:95) be an equivalent for all. And we have no equivalent that covers all except value. And what is meant by 'cattle' is game, because the name 'cattle' is applied to wild animals. And what is meant by what was narrated from the Companions is estimation, not obligation of the exact object. And because in His statement: 'So transgress against him with the like of what he transgressed against you' (2:194), this 'like' in the verse is value in compensation by consensus, so likewise here. (Fath) 'By the valuation' is attached to an omitted word meaning a value measured by the valuation of two just men. And what is meant by just is one who has knowledge and insight into the value of game, not the just in the chapter of testimony. (Fath) 'At its place of killing' with fatha on the mim means the place where the game was killed. ('A) 'Or the nearest location to it' means the place of killing if it is in a wilderness where game is not sold. ('A) 'A sacrificial animal from camels, cows, and sheep' and this is the narration of al-Karkhi, and the author of al-Hidayah chose it because of what was reported regarding the command to kill the wolf, mouse, kite, and crow, narrated by Ibn Abi Shayba. (Fath) 'Like zakat al-fitr' means he gives each poor person even if a dhimmi half a sa' of wheat or a sa' of dates or barley, and less than that is not permissible. (T) 'Or fast' etc.: [If he wishes, he values the killed game as food and then fasts. (T)] The killer of the game has the option to make its value a sacrificial animal that is valid for the udhiyah from camels, cows, and sheep and slaughter it in the Haram - and what is meant by the Ka'ba in the verse is the Haram, expressed by its most honorable part - or to make it food and give it in charity like sadaqat al-fitr, or to value it as food and then fast instead of the food of each poor person for a day. And from Muhammad and al-Shafi'i: =
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage explains how the penalty (jaza') for killing game is assessed. It begins with the literal meaning of the matn: the value of the game is determined by two just valuers at the location of the killing, and with that value the muhrim can buy a sacrificial animal, donate food, or fast. It then delves into a major dispute: whether the penalty must be a domestic animal that resembles the game in appearance (like-for-like) or its market value. Muhammad al-Shaybani and al-Shafi'i argue that Allah's words 'a penalty equivalent to what he killed from the cattle' require a physical counterpart from domestic animals, citing the practice of the Companions who specified a camel for an ostrich, a cow for a wild donkey, etc. They hold that only when no counterpart exists should value be used. In contrast, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf argue that the term 'equivalent' (mithl) is not limited to physical similarity; they use the example of property damage where two items of the same species are not truly equivalent due to differences in qualities. They contend that when a perfect physical match is impossible, the intended equivalent is in meaning, i.e., value. They support this by noting that the verse about game is general, so the 'equivalent' must be something that applies to all types of game, and only value is universal. They also point to Quran 2:194 where 'mithl' is unanimously interpreted as value in the context of compensation. The passage also details the methodology for valuation: consider the game's natural state, not trained abilities, and the valuation is for the expiation, not for compensating an owner. Finally, it explains the options for the muhrim: buy a sacrificial animal, feed the poor, or fast one day per poor person's meal.

Key Terms
مثل (mithl): Equivalent; in the verse, Hanafis interpret it as market value when a physical match is not possible or meaningful.
قيمة (qimah): Market value of the game as determined by two just valuers.
نعم (na'am): Cattle or domestic animals (camel, cow, sheep, goat).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the penalty for a muhrim who intentionally kills a deer (which has a domestic counterpart)?
A) A sheep
B) The market value of the deer
C) A deer from the wild
D) Fasting for one year

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi view is that the penalty for killing game in ihram is its market value, regardless of the existence of a physically similar domestic animal.

Penalty for Killing Game in Ihram: Value-Based Ruling and Disputes
Explains the penalty for hunting in ihram and intra-madhhab disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the penalty for killing game in ihram, explain the dispute between Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad/Shafi'i regarding mithl vs qimah, and apply the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The penalty for hunting in ihram is the value of the game, not a specific animal, and the hunter may choose hadi, charity, or fasting.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents the Hanafi ruling on the penalty (jaza') for a pilgrim in ihram who kills game. The text first states the base ruling: two just men assess the value, which is then used for a sacrificial animal, food charity, or fasting. It then delves into a central intra-madhhab and inter-madhhab dispute: is the penalty a physical equivalent from livestock or its monetary value? Understanding this dispute reveals how Hanafi usul principles, like the interpretation of 'mithl' and analogy from property torts, shape fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? Killing game (sayd) while in ihram. What is the hukm? The penalty (jaza') is wajib as an expiation for violating the sanctity of ihram.
The verse (Quran 5:95) specifies intentional killing, but the Hanafi school applies the ruling to both intentional and unintentional? Consult your fiqh manual for details.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is Quran 5:95: 'So a penalty: the like of what he killed from livestock.' Additionally, the practice of the Companions assigning specific animals for specific game is cited by the opposing view.
The exact wording of the verse is critical: 'fajaza'un mithlu ma qatala min al-na'am'.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the dalil prove the ruling? The obligation is clear from the imperative. The dispute centers on the meaning of 'mithl' (like). Does it require a physical likeness (a specific livestock animal) or a likeness in value?
Hanafi: The absolute meaning of 'like' is form, but when impossible, meaning (value) is taken. Shafi'i: It is exclusively physical form.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Muhammad al-Shaybani and al-Shafi'i hold that the penalty must be a physical equivalent from livestock resembling the game (e.g., camel for ostrich). Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that when physical likeness is impossible, the likeness in meaning (value) is obligatory.
This is both an intra-madhhab (Muhammad vs Abu Hanifa) and cross-madhhab (Hanafi vs Shafi'i) dispute.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The mufta bihi position is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: the penalty is the value assessed by two just men, and the hunter has the choice among hadi, food charity, or fasting. The hadi must be valid for udhiyah (sacrifice).
The choice (takhyir) is for the hunter, not the judges, based on the 'or' in the verse and the principle of ease.

جزاء قتل الصيد وجرحه
في ك وهو قيمة الصيد بتقويم عدلين في مقتله أو أقرب موضع منه، فيشتري بها هدياً، أي الجزاء، أي في أقرب، أي القاتل، وذبحه إن بلغت هدياً، أو طعاماً وتصدق به كالفطرة أو صام عن طعام كل مسكين يوما، ومعنى إن شاء بالحرم قیمته، إن شاء يشتري بها، أي بالطعام إن شاء، بالقيمة، أي عن نصف كل صاع
اتحاد
قيمة الصيد: الأصل في اعتبار قيمة الصيد اعتبار الزمان والمكان، وهو الأصح والمراد تقويمه باعتبار حالته الخلقية، وأما حالته الكسبية بالتعليم فغير معتبرة في التقويم للكفارة، بخلاف التقويم للضمان للمالك، وتعتبر القيمة من حيث كونه صيداً لا من حيث ما زاد بالصنعة فيه، وقال محمد والشافعي الجزاء ما يشبه الصيد في المنظر إن كان له نظير من النعم؛ لقوله تعالى: فَجَزَاء مِثْلُ مَا قَتَلَ مِنَ النَّعَم الله (المائدة : ٩٥) تقديره: فعليه جزاء من النعم مثل المقتول، فمن قال : إنه مثله من الدراهم فقد خالف النص، ولهذا أو جبت الصحابة النظير - أي المثل في الصورة - حتى يجب في النعامة ،بدنة، وفي الحمار الوحشي بقرة، وفي الظبي شاة، وفي الأرنب عناق، وفي ما لا نظير له كالعصفور يكون مضموناً بالقيمة، ولأبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف أن الواجب هو المثل، والمثل المطلق هو المثل صورة فعند تعذره يعتبر المثل معنى والمثل صورة بلا معنى لا يعتبر شرعاً. ولهذا لو أتلف مال إنسان وجب مثله إن كان مثلياً وإلا فقيمته حتى لو أتلف دابة لا يجب عليه دابة مثلها مع ا الجنس؛ لاختلاف المعاني، فما ظنك مع اختلاف الجنس، فإذا لم تكن البقرة مثلاً للبقرة فكيف تكون مثلاً للحمار الوحشي، وإذا تعذر الجنس صورة ومعنى وجب حمله على المثل معنى وهو القيمة؛ إما لكونه معهوداً في الشرع، أو لكونه مراداً بالإجماع فيما لا نظير له، فلا يكون النظير مراداً؛ لأن اللفظ الواحد لا يتناول موضعين مختلفين، ولأن قوله تعالى: ﴿ولا تَقْتُلُوا الصَّيْدَ وَأَنْتُمْ حُرُم (المائدة: ٩٥) عام لجميع الصيد، والضمير في قوله: ﴿وَمَنْ قَتَلَهُ مِنْكُمْ﴾ عائد إليه، فوجب أن يكون "المثل" في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَنْ قَتَلَهُ مِنْكُمْ مُتَعَمِّداً فَجَزَاءً مِثْلُ مَا قَتَلَ مِنَ النَّعَمِ ﴾ (المائدة: ٩٥) مثلا للكل، وليس لنا مثل يعم الكل إلا القيمة، والمراد بالنعم الصيد؛ لأن اسم النعم يطلق على الوحشي، والمراد بما روي عن الصحابة: التقدير دون إيجاب العين، ولأن في قوله تعالى: ﴿فَاعْتَدُوا عَلَيْهِ بِمِثْلِ مَا اعْتَدَى عَلَيْكُمْ﴾ (البقرة:١٩٤) هذا "المثل" في الآية: القيمة في الضمان بالإجماع، فكذا في هذا. (فتح) بتقويم: متعلق بمحذوف أي قيمة مقومة بتقويم رجلين عدلين والمراد بالعدل من له معرفة وبصارة بقيمة الصيد، لا العدل في باب الشهادة. (فتح) مقتله بفتح الميم أي في موضع قتل فيه الصيد. (ع) موضع منه: أي المقتل إن كان في برية لا يباع فيها الصيد. (ع) هدياً من إبل وبقر وغنم وهو رواية الكرخي، واختارها صاحب الهداية لما ورد من أمره عليها بقتل الذئب والفأرة والحدأة والغراب، رواه ابن أبي شيبة. (فتح) كالفطرة : فيعطي كل مسكين ولو ذميا نصف صاع من بر أو صاعا من تمر أو شعير، ولا يجوز أقل من ذلك. (ط) أو صام إلخ: [إن شاء قوم المقتول طعاما ثم صام. (ط)] الخيار لقاتل الصيد في أن يجعل قيمته هدياً يجزئ في الأضحية من إبل وبقر وغنم ويذبحه في الحرم، والمراد من الكعبة في الآية: الحرم، عبر عنه بأشرفه، أو يجعلها طعاماً ويتصدق به كما في صدقة الفطرة، أو يقومه طعاماً ثم يصوم مكان طعام كل مسكين يوما، وعن محمد والشافعي: =
مسكين يوما، ولو فضل أقل من نصف صاع تصدّق به أو صام يوما، وإن جرحه أو قطع عضوه أو نتف شعره ضمن ما نقص منه، الخيار إلى الحكمين لقوله تعالى: ﴿يَحْكُمُ بِهِ ذَوَا عَدْلٍ مِنْكُمْ ﴾ (المائدة: ٩٥) أثبت لهما الحكم في الهدي، ثم عطف عليه التكفير بالإطعام والصوم بكلمة "أو " ، فيكون الخيار إليهما ضرورة، وللشيخين أن قوله تعالى: أَوْ كَفَّارَة (المائدة: ٩٥) معطوف على "فجزاء"، وكذا قوله : أَوْ عَدْلُ ذَلِكَ صِيَاما (المائدة : ٩٥) معطوف عليه، فلا يدخل تحت حكمهما، وإنما كان يدخل إن لو كان مجروراً عطفاً على الضمير في "به"؛ لأنه مفعول "يحكم"، وهذا مرفوع، فلم يكن فيه دلالة على اختيار الحكمين، وإنما يرجع إلى الحكمين في معرفة القيمة لا غير، ولأن التخيير شرع رفقا لمن عليه، فيكون الخيار إليه كما في كفارة اليمين.
ثم إذا وقع الاختيار على الهدي لا يجوز إلا ما يجوز في الأضحية عند الإمام، فإذا بلغت القيمة ما لا يضحى به كالعناق مثلاً لم يجز فيه إلا التصدق، ولا يصح العناق جزاء، وقالا: يصح ويذبح؛ لعموم قوله: مِنَ النَّعَمِ ﴾ (المائدة: ٩٥)، ولأن إراقة الدم ليست بقربة إلا في زمن مخصوص كما عرف ثم الجزاء عندنا على التخيير المشروح من الهدي أو الإطعام أو الصيام، وعند زفر على الترتيب، فيجب الهدي أولاً، ثم الإطعام ثم الصيام؛ لأن الجزاء في مقابلة الجناية، والملائم بحال الجاني هو الترتيب، ولنا أن "أو " في الآية للتخيير، فإن اختار التكفير بالهدي فعليه الذبح في الحرم والتصدق بلحمه على الفقراء؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿هَدْياً بَالِغَ الْكَعْبَةِ (المائدة: ٩٥) أو بالإطعام، فيجوز في غير الحرم؛ لأنه قربة معقولة المعنى فلا يتقيد بالحرم خلافاً للشافعي، هو يقيس على الهدي، ولنا أن القربة في الذبح بالإراقة، وهي غير معقولة المعنى، فلهذا تقيد بالحرم أو بالصوم، فيجوز في غيره بالإجماع؛ لأنه عبادة قهر النفس، فلا يختلف باختلاف المكان. عيني، فتح، مستخلص) سنه صاع: من بر أو أقل من صاع تمر أو شعير أو كان الواجب ابتداء أقل منه. . (ط) نتف: الشعر والريش ونحوه نزعه. (مسكين) ضمن الخ: اعتباراً للجزء بالكل، وهذا إذا برئ وبقي أثره، أما إذا مات ضمن كله ولو لم يبق له أثر لا شيء عليه، وكذا لو قلع سنه فنبتت أو ضرب عينه فابيضت ثم زال البياض، وقال أبو يوسف يلزمه صدقة للألم، وعلى هذا لو قلع أو ضرب عينه فابيضت، فنبت له سن وزال البياض، وفي "البدائع": لا يسقط عنه الضمان [ رمز الحقائق: ۱۷۸/۱] وهو المناسب للإطلاق، ولو غاب عنه ولم يدر أمات أو لا لزمه كل القيمة، والمسألة مقيدة بأن لا يخرجه القطع عن حيز الامتناع، فإن أخرجه ضمن كل القيمة، وأن يقصد القطع، فإن لم يقصده كما إذا خلص حمامة من سنور فتلفت فلا شيء عليه، وكذا في كل قتل أريد به الإصلاح وأن لا يقتله بعد قبل أن يكفر، وإن قتله كان عليه كفارة واحدة، وما نقصته الجراحة ساقط. (فتح) ما نقص فيقوم سليما وجريحا فيغرم ما بين القيمتين. (ط)
Book of Hajj. Penalty for killing and wounding game. In Kanz: It is the value of the game assessed by two just men at the place it was killed or the nearest location to it; then he buys with it a hadi (sacrificial animal), meaning the penalty, meaning in the nearest, meaning the killer, and slaughters it if it reaches the amount for a hadi; or [he buys] food and gives it in charity like fitr; or he fasts for every poor person one day. The meaning: if he wishes, at the sanctuary its value; if he wishes, he buys with it; meaning with the food if he wishes; by the value; meaning from every half sa'.
Union. The value of the game: The basis in considering the value of the game is consideration of time and place, and this is the most correct. The intended meaning is its evaluation according to its natural state. As for its acquired state by training, it is not considered in the valuation for the expiation, contrary to valuation for compensation to the owner. The value is considered in terms of it being game, not in terms of any increase by craftsmanship. Muhammad and al-Shafi'i said: The penalty is what resembles the game in appearance if it has a counterpart from livestock; because of His statement: 'So a penalty: the like of what he killed from livestock' (5:95). Its interpretation: Upon him is a penalty from livestock like the killed. So whoever says it is like it from dirhams has contradicted the text. For this reason, the Companions made the counterpart obligatory – i.e., the likeness in form – so a badanah (camel) is obligatory for an ostrich, a cow for a wild donkey, a sheep for a gazelle, a young goat for a rabbit, and for what has no counterpart like a sparrow, it is guaranteed by value. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that the obligatory is the likeness, and the absolute likeness is the likeness in form. When it is impossible [in form], the likeness in meaning is considered, and a likeness in form without meaning is not considered legally. For this reason, if someone destroys another's property, its like is obligatory if it is a mithli (fungible); otherwise its value, even if he destroys an animal, an animal like it is not obligatory upon him even if of the same species, due to the difference in meanings. So what do you think about when the species differs? If the species is impossible both in form and meaning, then it must be carried to the likeness in meaning, which is the value; either because it is customary in the law, or because it is intended by consensus in what has no counterpart, so the counterpart is not intended, because one word does not cover two different places. And because His statement: 'Do not kill game while you are sacred' (5:95) is general for all game, and the pronoun in 'whoever kills it' refers back to it, so 'the like' in His statement: 'and whoever kills it intentionally, so a penalty: the like of what he killed from livestock' (5:95) must be a like for all, and we have no like that encompasses all except value. The intended meaning of 'livestock' is game, because the name 'livestock' is applied to wild animals. The intended meaning of what is narrated from the Companions is estimation without requiring the specific entity. And because in His statement: 'So transgress against him with the like of what he transgressed against you' (2:194), this 'like' in the verse is value in compensation by consensus, so likewise here. (Fath) 'By evaluation': connected to an omitted element: i.e., a value evaluated by the evaluation of two just men. 'Just' here means one who has knowledge and insight into the value of the game, not justice in the chapter of testimony. (Fath) 'His killing place' with fathah on the mim: i.e., the place where the game was killed. (Ayni) 'Or a place near it': i.e., the killing place if it is in a wilderness where game is not sold. (Ayni) 'A hadi from camels, cattle, and sheep' and this is the narration of al-Karkhi, and the author of al-Hidayah chose it because of the command reported concerning killing the wolf, the mouse, the kite, and the crow, narrated by Ibn Abi Shaybah. (Fath) 'Like fitr': so he gives each poor person, even a dhimmi, half a sa' of wheat or a sa' of dates or barley, and less than that is not permissible. (Taftazani) 'Or fasts etc.': [If he wishes, he values the killed game as food and then fasts. (Taftazani)] The choice is for the killer of the game: he may make its value a hadi that is valid for udhiyah from camels, cattle, and sheep, and slaughter it in the sanctuary; the intended meaning of the Kaaba in the verse is the sanctuary, expressed by its noblest; or he may make it food and give it in charity as in sadaqat al-fitr; or he may value it as food and then fast in place of food for each poor person one day. From Muhammad and al-Shafi'i: = One day per poor person, and if there is a remainder less than half a sa', he gives it in charity or fasts one day. And if he wounds it or cuts off its limb or plucks its feathers, he guarantees the diminution. The choice is for the two judges because of His statement: 'judgment by two just men from among you' (5:95). He established for them the judgment concerning the hadi, then He joined to it expiation by feeding and fasting with the word 'or', so the choice is necessarily for them. The two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that His statement: 'or an expiation' (5:95) is conjoined to 'so a penalty', and likewise His statement: 'or the equivalent of that in fasting' (5:95) is conjoined to it, so it does not enter under their judgment. It would only enter if it were in the genitive case, conjoined to the pronoun in 'be it' because it is the object of 'judges', and this is in the nominative, so there is no indication of the choice of the two judges in it. They only refer to the two judges for knowing the value, nothing else. And because making a choice is legislated out of ease for the one upon whom it is incumbent, so the choice is for him, as in the expiation of an oath. Then when the choice falls on the hadi, only what is valid for udhiyah according to the Imam (Abu Hanifa) is permissible. If the value reaches what is not valid for udhiyah, like a young goat, then only charity is permissible, and the young goat is not valid as a penalty. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is valid and he slaughters it, due to the generality of His statement: 'from livestock' (5:95), and because shedding blood is not an act of worship except at a specific time as is known. Then the penalty according to us is based on the explained choice of hadi, feeding, or fasting. According to Zufar, it is based on order: the hadi first, then feeding, then fasting, because the penalty is in exchange for the violation, and the appropriate thing for the situation of the violator is order. Our evidence is that 'or' in the verse is for choice. If he chooses expiation by hadi, then upon him is to slaughter in the sanctuary and give its meat in charity to the poor, due to His statement: 'a hadi reaching the Kaaba' (5:95). Or by feeding, it is permissible outside the sanctuary, because it is a rationally understandable act of worship, so it is not restricted to the sanctuary, contrary to al-Shafi'i, who analogizes it to the hadi. Our evidence is that the act of worship in slaughter is by spilling blood, which is not rationally understandable, so for this reason it is restricted to the sanctuary. Or by fasting, it is permissible elsewhere by consensus, because it is an act of worship of subduing the soul, so it does not differ by place. (Ayni, Fath, Mustakhlas) 'Year: a sa' of wheat or less than a sa' of dates or barley, or if the obligatory amount initially was less than that. (Taftazani) 'Plucking': pulling out hair, feathers, and the like. (Miskin) 'He guarantees the diminution etc.': considering the part as the whole. This is if it heals and its effect remains. If it dies, he guarantees the entire [value], even if no effect remains, there is nothing upon him. Likewise, if he pulls out its tooth and it grows back, or strikes its eye and it becomes white then the whiteness disappears. Abu Yusuf said: A charity is obligatory upon him for the pain. Based on this, if he pulls out or strikes its eye and it becomes white, then a tooth grows and the whiteness disappears, in al-Bada'i: the guarantee does not fall from him. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 178/1] And it is appropriate for the absolute statement. If it is absent and he does not know whether it died or not, the entire value is binding upon him. The issue is conditioned by: that the cutting does not remove it from the realm of being uncatchable; if it removes it, he guarantees the entire value, and that he intends the cutting; if he did not intend it, like if he rescued a pigeon from a cat and it died, then nothing is upon him. Likewise, in every killing intended for reformation, and that he does not kill it afterward before expiation; if he kills it, there is one expiation upon him, and the diminution from the wound is cancelled. (Fath) 'What is diminished': so he evaluates [the animal] sound and wounded and pays the difference between the two values. (Taftazani)
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, with commentary from Fath al-Qadir, 'Ayni, Taftazani, and others, treats the penalty (jaza') for a person in ihram who kills or wounds game (sayd). The base ruling from the matn states that the value of the killed game is assessed by two just men at the place of killing or the nearest such place. This value is then used to purchase a sacrificial animal (hady) if sufficient, otherwise it is given as food charity (like fitr: half sa' of wheat or a sa' of dates/barley per poor person), or the hunter fasts one day for each poor person's portion of food. The commentary then expands into several disputes. First, the nature of the penalty: Muhammad al-Shaybani and al-Shafi'i hold that the penalty must be a physical equivalent (mithl) from livestock resembling the game in form, citing the verse 'so a penalty: the like of what he killed from livestock' and the practice of the Companions (e.g., a camel for an ostrich). Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf argue that absolute likeness is likeness in form, but when that is impossible, the likeness in meaning (value) is considered; otherwise, no single physical animal can be a perfect equivalent even within the same species, let alone across species. They support this with the analogy of property torts: a mithli property requires compensation by its like, but non-mithli requires value. They further argue that the verse's 'like' must apply to all game, and only value can be a universal equivalent. The next dispute is about who holds the choice (khayr) among the three options. The passage reports a view that the choice belongs to the two judges (hakamayn) based on 'judgment by two just men'. But the shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that the choice is for the hunter himself, because 'or' in the verse joins the options to 'so a penalty', not to the object of 'judges'; the judges only determine the value, not the mode of expiation. Then the text discusses conditions for the hady: according to Abu Hanifa, it must be valid for udhiyah (sacrifice) in terms of age and type; if the value does not reach that, charity is given instead. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow slaughter of any livestock mentioned in 'from livestock'. Finally, the passage covers wounding: the hunter guarantees the diminution in value, with details about healing, death, and intent. Notably, if the animal dies after healing with no effect, nothing is due; if it dies from the wound, full value is due. Abu Yusuf also requires sadaqah for pain. The overall ruling is mufta bihi with the choice for the hunter, based on ease (takhfif).

Key Terms
صيد (sayd): Game animals that are permissible to eat outside of ihram but prohibited to hunt while in ihram or in the sanctuary.
جزاء (jaza'): The penalty or compensation for killing or wounding game while in ihram, consisting of hadi, food charity, or fasting.
مثل (mithl): Likeness; used in the verse to describe the penalty. The dispute is whether it means physical similarity (a specific animal) or equivalence in value.
قيمة (qimah): Monetary value assessed by two experts for the purpose of the penalty.
هدي (hady): An animal (camel, cow, sheep) that is slaughtered in the sanctuary (Mina) as part of the penalty.
عدلين (adlayn): Two just men; here meaning two experts who know the value of game, not necessarily witnesses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, who has the choice (khayr) among the three options (hadi, food, fasting) for the penalty of killing game in ihram?
A) The two just men who assess the value
B) The hunter himself
C) The judge (qadi)
D) The imam of the sanctuary

Key Takeaway
The penalty for killing game in ihram is the value assessed by two experts, and the hunter may choose between hadi, charity, or fasting.

Who Chooses the Penalty? The Hakamayn vs. the Muhrim
Intra-Hanafi dispute over who selects penalty type for killing game

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi position on who chooses the penalty type for killing game during Hajj and explain the grammatical argument (i'rab) from Quran 5:95 that supports it.

Core Idea
The two just men only value the game; the muhrim chooses the penalty type.

When a pilgrim in ihram kills game, the Quran requires a penalty. But who decides whether the penalty is a sacrifice, feeding the poor, or fasting? This lesson unpacks a subtle grammatical dispute within the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa argues that the two just men only assess the value, while the Sahibayn hold they also choose the type. The ruling hinges on the case ending of a single word.

Guided Path
1
State the dispute
Identify the two positions within the Hanafi school: the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that the two just men (al-hakamayn) choose the type of penalty; Abu Hanifa holds that the muhrim chooses. The two just men only determine the value of the game.
2
Examine the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn rely on the word 'or' (أو) in Quran 5:95 that connects 'or a compensation' and 'or the equivalent of that in fasting' to the verb 'judges', implying the two just men have authority over the choice.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's grammatical counter
Abu Hanifa points out that 'or a compensation' (أَوْ كَفَّارَة) and 'or the equivalent of that in fasting' (أَوْ عَدْلُ ذَلِكَ صِيَامًا) are in the nominative case (marfu'), not genitive. If they were governed by the verb, they would be genitive (majrur). Therefore, they are independent clauses, not under the judgment of the two just men.
This is a classic Hanafi use of i'rab (grammatical analysis) for legal deduction.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Abu Hanifa's view, after the two just men assign a value, the muhrim may choose any of the three penalties (hady, feeding, or fasting). Under the Sahibayn's view, the two just men decide which specific penalty applies.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's view. This is supported by the weight of the grammatical argument and later Hanafi authorities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جزاء قتل الصيد وجرحه
مسكين يوما، ولو فضل أقل من نصف صاع تصدّق به أو صام يوما، وإن جرحه
من الطعام بعد هذا الحساب
أو قطع عضوه أو نتف شعره ضمن ما نقص منه،
أي الصيد
إن شاء
إن شاء
المحرم الصيد
- الخيار إلى الحكمين لقوله تعالى: ﴿يَحْكُمُ بِهِ ذَوَا عَدْلٍ مِنْكُمْ ﴾ (المائدة: ٩٥) أثبت لهما الحكم في الهدي، ثم عطف عليه التكفير بالإطعام والصوم بكلمة "أو " ، فيكون الخيار إليهما ضرورة، وللشيخين أن قوله تعالى: أَوْ كَفَّارَة (المائدة: ٩٥) معطوف على "فجزاء"، وكذا قوله : أَوْ عَدْلُ ذَلِكَ صِيَاما (المائدة : ٩٥) معطوف عليه، فلا يدخل تحت حكمهما، وإنما كان يدخل إن لو كان مجروراً عطفاً على الضمير في "به"؛ لأنه مفعول "يحكم"، وهذا مرفوع، فلم يكن فيه دلالة على اختيار الحكمين، وإنما يرجع إلى الحكمين في معرفة القيمة لا غير،
Compensation for killing game and wounding him: a poor person for a day, and if less than half a sa' remains, give charity or fast a day. And if he wounds him or cuts his limb or plucks his hair, he guarantees what is diminished from him, i.e., the game, if he wishes (repeated). The choice is for the two just men, due to His statement: '...judged by two just men among you' (5:95). He established for them the judgment concerning the sacrificial animal, then He connected to it the atonement by feeding and fasting with the word 'or', so the choice is necessarily for them. And for the two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): His statement 'or a compensation' (5:95) is attached to 'so a penalty', and likewise His statement 'or the equivalent of that in fasting' is attached to it, so it does not come under their judgment. It would only come under if it were in the genitive case attached to the pronoun in 'by it' because it is the object of 'judges', and this is nominative, so there is no indication of the choice of the two just men. Rather, they are referred to only for knowledge of the value, nothing else.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the interpretation of Quran 5:95 concerning the penalty for a muhrim who kills game. The initial part of the text appears corrupted, but the core issue is clear: the phrase 'the choice is for the two just men' represents the view attributed to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), who hold that the two just men have the authority to choose the type of penalty (hady, feeding, or fasting). The author of the matn (likely al-Quduri) initially states this view, but then presents Abu Hanifa's argument using the wording 'for the two shaykhs' (wa li al-shaykhayn). Abu Hanifa argues that the verse 'or a compensation' and 'or the equivalent of that in fasting' are in the nominative case, not attached to the object of 'judges', so the two just men only determine the value of the game, not the choice of penalty type. The penalty type is chosen by the muhrim himself, similar to the oath expiation. This is a classic Hanafi method of grammatical analysis (i'rab) to derive rulings. The passage demonstrates the importance of Arabic syntax in legal deduction.

Key Terms
الحكمين (al-hakamayn): Two just men authorized to judge the compensation for killing game during Hajj.
الجزاء (al-jaza'): The penalty required for killing game while in ihram: hady, feeding the poor, or fasting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The type of penalty (hady, feeding, fasting).
B) The value of the game.
C) The number of days of fasting.
D) Which animals are considered game.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the muhrim chooses the penalty type; the two just men only assess the value.

Penalty for Killing Game: Hady, Feeding, or Fasting
Rulings on penalty types, their conditions, and exempt animals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three penalty options, explain the Hanafi position on their order, and identify which animals are exempt from compensation and the evidence for each.

Core Idea
The penalty for killing game is a choice between hady, feeding, or fasting; hady must be in the Haram, but feeding is valid anywhere.

This passage details the penalty (jaza') for a muhrim who kills game. It addresses the type of hady animal, whether the penalty is by choice or fixed order, and where each option can be performed. It also lists harmful animals that are exempt from compensation, based on explicit hadith. Understanding these nuances is critical for correctly applying the Hajj penalties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three penalty options and the order dispute
Read the first part of the passage. It states that the penalty is either hady (sacrificial animal), feeding the poor, or fasting. Zufar held a fixed order; the Hanafi school holds that the muhrim chooses freely. Identify the Quranic 'or' as the proof for choice.
The Arabic 'أو' (or) in verse 5:95 is the key textual evidence.
2
Understand the conditions for the hady animal
According to Abu Hanifa, the hady must be an animal eligible for udhiya (Eid sacrifice). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow any cattle. Note the difference based on the generality of 'min al-na'am' (from the cattle) versus restriction via analogy to udhiya.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the mufta bihi is the choice-based view, but the hady condition is important in practice.
3
Analyze location restrictions
Hady must be slaughtered in the Haram (due to 'baligh al-Ka'ba'). Feeding is permissible outside the Haram because it is a rationally understood act of worship, unlike slaughter. Fasting is valid anywhere by consensus.
Contrast with al-Shafi'i who analogizes feeding to hady.
4
List the exempt harmful animals
The passage lists crow, kite, wolf, snake, scorpion, mouse, and ferocious dog. Understand that only the pied crow (the harmful one) is exempt, not the magpie. The dog must be ferocious ('aqur).
The evidence is the hadith of the five evil ones (kite, snake, scorpion, mouse, ferocious dog). The wolf is added via other narrations.
5
Identify when full value vs. partial compensation is due
Full value is due for acts that remove the animal's ability to escape (e.g., cutting legs, breaking wings). Partial compensation is for lesser harm (e.g., plucking feathers that don't impede flight). Breaking eggs and milking also incur value.
The principle: if the muhrim destroys the animal's means of defense (man'i), full value; otherwise, only the diminution in value.

وتجب القيمة: لأن بنتف الريش وقطع القوائم فوت عليه الأمن بتفويت آلة الامتناع فكان كالإتلاف، ومقتضاه أن نتف الريش إذا لم يمنعه الطيران لا يوجب ضمان كل القيمة، بل النقصان فقط، وأما في كسر البيض فروي ذلك عن علي وابن عباس اللهما ، ولأنه أصل الصيد وله عرضية أن يصير صيداً فنزل منزلته احتياطاً، وقوله: و خروج فرخ" أي يجب قيمة البيض والفرخ الحي إن ظهر من البيض بعد كسره فرخ ميت، والقياس أن لا يجب به سوى البيضة، وكذا لو ضرب بطن ظبية فألقت جنيناً ميتاً ثم ماتت تجب قيمتهما، أما الأم فظاهر وأما الجنين فلأن ضرب البطن سبب ظاهر لموته، وقد ظهر عقبه ميتاً فيحال عليه، بخلاف من ضرب بطن امرأة فألقت جنيناً ميتاً وماتت، حيث يجب ضمان الأصل لا ضمان الجنين سوى الغرة نصف عشر الدية في سنته في الحرة، وفي الأمة يجب قيمة الأم ونصف عشر قيمة الولد لو كان ذكراً أو عشر قيمته لو كان أنثى، وإن قتل خنزيراً أو قرداً أو فيلاً تحب القيمة؛ لأنها الصيود، ولا تبتدئ بالأذى غالباً خلافاً لزفر؛ لأنها ليست بصيود عنده، وإن قتل الضب من واليربوع تجب القيمة عند الإمام؛ لأنها من الصيود، وعندهما من حشرات الأرض، وعلل الزيلعي وجوب الجزاء بقتل الضب واليربوع بأنها ليست من المستثنيات في الحديث، ولا تبتدئ بالأذى. (فتح، عيني)

وحية وعقرب: لقوله عليه: "خمس" من الفواسق يقتلن في الحل والحرم الحدأة، والحية، والعقرب، والفأرة، والكلب العقور". (فتح، مستخلص وكلب عقور من العقر وهو الجرح. تبيين الحقائق: ٣٨٣/٢] وعن أبي يوسف أن الأسد بمنزلة الكلب العقور، وفي ظاهر الرواية: السباع كلها صيد إلا الكلب والذئب، وقيد بالعقور اتباعاً للحديث مع أن العقور وغيره سواء أهلياً كان أو وحشياً؛ لأن غير العقور ليس بصيد، فلا يجب الجزاء بقتله، ولكن لا يحل قتل ما لا يؤذي إذا لم يكن لمه ضرر (فتح) عقور وعن أبي حنيفة: العقور وغيره والمستأنس والمتوحش منه سواء، وعنه : لا يجب أيضاً شيء بقتل السنور ولو كان بريا. (ع)
Then, if the choice falls on the sacrificial animal, only what is permissible for the animal of sacrifice (udhiya) is permissible according to Imam Abu Hanifa. If the value reaches what is not sacrificed, such as a young goat, then only charity is permissible, and the young goat is not valid as a penalty. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is valid and should be slaughtered, due to the generality of His statement: 'from the cattle' (5:95), and because the shedding of blood is not an act of worship except in a specific time as known. Then the penalty according to us is based on the explained choice: either hady, feeding, or fasting. According to Zufar, it is based on order: hady first, then feeding, then fasting, because the penalty is in exchange for the offense, and what is suitable for the offender is order. Our proof is that 'or' in the verse indicates choice. If he chooses atonement by hady, he must slaughter in the Haram and give its meat in charity to the poor, due to His statement: 'hady reaching the Ka'ba' (5:95). Or by feeding: it is permissible outside the Haram, because it is a rationally understandable act of worship, so it is not restricted to the Haram, contrary to al-Shafi'i, who analogizes to hady. Our proof is that the act of worship in slaughter is through the shedding of blood, which is not rationally understandable, so it is restricted to the Haram. Or by fasting: it is permissible elsewhere by consensus, because it is an act of subduing the soul, so it does not differ by place. (Commentaries)...

[Page 303] The value is obligatory for plucking its feathers, cutting its legs, milking it, breaking its eggs, and the exit of a dead chick due to the break. (Full value for the bird). And nothing for killing a crow, kite, wolf, snake, scorpion, mouse, and ferocious dog (wild and domestic). The value is obligatory because plucking feathers and cutting legs removes its safety by removing its means of defense, so it is like destroying it. Its implication is that plucking feathers that does not prevent it from flying does not necessitate full value, only the diminution. As for breaking eggs, it is narrated from Ali and Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them), and because it is the origin of game and has the potential to become game, so it is treated as such out of precaution. His statement (Quduri): 'and the exit of a chick' means the value of the egg and the live chick is obligatory if from the egg after breaking a dead chick emerges. By analogy, only the value of the egg would be obligatory. Similarly, if he struck the belly of a doe and she aborted a dead fetus, then died, the value of both is obligatory. As for the mother, it is clear; as for the fetus, because striking the belly is an apparent cause of its death, and it appeared dead afterwards, so it is attributed to it. This differs from striking a woman's belly causing a dead fetus and her death, where only the compensation for the woman is obligatory, not the fetus, except the ghurra (half of one-tenth of the diyah) for a free woman. For a slave woman, the value of the mother and half-tenth of the value of the child if male, or one-tenth if female. If he kills a pig, monkey, or elephant, the value is obligatory because they are game and do not usually initiate harm, contrary to Zufar, because they are not game according to him. If he kills a dabb (lizard) or jerboa, the value is obligatory according to Imam Abu Hanifa because they are game; according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), they are considered vermin. al-Zayla'i explained the obligation for killing dabb and jerboa by the fact that they are not among the exceptions in the hadith and do not initiate harm. (Fath, 'Ayni) Cutting its legs and breaking its wings takes it out of being able to defend itself with its wings and legs. (Miskin) Milking: meaning the value of the milk from milking is obligatory because milk is part of its parts. Breaking its eggs: because it is the origin of game, so the value of the eggs is obligatory; if they are rotten, nothing is obligatory. ('Ayni) 'Exit': similarly, the value is obligatory for the exit (i.e., of the chick) due to the break, because the apparent cause is that it died from it. ('Ayni) Crow: it eats carrion and initiates harm, unlike the magpie and the crow of the cornfield. ('Ayni) He (Quduri) made it absolute, so it includes killing in ihram or the Haram. What is meant is the pied crow that eats carrion and mixes impurity with pure food. As for the magpie, the muhrim incurs compensation for killing it because it is not called a crow customarily and does not initiate harm. (Fath) 'Kite' meaning: he does not kill a kite – on the pattern of 'utbah, a bird that catches field mice. ('Ayni, Miskin) 'Wolf': in the narration of al-Karkhi, and the author of al-Hidayah chose it, due to the command of the Prophet (ﷺ) to kill the wolf, mouse, kite, and crow, narrated by Ibn Abi Shayba. (Fath) 'Snake and scorpion': due to his statement (ﷺ): 'Five evil ones are killed in the halal and Haram: the kite, snake, scorpion, mouse, and ferocious dog.' (Fath, Mustakhlas) 'Ferocious dog' (kalb 'aqur): from 'aqr meaning wounding. (Tabiyin al-Haqa'iq 2:383) And from Abu Yusuf: the lion is like the ferocious dog. In the zahir al-riwaya: all predators are game except the dog and wolf. It is restricted to 'aqur following the hadith, although the ferocious and non-ferocious are the same, domestic or wild; because the non-ferocious is not game, so no compensation is obligatory for killing it, but it is not permissible to kill what does not harm if there is no harm from it. (Fath) 'Aqur: And from Abu Hanifa: the ferocious and non-ferocious, domesticated and wild, are the same. And from him: nothing is obligatory for killing a cat even if it is wild. ('Ayni)
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the penalty (jaza') for killing game while in ihram, following the earlier dispute on who chooses the penalty. It is a ruling with proof, covering several sub-issues. The text first addresses the minimum value of the hady (sacrificial animal): according to Abu Hanifa, it must be an animal eligible for udhiya (sacrifice on Eid al-Adha), so a young goat is insufficient. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow it based on the generality of 'min al-na'am'. Then it presents Zufar's view that the penalties are in a fixed order (hady first, then feeding, then fasting), which is rejected because the Quranic 'or' indicates choice. The location of the penalty is specified: hady must be in the Haram, feeding can be outside, fasting anywhere. This is contrasted with al-Shafi'i's analogical reasoning. The second part discusses cases where full value is required: plucking feathers or cutting legs that impair flight, milking, breaking eggs (from which a dead chick emerges). Harmful animals are exempt: crow, kite, wolf, snake, scorpion, mouse, and ferocious dog. Details on the definition of crow (excluding magpie) and dog (restricted to those that attack) are given, with references to hadith. The passage also covers comparisons to human injury cases (ghurra for fetus). The commentary within parentheses clarifies each point.

Key Terms
الهدي (al-hady): The sacrificial animal offered as a penalty for killing game; must be taken to the Haram.
الإطعام (al-it'am): Feeding the poor, either in the Haram or outside, as a penalty option.
الصيام (al-siyam): Fasting as a penalty, valid anywhere.
الغراب (al-ghurab): The crow; specifically the pied crow that eats carrion and harms, exempt from compensation.
الكلب العقور (al-kalb al-'aqur): Ferocious dog that attacks; included in the five harmful animals exempt from penalty.

Key Takeaway
The penalty for killing game while in ihram is a choice between hady (in the Haram), feeding (anywhere), or fasting (anywhere); harmful animals are exempt from compensation.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
6 min
Compensation for Plucking Feathers and Cutting Legs
State ruling and explain compensation for plucking and cutting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that plucking feathers and cutting legs of game in ihram require full compensation, and apply the qiyas to determine when only the decrease in value is due.

Core Idea
Removing the game's means of self-defense is like destroying it, requiring full compensation.

When a muhrim harms game by plucking its feathers or cutting its legs, he has effectively removed the animal's means of self-defense, making it vulnerable. This act is treated as destruction, necessitating the full value. However, if the harm does not impair the animal's ability to escape, only the reduction in value is owed. Understanding this principle will help you determine compensation in various scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts triggering full value
The text lists plucking feathers, cutting legs, and milking as acts requiring full compensation. What do these have in common?
They all remove a means of self-defense or use.
2
Understand the qiyas reasoning
The author explains that by removing the means of self-defense (آلة الامتناع), the security of the game is forfeited, and this is like causing destruction. In Hanafi usul, this is a qiyas jaliy.
Means of self-defense includes feathers for flight and legs for running.
3
Apply the exception
If plucking feathers does not prevent the bird from flying, then the full value is not due; only the decrease in value because of the missing feathers is compensated.
This shows that the full value is based on the effective loss of security.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جزاء قتل الصيد وجرحه وتجب القيمة بنتف ريشه وقطع قوائمه وحلبه وكسر بيضه وخروج فرخ ميت به، الكاملة [؟] وتجب القيمة: لأن بنتف الريش وقطع القوائم فوت عليه الأمن بتفويت آلة الامتناع فكان كالإتلاف، ومقتضاه أن نتف الريش إذا لم يمنعه الطيران لا يوجب ضمان كل القيمة، بل النقصان فقط، وأما في كسر البيض فروي ذلك عن علي وابن عباس رضي الله عنهما، ولأنه أصل الصيد وله عرضية أن يصير صيداً فنزل منزلته احتياطاً، وقوله: و خروج فرخ" أي يجب قيمة البيض والفرخ الحي إن ظهر من البيض بعد كسره فرخ ميت، والقياس أن لا يجب به سوى البيضة، وكذا لو ضرب بطن ظبية فألقت جنيناً ميتاً ثم ماتت تجب قيمتهما، أما الأم فظاهر وأما الجنين فلأن ضرب البطن سبب ظاهر لموته، وقد ظهر عقبه ميتاً فيحال عليه، بخلاف من ضرب بطن امرأة فألقت جنيناً ميتاً وماتت، حيث يجب ضمان الأصل لا ضمان الجنين سوى الغرة نصف عشر الدية في سنته في الحرة، وفي الأمة يجب قيمة الأم ونصف عشر قيمة الولد لو كان ذكراً أو عشر قيمته لو كان أنثى، وإن قتل خنزيراً أو قرداً أو فيلاً تجب القيمة؛ لأنها الصيود، ولا تبتدئ بالأذى غالباً خلافاً لزفر؛ لأنها ليست بصيود عنده، وإن قتل الضب من واليربوع تجب القيمة عند الإمام؛ لأنها من الصيود، وعندهما من حشرات الأرض، وعلل الزيلعي وجوب الجزاء بقتل الضب واليربوع بأنها ليست من المستثنيات في الحديث، ولا تبتدئ بالأذى. (فتح، عيني)
Chapter of Hajj. Compensation for killing and wounding game. And the value is obligatory for plucking its feathers, cutting its legs, milking it, breaking its eggs, and the emergence of a dead chick from it, the complete [؟]. And the value is obligatory because by plucking the feathers and cutting the legs, he deprived it of security by removing its means of self-defense, so it is like causing destruction. Its implication is that if plucking the feathers does not prevent it from flying, it does not necessitate compensation of the entire value, but only the decrease. As for breaking the eggs, that is reported from Ali and Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them, and because the egg is the origin of the game and has the potential to become game, so it is treated as such as a precaution. And His statement: 'and the emergence of a chick' means the value of the egg and the live chick is obligatory if after breaking the egg a dead chick appears, but by analogy only the egg should be obligatory. Similarly, if one strikes the belly of a gazelle and it aborts a dead fetus and then dies, the value of both is obligatory. As for the mother, it is apparent; as for the fetus, because striking the belly is an apparent cause for its death, and it appeared dead after him, so it is attributed to him. Contrary to the case where one strikes the belly of a woman and she aborts a dead fetus and dies: the compensation for the mother is obligatory, but for the fetus only the ghurra is obligatory, which is half of one-tenth of the diya for a free person, and for a slave woman, the value of the mother and half of one-tenth of the value of the child if it is male, or one-tenth of its value if it is female. And if one kills a pig, monkey, or elephant, the value is obligatory because they are game and do not usually initiate harm, contrary to Zufar, because in his view they are not game. And if one kills a dabb (lizard) or a jerboa, the value is obligatory according to Imam Abu Hanifa because they are game, but according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) they are among the insects of the earth. Al-Zayla'i explained the obligation of compensation for killing the dabb and jerboa by saying they are not among the exceptions in the hadith and do not initiate harm. (Fath, Ayni)
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the compensation (jaza') for a muhrim who harms game. The initial ruling states that the value (qimah) is due for specific acts: plucking feathers, cutting legs, milking, breaking eggs, and causing a dead chick to emerge. The commentary explains the reasoning: plucking and cutting remove the game's means of self-defense, making it like outright destruction. If plucking doesn't prevent flight, only the reduction in value is due. Breaking eggs is supported by reports from Ali and Ibn Abbas, and because the egg is the origin of the game. The analogy with a gazelle fetus shows that if the mother dies from a blow, the full value of both is due. For a human fetus, only the ghurra (half of one-tenth of diya) is due for a free woman, and a proportional amount for a slave woman. The passage then covers specific animals: pig, monkey, and elephant are game and require compensation, contrary to Zufar who denies they are game. For the dabb (lizard) and jerboa, Imam Abu Hanifa requires compensation, while the Sahibayn consider them insects (no compensation). Al-Zayla'i supports Abu Hanifa because they are not in the five exceptions of the hadith and do not initiate harm. The Hanafi position is that compensation is wajib for these acts and animals, with the noted intra-madhhab difference for dabb and jerboa.

Key Terms
القيمة (al-qimah): The market value of the game animal or its parts, assessed at the place and time of the injury.
الصيد (al-sayd): Wild animals or birds that are permissible to hunt outside ihram but prohibited in ihram or the Haram.
آلة الامتناع (aalat al-imitinaa): The means of self-defense, such as feathers for flight and legs for running, whose removal triggers full compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) A sheep as penalty

Key Takeaway
Full compensation for harming game is due only when the act removes the animal's means of self-defense; otherwise, only the diminished value is compensated.

Compensation for Breaking Eggs and Aborting Game Fetuses
Explain compensation for eggs and fetuses with analogy and contrast.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the compensation required for breaking game eggs and causing a game fetus to be aborted, and contrast it with the compensation for a human fetus.

Core Idea
A game egg is compensated as the origin of game; a game fetus is included in the mother's compensation, unlike a human fetus with a fixed ghurra.

The text extends compensation to breaking eggs and causing fetal death in game animals, with a striking contrast to human fetuses. For game, the value of the egg and the fetus is included in the mother's compensation, while for humans, only the mother's compensation is due plus a fixed ghurra for the fetus. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the analogy with the gazelle.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling for breaking eggs
The text says that breaking the eggs of game requires the value of the eggs. It supports this with a report from Ali and Ibn Abbas, and by reasoning that the egg is the origin of the game (أصل الصيد) and has the potential to become game.
Compensation is wajib even though the egg is not a fully developed animal.
2
Understand the analogy with the gazelle fetus
If a muhrim strikes a gazelle's belly and it aborts a dead fetus and then dies, the value of both mother and fetus is due. The cause (striking) is apparent and leads to death.
The fetus is treated as part of the mother's value; it is not a separate fixed compensation.
3
Contrast with the human fetus
For a human fetus, only the ghurra (half of one-tenth of diya for a free person) is due, not the full value of the mother. This is because the human fetus has a separate legal status.
The difference shows that game animals are treated as property, while humans have special rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جزاء قتل الصيد وجرحه وتجب القيمة بنتف ريشه وقطع قوائمه وحلبه وكسر بيضه وخروج فرخ ميت به، الكاملة [؟] وتجب القيمة: لأن بنتف الريش وقطع القوائم فوت عليه الأمن بتفويت آلة الامتناع فكان كالإتلاف، ومقتضاه أن نتف الريش إذا لم يمنعه الطيران لا يوجب ضمان كل القيمة، بل النقصان فقط، وأما في كسر البيض فروي ذلك عن علي وابن عباس رضي الله عنهما، ولأنه أصل الصيد وله عرضية أن يصير صيداً فنزل منزلته احتياطاً، وقوله: و خروج فرخ" أي يجب قيمة البيض والفرخ الحي إن ظهر من البيض بعد كسره فرخ ميت، والقياس أن لا يجب به سوى البيضة، وكذا لو ضرب بطن ظبية فألقت جنيناً ميتاً ثم ماتت تجب قيمتهما، أما الأم فظاهر وأما الجنين فلأن ضرب البطن سبب ظاهر لموته، وقد ظهر عقبه ميتاً فيحال عليه، بخلاف من ضرب بطن امرأة فألقت جنيناً ميتاً وماتت، حيث يجب ضمان الأصل لا ضمان الجنين سوى الغرة نصف عشر الدية في سنته في الحرة، وفي الأمة يجب قيمة الأم ونصف عشر قيمة الولد لو كان ذكراً أو عشر قيمته لو كان أنثى، وإن قتل خنزيراً أو قرداً أو فيلاً تجب القيمة؛ لأنها الصيود، ولا تبتدئ بالأذى غالباً خلافاً لزفر؛ لأنها ليست بصيود عنده، وإن قتل الضب من واليربوع تجب القيمة عند الإمام؛ لأنها من الصيود، وعندهما من حشرات الأرض، وعلل الزيلعي وجوب الجزاء بقتل الضب واليربوع بأنها ليست من المستثنيات في الحديث، ولا تبتدئ بالأذى. (فتح، عيني)
Chapter of Hajj. Compensation for killing and wounding game. And the value is obligatory for plucking its feathers, cutting its legs, milking it, breaking its eggs, and the emergence of a dead chick from it, the complete [؟]. And the value is obligatory because by plucking the feathers and cutting the legs, he deprived it of security by removing its means of self-defense, so it is like causing destruction. Its implication is that if plucking the feathers does not prevent it from flying, it does not necessitate compensation of the entire value, but only the decrease. As for breaking the eggs, that is reported from Ali and Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them, and because the egg is the origin of the game and has the potential to become game, so it is treated as such as a precaution. And His statement: 'and the emergence of a chick' means the value of the egg and the live chick is obligatory if after breaking the egg a dead chick appears, but by analogy only the egg should be obligatory. Similarly, if one strikes the belly of a gazelle and it aborts a dead fetus and then dies, the value of both is obligatory. As for the mother, it is apparent; as for the fetus, because striking the belly is an apparent cause for its death, and it appeared dead after him, so it is attributed to him. Contrary to the case where one strikes the belly of a woman and she aborts a dead fetus and dies: the compensation for the mother is obligatory, but for the fetus only the ghurra is obligatory, which is half of one-tenth of the diya for a free person, and for a slave woman, the value of the mother and half of one-tenth of the value of the child if it is male, or one-tenth of its value if it is female. And if one kills a pig, monkey, or elephant, the value is obligatory because they are game and do not usually initiate harm, contrary to Zufar, because in his view they are not game. And if one kills a dabb (lizard) or a jerboa, the value is obligatory according to Imam Abu Hanifa because they are game, but according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) they are among the insects of the earth. Al-Zayla'i explained the obligation of compensation for killing the dabb and jerboa by saying they are not among the exceptions in the hadith and do not initiate harm. (Fath, Ayni)
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the compensation (jaza') for a muhrim who harms game. The initial ruling states that the value (qimah) is due for specific acts: plucking feathers, cutting legs, milking, breaking eggs, and causing a dead chick to emerge. The commentary explains the reasoning: plucking and cutting remove the game's means of self-defense, making it like outright destruction. If plucking doesn't prevent flight, only the reduction in value is due. Breaking eggs is supported by reports from Ali and Ibn Abbas, and because the egg is the origin of the game. The analogy with a gazelle fetus shows that if the mother dies from a blow, the full value of both is due. For a human fetus, only the ghurra (half of one-tenth of diya) is due for a free woman, and a proportional amount for a slave woman. The passage then covers specific animals: pig, monkey, and elephant are game and require compensation, contrary to Zufar who denies they are game. For the dabb (lizard) and jerboa, Imam Abu Hanifa requires compensation, while the Sahibayn consider them insects (no compensation). Al-Zayla'i supports Abu Hanifa because they are not in the five exceptions of the hadith and do not initiate harm. The Hanafi position is that compensation is wajib for these acts and animals, with the noted intra-madhhab difference for dabb and jerboa.

Key Terms
البيض (al-bayd): The egg of a game bird; breaking it requires compensation of its value.
الجنين (al-janin): The fetus of an animal; for game, it is compensated as part of the mother's value.
الغرة (al-ghurra): A fixed compensation for a human fetus: half of one-tenth of the diya for a free person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only the value of the mother
B) Only the value of the fetus
C) The value of both mother and fetus
D) A ghurra for the fetus and full value for the mother

Key Takeaway
Game eggs and fetuses are compensated as part of the game's value, treating them as potential game, unlike human fetuses with fixed compensation.

Compensation for Killing Pig, Monkey, Elephant, Dabb, and Jerboa
Explain compensation for specific animals and the intra-madhhab dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which animals require compensation when killed in ihram according to the Hanafi school, including the intra-madhhab dispute on dabb and jerboa, and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Pig, monkey, elephant, dabb, and jerboa are game requiring compensation; the Hanafi school favours Abu Hanifa's view over the Sahibayn's on dabb and jerboa.

The text specifies that killing a pig, monkey, or elephant in ihram requires compensation because they are considered game and do not normally initiate harm. Zufar disagrees regarding these animals. Then it discusses dabb (lizard) and jerboa: Abu Hanifa requires compensation, but his two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider them mere insects with no compensation. Al-Zayla'i supports Abu Hanifa by noting these animals are not among the exceptions in the hadith and are not aggressive. Understanding this dispute is essential for a mufti to issue the correct fatwa.

Guided Path
1
List the animals mentioned in the text
The text mentions pig, monkey, elephant, dabb, and jerboa as specific animals for which compensation is debated.
These are in addition to general game animals.
2
Understand the Hanafi criterion for game
Compensation is due for animals that are 'sayd' (wild game) and do not normally initiate harm. This excludes harmful animals (like snakes) and domestic animals.
The text says: 'because they are game and do not usually initiate harm.'
3
Identify the disagreement with Zufar
Zufar holds that pig, monkey, and elephant are not game (sayd), so no compensation is due for killing them in ihram.
Zufar's view is mentioned but the relied-upon Hanafi position is that they are game.
4
Analyze the intra-madhhab dispute on dabb and jerboa
Abu Hanifa says they are game, so compensation wajib. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say they are insects of the earth (hajarat al-ard), so no compensation. Al-Zayla'i supports Abu Hanifa with reasoning: they are not exceptions in the hadith and do not initiate harm.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.

Animals Exempt from Compensation in Ihram
Exception list for compensation in ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the animals exempt from compensation when killed by a muhrim, state the Hanafi position with evidence, and explain the intra-madhhab differences regarding the wolf, dog, and cat.

Core Idea
A muhrim may kill five harmful animals without compensation; Hanafis extend this to the wolf and cat by additional proofs.

In the state of ihram, killing game (sayd) normally requires compensation (jaza'). However, certain harmful animals are explicitly exempted by a well-known hadith. This lesson examines which animals are exempt according to the Hanafi school, the textual evidence, and the internal differences among Hanafi imams. Understanding these exceptions is essential for any muhrim to avoid unnecessary penalty or legal misstep.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule and exception
Begin with the principle that a muhrim is forbidden from hunting game; killing it incurs compensation. The hadith of five harmful animals creates an exception.
Game (sayd) refers to wild edible animals; harmful creatures are not considered game.
2
Analyze the hadith of the five fawasiq
Memorize the hadith: 'Five harmful beasts are to be killed in the state of non-ihram and in the state of ihram: the kite, the snake, the scorpion, the mouse, and the biting dog.' This is the core dalil.
The hadith is mutawatir in meaning (qat'i al-thubut) but zanni al-dalala regarding inclusion of other animals.
3
Examine each exempt animal in the text
Work through the commentary's list: crow (only the speckled, harmful type), kite, wolf (per preferred narration), snake, scorpion, biting dog, and cat (per Abu Hanifa). Note the exclusion of magpie from the crow category.
The crow exemption applies only to the abqa' (speckled crow) that eats carrion and initiates harm.
4
Understand intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Note the differences: Abu Yusuf includes the lion under 'biting dog'; Zahir al-Riwayah states all predators are game except dog and wolf; Abu Hanifa exempts the biting and non-biting dog and the cat.
The mufta bihi is the position that includes the five explicit animals plus the wolf and cat based on preferred narrations.
5
Apply the ruling to modern scenarios
Distinguish between animals that are inherently harmful (e.g., scorpion, snake) and those that are wild but not necessarily harmful (e.g., lion, if not attacking). Only those proven by dalil are exempt.
Non-harmful animals like a wild rabbit are game and require compensation if killed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقطع قوائمه وكسر جناحيه فخرج من أن يكون ممتنعاً بجناحه وقوائمه. (مسكين) وحلبه: أي تجب قيمة اللبن من حلبه؛ لأن اللبن من أجزائه وكسر بيضه لأنه أصل الصيد فتجب قيمة البيض، وإن كان فاسداً لا يجب شيء. (ع) وخروج: أي كذا تجب القيمة في خروج (ع) به أي بالكسر ; لأن الظاهر أنه مات به. (ع) غراب: يأكل الجيف ويبتدئ بالأذى، دون العقعق وغراب الذرع . (ع)] أطلقه، فعم القتل في الإحرام أو الحرم، والمراد به الأبقع الذي يأكل الجيف ويخلط النجس مع الطاهر في التناول، وأما العقعق فيجب الجزاء على المحرم بقتله؛ لأنه لا يسمى غرابا عرفاً، ولا يبتدئ بالأذى.
