Hanafi Proof Against al-Shafi'i: Why the Slaughter is Invalid
Inter-madhhab dispute on validity of muhrim's slaughter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dalil that the Quranic term 'qatl' indicates invalid slaughter and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Allah called it killing, not slaughter; therefore it is not valid tadhkiyah.

Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the slaughter itself is technically valid but prohibited for the muhrim. The Hanafis respond with a powerful linguistic proof: the Quran itself uses the word 'qatl' (killing) for this act, not 'dhabh' (slaughter). This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
State the Shafi'i position
Al-Shafi'i holds that the slaughter is effective and makes the meat halal for others, but haram for the muhrim due to his violation.
His basis: the act of slaughter is physically performed correctly.
2
Present the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof is that Allah calls it 'qatl' (killing) in the Quran, not 'dhabh' (slaughter).
Quran 5:95: 'O you who believe, do not kill game while you are in ihram.'
3
Explain wajh al-dalalah
The word 'qatl' signifies taking life without proper tadhkiyah. Therefore the act is not tadhkiyah at all, so it cannot produce halal meat.
This is a direct linguistic inference from the Quran.
4
Address the Shafi'i counter-argument
The Shafi'i says tadhkiyah is present in form. The Hanafi respond that the prohibition changes the nature of the act; it is not valid tadhkiyah.
The Hanafi position is that the act is invalid ab initio.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو ذبح محرم صيدا حرُمَ، وغرمَ بأكله، لا محرم آخر. ولو ذبح محرم صيداً: أي وكذا لو ذبحه الحلال في الحرم حرم أكله على الذابح وعلى غيره، وذبيحته ميتة كذبيحة المجوسي، وقال الشافعي لا يحل للمحرم القاتل ويحل لغيره؛ لأن الذكاة موجودة حقيقة فتعمل عملها على الذابح؛ لارتكابه النهي فيبقى في حق غيره من المحرمين أو في غيرهم، بل في حق نفسه بعد التحلل على الأصل، ولنا أنه تعالى سماه قتلاً، فدل على أنه ليس بذكاة. غير أنه حرم أكله وذبيحته ميتة سواء أكله محرم أو لا . (ط) وغرم بأكله : [ أي لو أكل المحرم الذابح من لحم الذي ذبحه ضمن قيمة ما أكل. (ع)] هذا عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا : لا يضمن الذابح أيضاً بأكله؛ لأنه ميتة، وتناول الميتة يوجب إلا الاستغفار وله أنه حرام عليه ؛ لكونه محظور إحرامه لا لكونه ميتة بخلاف محرم آخر، فإن حرمة تناوله كونه ميتة لا إحرامه؛ ولهذا لا يجوز للحلال أكله والحاصل أن حرمته على الذابح من وجهين: كونه ميتة وتناوله محظور إحرامه فأضيفت حرمة التناول إلى إحرامه، فوجب عليه قيمة ما أكل، وأما المحرم الآخر، فالحرمة عليه من جهة واحدة وهي كونه ميتة فيه فلم يتناول محظور إحرامه، ولا شيء بأكل الميتة سوى التوبة والاستغفار. (عيني، فتح)
If a muhrim slaughters game, it is prohibited, and he is liable for what he eats, not another muhrim. And if a muhrim slaughters game: meaning, similarly if a non-muhrim slaughters it in the Haram, its consumption is prohibited for the slaughterer and others, and his slaughtered animal is carrion like the slaughter of a Magian. Al-Shafi'i said: It is not permissible for the muhrim who killed it but permissible for others, because effective slaughter exists in reality so it operates on the slaughterer due to his commission of the prohibition, so it remains in effect for others among the muhrim or others, even for himself after leaving ihram according to the principle. And for us (Hanafis): Allah Most High called it killing, indicating that it is not valid slaughter. However, its consumption is prohibited and its slaughtered animal is carrion whether a muhrim eats it or not. (T) And he is liable for his eating: meaning if the muhrim slaughterer eats from the meat he slaughtered, he must pay the value of what he ate. This is according to Abu Hanifah. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: The slaughterer is not liable for his eating either, because it is carrion, and consuming carrion only requires seeking forgiveness. And for him (Abu Hanifah): It is prohibited for him because it is a restriction of his ihram, not because it is carrion, unlike another muhrim, for whom the prohibition of consumption is because it is carrion, not his ihram. Hence, a non-muhrim is not permitted to eat it. The conclusion: Its prohibition on the slaughterer is from two aspects: being carrion and its consumption being a prohibited act of his ihram, so the prohibition of consumption is attributed to his ihram, thus he must pay the value of what he ate. As for another muhrim, the prohibition upon him is from one aspect alone—it being carrion—so he has not consumed a prohibited act of his ihram, and there is nothing for eating carrion except repentance and seeking forgiveness. (Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling that a muhrim's slaughter of game is invalid and the meat is carrion. It includes a dispute with al-Shafi'i, who holds the slaughter valid for others. The Hanafi proof is that Allah calls it 'qatl' (killing), not tadhkiyah. An intra-Hanafi disagreement is discussed: Abu Hanifah requires the muhrim to pay for any meat he eats, while the Sahibayn do not. The commentary explains the reasoning—the prohibition for the slaughterer has two aspects (carrion and ihram violation), so liability arises; for another muhrim, only the carrion aspect applies, so no liability.

Key Terms
قتل (qatl): Killing; taking life without proper tadhkiyah.
ذكاة (tadhkiyah): Islamic ritual slaughter that renders meat halal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary Hanafi textual evidence that a muhrim's slaughter of game is invalid?
A) A hadith prohibiting hunting in ihram.
B) The Quran's use of the word 'qatl' instead of 'dhabh'.
C) Consensus of the Companions.
D) Analogy to slaughtering a domesticated animal in the Haram.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses the Quranic word 'qatl' to prove that a muhrim's slaughter is inherently invalid.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Liability for Muhrim Eating His Own Game
Intra-Hanafi dispute on liability for eating game

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn on liability for a muhrim who eats from his own game slaughter, and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifah holds liability for the muhrim slaughterer; the Sahibayn do not; the relied-upon view is Abu Hanifah's.

While the Hanafi school agrees that a muhrim's slaughter is invalid, there is a difference of opinion on whether the muhrim must pay compensation if he eats the meat. Abu Hanifah says yes, because the prohibition has two aspects; the two disciples say no, because the meat is merely carrion. This lesson explores that nuanced debate.

Guided Path
1
State the disagreement
Abu Hanifah says the muhrim must pay the value of what he ate. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say he only repents, no payment.
Both agree the slaughter is invalid and the meat is carrion.
2
Understand Abu Hanifah's proof
For the muhrim slaughterer, the prohibition is twofold: the meat is carrion AND eating it is a violation of his ihram. Therefore he must pay for violating ihram.
The ihram violation triggers a compensation akin to fidyah.
3
Understand the Sahibayn's proof
They argue that the meat is simply carrion, and eating carrion does not require payment—only repentance.
They do not see the additional ihram dimension.
4
Identify the tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is Abu Hanifah's, as supported by later scholars like al-Marghinani.
This is the view given in al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

غرم (ghurm): Liability to pay compensation (value of the meat consumed).

Permissibility of Muhrim Eating Game Caught by a Halal
Ruling on a muhrim eating game caught by a halal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a muhrim eating game caught by a non-muhrim and explain the condition that the muhrim must not have indicated or ordered the hunt.

Core Idea
The muhrim may eat game caught by a halal unless he indicated or ordered the hunt.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario during Hajj: can a person in ihram eat game that a non-muhrim has hunted? The Hanafi school permits it under strict conditions, while other schools disagree. We'll examine the proofs and the practical difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? What is the hukm (permissible/prohibited) in the Hanafi school?
The act is a muhrim eating game caught by a halal (non-muhrim).
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the Hanafi school cite? Look at the incident of Abu Qatada.
The proof is from the Sunnah (hadith).
3
Note the ikhtilaf
Which schools disagree and what is their proof?
Malik and al-Shafi'i prohibit if hunted for the muhrim, citing a hadith.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
How do Hanafis respond to the opposing hadith? They deem it weak or interpret it narrowly.
The response involves both criticism of authenticity and restricted interpretation.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference in rulings between the schools?
In a scenario where a non-muhrim hunts for a muhrim without any indication, Hanafis permit, Shafi'is prohibit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحل له أي حل للمحرم لحم ما صاده حلال من أرض الحل وذبحه في الحل؛ لأن ما ذبحه الحلال في الحرم محرم وميتة، سواء كان صاد لأجله أو لا، بشرط أن لا يكون دلالة المحرم عليه ولا أمره بصيده، وقال مالك: إن اصطاده الحلال لأجل المحرم لا يحل لأن يتناوله وبه قال الشافعي؛ لقوله علية : "الصيد حلال لكم ما لم تصيدوه أو يصاد لكم"، رواه أبو داود ولنا أن أبا قتادة الله لم يصد حمار الوحش لنفسه خاصة، بل له ولأصحابه، وهم محرمون فأباحه لهم عليها و لم يحرمه بإرادته أن يكون لهم، وما روياه ضعيف ولئن صح يحمل على ما إذا صيد له بأمره، وإنما قيد الحل بعدم الدلالة والأمر؛ لأنه لو دل أو أمر لا يحل وعليه الجزاء وكما يجب الجزاء بالدلالة فكذا بالإشارة بشرط أن لا يكون للقاتل علم بالصيد قبل الدلالة أو الإشارة (عيني، فتح) وذبحه: سواء اصطاده لأجله أولا . (ط)
And it is permissible for him: meaning, it is permissible for the muhrim the meat which a non-muhrim hunted from the non-sanctuary land and slaughtered in the non-sanctuary; because what a non-muhrim slaughters in the Haram is prohibited and carrion, whether he hunted it for his sake or not, on condition that the muhrim did not indicate it nor order him to hunt it. And Malik said: If a non-muhrim hunts it for the sake of the muhrim, it is not permissible for him to eat it, and al-Shafi'i said likewise, due to his (saw) statement: "Game is lawful for you as long as you have not hunted it or it has not been hunted for you." Reported by Abu Dawud. And for us (Hanafis): Abu Qatada (ra) did not hunt the wild donkey for himself alone, but for himself and his companions, and they were muhrim, and the Prophet (saw) permitted it to them and did not prohibit it due to his intension that it be for them. And what they narrated is weak, and if authentic, it is interpreted as the case when it is hunted by his order. And the permissibility is conditioned on the absence of indication and order; because if he indicated or ordered, it is not permissible and he is liable for the penalty. And just as the penalty is obligatory by indication, so also by a sign, on condition that the killer did not have knowledge of the game before the indication or sign. (Ayni, Fath) And his slaughter: whether he hunted it for his sake or not. (T)
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage deals with the permissibility for a muhrim to eat game that was hunted and slaughtered by a non-muhrim (halal) from outside the Haram. The ruling is that it is permissible provided the muhrim did not indicate the game or order its hunt. The text presents the opposing views of Malik and al-Shafi'i, who hold it impermissible if the game was hunted specifically for the muhrim. The Hanafi proof is the incident of Abu Qatada, who hunted a wild donkey while his companions were in ihram, and the Prophet permitted them to eat it. The Hanafis respond that the hadith cited by the opponents is weak, and if authentic, it refers to when the game is hunted by the muhrim's direct order. The condition of no indication or order is emphasized because if the muhrim indicates or orders, the game becomes prohibited and he must pay a penalty.

Key Terms
دلالة (dalalah): Indication or pointing out game to a non-muhrim, which if done by a muhrim, makes the game prohibited for him.
محرم (muhrim): A person in the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah.
حلال (halal): A person not in ihram; a non-muhrim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under which condition is it permissible for a muhrim to eat game hunted by a non-muhrim according to the Hanafi school?
A) If the game was hunted specifically for the muhrim.
B) If the muhrim did not indicate or order the hunt.
C) If the game was hunted inside the Haram.
D) If the muhrim is a scholar.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits a muhrim to eat game caught by a non-muhrim provided the muhrim did not indicate or order the hunt.

Penalty for Killing Game in the Haram by a Non-Muhrim
Ruling with proof on penalty for killing Haram game

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on killing game in the Haram by a non-muhrim, distinguish it from the muhrim's case, and evaluate the objections raised by al-Shafi'i and Zafar.

Core Idea
The non-muhrim pays the value; fasting is invalid because the obligation is a guarantee (daman), not expiation (kaffarah).

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq rules on a non-muhrim (halal) who kills game in the Haram. It clarifies that the penalty is the value of the game given as charity, not fasting. The text also addresses a dispute with al-Shafi'i (who analogizes to a muhrim's kaffarah) and an intra-Hanafi dissent from Zafar (who permits fasting). The relied-upon Hanafi position is that only monetary compensation suffices, with fasting being invalid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Pinpoint the exact act: a non-muhrim (halal) kills game within the Haram (sanctuary of Makkah). The ruling is that he must pay the value of the game as charity to the poor.
Note the qualification 'halal'—this distinguishes from a muhrim who kills game.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith: 'لا ينفر صيدها' (Do not chase its game). This hadith indicates the sanctity of the Haram's game and prohibits chasing, which by implication prohibits killing.
The hadith is about the Haram of Makkah; it does not directly state killing, but the prohibition of chasing implies it.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The prohibition of chasing (and thus killing) establishes that the game has sanctity (hurma) due to the Haram. Taking this life requires compensation (daman) because the game is treated as property that has value, even though it is not owned before being secured (ihraz).
The Hanafi position is that the obligation is a guarantee (daman) for the thing, not expiation (kaffarah) for the act.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Al-Shafi'i holds that the penalty is kaffarah (expiation) analogous to a muhrim's case, allowing fasting. Zafar (within Hanafi) also permits fasting, arguing the obligation is a penalty for injury, not a substitute for the thing.
The Hanafi response distinguishes: for a muhrim, the prohibition is due to his state (ihram), so it is kaffarah; for a non-muhrim, the prohibition is due to the location (Haram), so it is daman.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah) is that fasting does not suffice, and slaughter of an equivalent animal suffices if its value as slaughtered equals the value of the killed game. This is because the obligation is compensation for the thing lost.
The text also mentions a dispute about slaughter: some require the value to be equal when slaughtered, but in Zahir al-Riwayah, slaughter suffices generally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و بذبح الحلال أي يجب بذبح الحلال صيد الحرم قيمة ذلك الصيد؛ لأن الصيد استحق الأمن بسبب الحرم؛ لقوله عليه: "لا ينفر صيدها"، فاستفيد منه بطريق الدلالة حرمة القتل، فتجب القيمة وعليه انعقد الإجماع. وقوله: " يتصدق بها أي على الفقراء سوى الأصول والفروع، ولا يشترط الإسلام ويجزئه الإطعام في صيد الحرم، وقيد بالحلال؛ لأن المحرم إذا قتل صيد الحرم يلزمه كفارة واحدة لأجل الإحرام لا لأجل الحرم؛ لأن معنى تفويت الأمن إذا اعتبر مرة لإيجاب الضمان لا يمكن اعتباره ثانياً بسبب الحرم، واعتبار الإحرام أولى؛ لما فيه معنى الجزاء، وقال الشافعي: يكفر قياساً على قتل المحرم، وفي جواز الهدي روايتان عن أصحابنا. (فتح، مستخلص، عيني)
يتصدق بها، ولا صوم. ومن دخل الحرم بصيد أرسله، فإن باعه ردّ البيع إن بقي، وإن فات فعليه الجزاء. ومن أحرم و في بيته أو قفصه صيد لا يرسله، ولو أخذ حلال صيدا يتصدق بقيمته والحال أنه ولا صوم [ أي لا يجزيه صوم في هذه المسألة أي لا يجوز الصوم؛ لأن الواجب هو الضمان بالقتل وليس بكفارة، والصوم لا يصلح ضماناً، وقال زفر : يجوز فيه الصوم؛ لأن وجوب الجزاء إنما كان لاعتبار الجناية على الصيد لا بدلا عن المتلف؛ لأن الصيد قبل الإحراز لا قيمة له؛ لأنه مباح والمباح لا يتقوم إلا بالإحراز، فإذا وجب باعتبار الجناية كان كفارة كالمحرم فيجزئه الصوم رمز الحقائق (۱۷۹/۱] قلنا: إن الحرمة في المحرم باعتبار معنى فيه وهو إحرامه فيكون جزاء الفعل وهو الكفارة، والحرمة في صيد الحرم باعتبار معنى في الصيد، فصار بدل المحل، والصوم يصلح جزاء الأفعال لا ضمان المحال. واختلفوا في الذبح، فقيل: لا يجزئه الذبح إلا أن تكون قيمته مذبوحاً مثل قيمة الصيد المقتول فيجزئه عن الإطعام وفي ظاهر الرواية يجزئه؛ لأنه فعل مثل ما جنى. (فتح)
By the slaughter of a non-muhrim: meaning, by the slaughter of a non-muhrim of the game of the Haram, its value is obligatory; because the game earned sanctity due to the Haram; due to his (saw) statement: "Do not chase its game." So from it by way of indication is derived the prohibition of killing, so its value is obligatory, and upon this consensus was formed. And his statement: "He gives charity with it" meaning, to the poor, excluding ancestors and offspring, and Islam is not a condition, and feeding suffices in the game of the Haram. And it is restricted to the non-muhrim because if a muhrim kills game of the Haram, one expiation is due for his ihram, not for the Haram; because the concept of losing sanctity, if considered once for liability, cannot be considered a second time due to the Haram, and considering ihram is prioritised because it contains the meaning of penalty. And al-Shafi'i said: He must perform expiation (kaffarah) by analogy to killing by a muhrim. And there are two narrations from our companions concerning the permissibility of a sacrificial animal. (Fath, Mustakhlas, Ayni)
He gives charity with it, and no fasting. And whoever enters the Haram with game must release it; if he sells it, the sale is rejected if the game remains, and if it is lost, then he is liable for the penalty. And whoever enters ihram and there is game in his house or cage, he does not have to release it. And if a non-muhrim takes game, he gives charity with its value, and it is the case that there is no fasting [meaning, fasting does not suffice in this matter, i.e., fasting is not permissible because the obligation is liability for killing, not expiation, and fasting is not valid as liability. And Zafar said: Fasting is permissible in it, because the obligation of the penalty was only due to considering the injury upon the game, not as a substitute for the destroyed thing; because game before being secured has no value, since it is permissible and the permissible is not measured except by securing. So when it becomes obligatory due to injury, it is expiation like the muhrim, so fasting suffices. (Ramz al-Haqaiq 1/179). We (Hanafis) say: The prohibition in the muhrim is due to a meaning in him, which is his ihram, so it is a penalty for the act, which is expiation. And the prohibition in the game of the Haram is due to a meaning in the game, so it becomes a substitute for the thing. And fasting is suitable as a penalty for acts, not for liability for things. And they differed about slaughter: it is said that slaughter does not suffice unless its value as slaughtered is like the value of the killed game, then it suffices for feeding. And in Zahir al-Riwayah, it suffices, because he did the like of what he perpetrated. (Fath)
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on a non-muhrim (halal) who kills game in the Haram (sanctuary). He must pay the value of the game and give it as charity to the poor. Fasting is not an option, unlike the case of a muhrim who kills game (where kaffarah can be fasting). The text explains that for a non-muhrim, the obligation is based on the sanctity of the Haram, not on ihram, so it is a compensation for the loss of property, not a kaffarah for sin. The text also addresses a dispute with al-Shafi'i, who analogizes it to a muhrim's kaffarah. The Hanafi response distinguishes between the two: a muhrim's prohibition is due to his state, so the penalty is a kaffarah; a non-muhrim's prohibition is due to the location, so it is a guarantee (daman). The text includes a minority view from Zafar that fasting is valid, but the relied-upon view prohibits it. On the issue of slaughter (dhabh), the dominant view in Zahir al-Riwayah is that slaughtering an animal of equivalent value suffices as charity.

Key Terms
جزاء (jaza'): Penalty or compensation, here specifically the value of the game given in charity.
حلال (halal): A non-muhrim, i.e., a person not in the state of ihram.
ضمان (daman): Guarantee or liability; here, the obligation to compensate for the lost game.
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation, a penalty for violating a prohibition during ihram, which can include fasting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the primary penalty for a non-muhrim who kills game in the Haram?
A) Fasting for three days.
B) Paying the value of the game as charity.
C) Slaughtering a sheep and distributing the meat.
D) Both fasting and charity.

Key Takeaway
For a non-muhrim killing game in the Haram, the penalty is a guarantee (daman) of the game's value, not a kaffarah, so fasting is invalid; slaughter of an equivalent animal suffices per Zahir al-Riwayah.

Ruling on Game Brought into the Haram: Obligation to Release and Prohibition of Sale
Ruling on releasing game and invalidating its sale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on releasing game brought into the Haram, apply the condition that distinguishes wajib from not wajib, and evaluate the inter-madhhab dispute over the obligation.

Core Idea
Game brought into the Haram gains sanctity and must be released, but the owner retains ownership.

When a non-muhrim enters the Haram with game, the game acquires a sacred status. The Hanafi school holds that it must be released, but the owner does not lose ownership. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the Quranic proof, the dispute with the Shafi‘i and Maliki schools, and the intra-Hanafi difference regarding sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is bringing game into the Haram while not in ihram. The ruling is that releasing the game (irsal) is wajib.
If the game is in one's luggage or cage, release is not obligatory.
2
Locate the dalil
The Quranic verse 3:97: 'And whoever enters it is secure.' This establishes sanctity for all that enters the Haram.
The dalil is qat‘i al-thubut but zanni al-dalala in this context.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The verse implies that game entering the Haram becomes secure from disturbance, thus it must be released.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Al-Shafi‘i and Malik hold that release is not obligatory because legal rights do not supersede personal ownership without clear evidence.
The Hanafi response: the game becomes part of the Haram's protected fauna.
5
Analyze the sale ruling
Selling such game is batil (void) because the game cannot be owned once brought into the Haram. If the game perishes, the seller must pay compensation.
Intra-Hanafi: Abu Hanifah permits sale if the game is outside the Haram even if both parties are inside; Muhammad prohibits it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحرم بصيد : أي من دخل الحرم بصيد وهو حلال؛ لأن المحرم يجب عليه الإرسال في الحال، ولا يتوقف وجوبه على دخول الحرم. وقوله: "أرسله ليس المراد من الإرسال تسييبه؛ لأن تسييب الدابة حرام بل يطلقه على وجه لا يضيع، ولا يخرج عن ملكه بهذا الإرسال حتى لو خرج إلى الحل فله أن يمسكه، ولو أخذه إنسان يسترده، وأطلق في الصيد] فشمل ما إذا كان من الجوارح، فلو دخل الحرم ومعه باز فأرسله فقتل حماماً من الحرم لا شيء عليه، وعند الشافعي: ليس عليه إرسال وهو قول مالك؛ لأن حق الشرع لا يظهر في مملوك العبد لحاجة العبد، ولنا: أنه بدخول الحرم صار من صيد الحرم، فصار كما لو دخل بنفسه فلا يجوز التعرض له، ولأنه بدخول الحرم استحق الأمن؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَنْ دَخَلَهُ كَانَ آمِناً (آل عمران: ۹۷)، وهذا إذا كان الصيد في يده حقيقة، وإن كان في رحله أو قفصه لا يجب إرساله. (فتح، مستخلص) فإن باعه أي الحلال أو الحرام وقد أخذه حلالاً حتى لو كان حراما وقت الأخذ لا يملكه بالأخذ فيكون بيعه باطلا لا فاسدا و قوله: "رد" البيع أي يجب رد بيعه إن كان الصيد باقيا؛ لأن البيع فاسد لمكان النهي، ولا فرق بين ما باعه في الحرم أو بعد ما أخرجه؛ لأنه صار بالإدخال من صيد الحرم، فلا يحل إخراجه بعد ذلك، ولو تبايع الحلالان وهما في الحرم، والصيد في الحل، جاز عند أبي حنيفة، وقال محمد: لا يجوز؛ لأنه ممنوع عن التعرض له بالرمي، فكذا بالبيع؛ ولأنه ليس بمتعرض له حساً. وقوله: "وإن فات" عبر بالفوات ليشمل ما لو كان بالهلاك أو بغيبة المشتري، ووجوب الجزاء في هذه الصورة؛ لأن رد البيع تعذر بالموت فنزل منزلة الإتلاف. (فتح، مستخلص)
Entering the Haram with game: meaning, whoever enters the Haram with game while he is non-muhrim; because the muhrim is obligated to release it immediately, and its obligation does not depend on entering the Haram. And his words: "He releases it" does not mean releasing it freely, because letting an animal loose freely is forbidden, rather he releases it in a way that it does not get lost, and it does not leave his ownership by this release, to the extent that if it goes out to the non-sanctuary, he may catch it, and if someone takes it, he may reclaim it. And the expression [is general] so it includes if it is a bird of prey; so if he enters the Haram with a falcon and releases it, and it kills a pigeon of the Haram, he is not liable for anything. And according to al-Shafi'i: he is not obliged to release it, and this is also the view of Malik, because legal rights do not appear in the owned property of the servant due to his need. And for us (Hanafis): by entering the Haram, it becomes part of the game of the Haram, so it is as if it entered by itself, thus it is not permissible to interfere with it, and because by entering the Haram it earned sanctity; due to Allah's statement: "And whoever enters it is secure" (Aal-e-Imran: 97). And this is the case if the game is actually in his hand. If it is in his luggage or cage, he is not obliged to release it. (Fath, Mustakhlas) Then, if he sells it, i.e., the game, whether the seller is halal or muhrim, and he took it as a halal person; even if he took it as a muhrim, he does not own it by taking, so his sale is void (batil), not merely invalid (fasid). And his words: "the sale is rejected" meaning its sale must be rejected if the game remains, because the sale is invalid due to the prohibition. There is no difference between selling it in the Haram or after taking it out, because by bringing it in it became part of the game of the Haram, so it is not permissible to take it out after that. And if two halal persons trade while they are in the Haram and the game is in the non-sanctuary, it is permissible according to Abu Hanifah, but Muhammad said it is not permissible, because one is prohibited from approaching it with the intention of hunting, and likewise by sale, and because it is not actually approaching it. And his words: "And if it is lost" he used the term 'lost' to include whether it is by death or by the absence of the buyer. And the obligation of the penalty in this case is because the rejection of the sale became impossible due to death, so it is treated as destruction. (Fath, Mustakhlas)
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage addresses the obligation to release game that one brings into the Haram if one is a non-muhrim. The ruling is: the game must be released, but the owner retains ownership; if it leaves the Haram, he may recapture it, and if someone else takes it, he may reclaim it. The text includes a dispute with al-Shafi'i and Malik, who do not obligate release. The Hanafi proof is that the game gains sanctity by entering the Haram (Quran 3:97). A conditional exception: if the game is in the traveler's luggage or cage, release is not obligatory. The passage then covers the sale of such game: the sale is void (batil), not merely invalid (fasid), because the game cannot be owned once in the Haram. If the game is destroyed, the seller must pay compensation. An intra-Hanafi dispute is noted: Abu Hanifah permits sale of game located in the non-sanctuary even if both parties are in the Haram, while Muhammad prohibits it.

Key Terms
إرسال (irsal): Releasing the game in a controlled manner that does not risk loss; the owner retains ownership.
بيع فاسد (bay' fasid): An invalid sale (fasid), which if possession is taken, must be rescinded. Here it is actually batil (void) because the object is not owned.
تسييب (tasyib): Releasing an animal freely without restriction; prohibited in the Haram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a non-muhrim enters the Haram with game in his hand, what must he do?
A) Release it but keep ownership.
B) Sell it immediately.
C) Keep it and not release.
D) Slaughter it and give charity.

Key Takeaway
Game brought into the Haram becomes protected; it must be released but remains owned; its sale is void.

Ruling on Releasing Game While in Ihram
Ruling on a muhrim not required to release game already in his home or cage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a muhrim is not required to release game already in his home or cage, and explain the proof from tacit consensus (ijma' fi'li) in contrast to the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
A muhrim is not required to release game already in his possession — the Companions' practice establishes tacit consensus.

Many assume that entering ihram requires freeing any game in one's home or cage. The Hanafi school, however, holds that this is not required. This ruling is based on the unbroken practice of the Companions, who kept domestic fowl while in ihram without being told to release them. In this lesson, we will examine the proof and address the opposing view of Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act under discussion? The act is a muhrim retaining possession of game (e.g., domestic fowl or caged game) that was already in his home or cage at the time of entering ihram. The Hanafi ruling: it is not obligatory to release it.
The term 'game' here includes animals that are lawful to hunt but are already in one's possession.
2
State the Hanafi position clearly
The Hanafi position (zahir al-riwayah) is that the muhrim is absolutely not required to release the game, whether it is in his hand, his luggage, or his cage. This applies equally to domestic fowl and other game kept in enclosures.
No intra-Hanafi disagreement on this point; all three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) agree.
3
Present the opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the muhrim must release such game. His argument: by keeping the game in his possession, the muhrim is 'interfering' with it, which is prohibited during ihram. Just as he must release game caught in his hand, he must release that in his home.
This is an inter-madhhab dispute; the practical difference is whether the muhrim is obliged to open the cage.
4
Analyze the Hanafi proof (dalil)
The Hanafi proof is tacit consensus (ijma' fi'li): the Companions would enter ihram while having domestic fowl (duwajin) in their homes, and it is not reported that they were required to release them. This practice has continued uninterrupted among Muslims to this day, establishing permissibility.
Ijma' fi'li is a valid source of law for Hanafis; it is based on continuous action without verbal opposition.
5
Understand the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical outcome) is clear: a Hanafi muhrim may keep his caged birds or domestic fowl, while a Shafi'i muhrim would be obliged to release them. The Hanafi position avoids unnecessary hardship.
This ruling only applies to game already in one's possession; it does not permit actively hunting or acquiring new game.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا يرسله [ أي لا يلزمه ذلك سواء كان في يده أو في رحله في الأصح. (ط) أي لو كان في قفصه صيد لا يلزمه مطلقاً، سواء كان في يده أو رحله وقال الشافعي يلزمه إرساله؛ لأنه متعرض للصيد بإمساكه في ملكه، وذلك حرام بإحرامه ووجب تركه بإرساله كما إذا كان في يده ولنا أن الصحابة كانوا يحرمون وفي بيوتهم دواجن أي غير السوائم، و لم ينقل أنهم أو جبوا إرسالها ، وبذلك جرت أفعال الأمة إلى يومنا هذا، فصار إجماعا فعلا؛ إرساله
، ولو أخذ حلال صيدا أي الصيد أي البائع وهو الضمان يتصدق بقيمته والحال أنه ولا صوم [ أي لا يجزيه صوم في هذه المسألة أي لا يجوز الصوم؛ لأن الواجب هو الضمان بالقتل وليس بكفارة، والصوم لا يصلح ضماناً، وقال زفر : يجوز فيه الصوم؛ لأن وجوب الجزاء إنما كان لاعتبار الجناية على الصيد لا بدلا عن المتلف؛ لأن الصيد قبل الإحراز لا قيمة له؛ لأنه مباح والمباح لا يتقوم إلا بالإحراز، فإذا وجب باعتبار الجناية كان كفارة كالمحرم فيجزئه الصوم رمز الحقائق (۱۷۹/۱] قلنا: إن الحرمة في المحرم باعتبار معنى فيه وهو إحرامه فيكون جزاء الفعل وهو الكفارة، والحرمة في صيد الحرم باعتبار معنى في الصيد، فصار بدل المحل، والصوم يصلح جزاء الأفعال لا ضمان المحال. واختلفوا في الذبح، فقيل: لا يجزئه الذبح إلا أن تكون قيمته مذبوحاً مثل قيمة الصيد المقتول فيجزئه عن الإطعام وفي ظاهر الرواية يجزئه؛ لأنه فعل مثل ما جنى. (فتح)
He does not release it [meaning, it is not incumbent upon him, whether it is in his hand or in his luggage, according to the most correct view. (T) Meaning, if there is game in his cage, he is absolutely not obliged, whether it is in his hand or his luggage. And al-Shafi'i said: He is obliged to release it, because he is interfering with the game by keeping it in his possession, and that is prohibited in his ihram, and he must leave it by releasing it, just as if it were in his hand. And for us (Hanafis): the companions used to enter ihram while they had domestic fowl (i.e., non-pasturing animals) in their homes, and it is not reported that they obliged their release, and the actions of the community have continued thus until today, so it has become a tacit consensus (ijma' fi'li). And if a non-muhrim takes game, meaning the game, i.e., the seller, and it is the guarantee, he gives charity with its value, and it is the case that there is no fasting [meaning, fasting does not suffice in this matter, i.e., fasting is not permissible because the obligation is liability for killing, not expiation, and fasting is not valid as liability. And Zafar said: Fasting is permissible in it, because the obligation of the penalty was only due to considering the injury upon the game, not as a substitute for the destroyed thing; because game before being secured has no value, since it is permissible and the permissible is not measured except by securing. So when it becomes obligatory due to injury, it is expiation like the muhrim, so fasting suffices. (Ramz al-Haqaiq 1/179). We (Hanafis) say: The prohibition in the muhrim is due to a meaning in him, which is his ihram, so it is a penalty for the act, which is expiation. And the prohibition in the game of the Haram is due to a meaning in the game, so it becomes a substitute for the thing. And fasting is suitable as a penalty for acts, not for liability for things. And they differed about slaughter: it is said that slaughter does not suffice unless its value as slaughtered is like the value of the killed game, then it suffices for feeding. And in Zahir al-Riwayah, it suffices, because he did the like of what he perpetrated. (Fath)
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage addresses two rulings. First, if a person enters ihram and there is game in his home (e.g., domestic fowl) or in a cage, he is not required to release it. The text contrasts the Hanafi view with al-Shafi'i, who would obligate release. The Hanafi proof is the practice of the Companions, who kept domestic animals while in ihram without being told to release them, constituting a tacit consensus. The second ruling concerns a non-muhrim who takes (i.e., kills or seizes) game in the Haram: he must give the value in charity, and fasting is not accepted. This is a repetition from Lesson 3, emphasizing that for a non-muhrim the penalty is a guarantee, not expiation. The passage also addresses an alternative view by Zafar allowing fasting, and a discussion on sacrificing an animal of equivalent value.

Key Terms
سوائم (sawa'im): Pasturing livestock; contrasted with domestic fowl (duwajin) which are kept in homes.
إجماع فعلي (ijma' fi'li): Tacit consensus: continuous practice of the community without verbal consensus.
داجن (ج. دواجن) (dājin (pl. dawājin)): Domestic fowl or tame birds that live in homes, as opposed to wild game.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The Penalty for Killing Game in the Haram: Daman, Not Kaffarah
Ruling on penalty for killing game in Haram with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school treats the penalty for killing game in the Haram as daman (compensation) and state that fasting is not a valid substitute.

Core Idea
The penalty for killing game in the Haram is a guarantee (daman), not an expiation; therefore fasting cannot replace it.

This passage introduces the fundamental ruling that when one kills or wounds game within the sanctuary (Haram), he must give the value in charity, and fasting is not accepted. The commentary then delves into the legal reasoning, distinguishing between compensation for property (daman) and expiation for acts (kaffarah), explaining why the Hanafi school rejects Zufar's view that fasting suffices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling
The text states: 'جزاء قتل الصيد وجرحه يتصدق بها، ولا صوم.' Penalty is charitable giving of value, no fasting.
The ruling is clear: give in charity, do not fast.
2
Distinguish between daman and kaffarah
The commentary explains that the obligation is daman, not kaffarah, because the violation involves the sanctity of a place (the Haram) and the game as property.
Daman is compensation for property; kaffarah is expiation for an act.
3
Analyze Zufar's counterargument
Zufar argues it is kaffarah because the game has no value before acquisition, so the penalty is for the aggression.
His reasoning: the penalty is for the act of aggression, not for the property.
4
Examine the Hanafi response
The Hanafi position differentiates: the muhrim's violation is due to his own state (ihram) so it's kaffarah; the Haram's game violation is due to the game's sanctity, so it's compensation for the property, and fasting cannot compensate for property.
Key: fasting suits acts, not compensating property.
5
Understand the practical implication
Fasting is not valid; only monetary or equivalent compensation (feeding, slaughter) works.
The mufta bihi position is that fasting is not sufficient.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جزاء قتل الصيد وجرحه يتصدق بها، ولا صوم. ومن دخل الحرم بصيد أرسله، فإن باعه ردّ البيع إن بقي، وإن فات فعليه الجزاء. أي بالقيمة على الفقراء أي مع صيد أي الصيد أي الصيد لفساد البيع فات فعليه الجزاء. ومن أحرم و في بيته أو قفصه صيد لا يرسله، ولو أخذ حلال صيدا أي الصيد أي البائع وهو الضمان يتصدق بقيمته والحال أنه ولا صوم [ أي لا يجزيه صوم في هذه المسألة أي لا يجوز الصوم؛ لأن الواجب هو الضمان بالقتل وليس بكفارة، والصوم لا يصلح ضماناً، وقال زفر : يجوز فيه الصوم؛ لأن وجوب الجزاء إنما كان لاعتبار الجناية على الصيد لا بدلا عن المتلف؛ لأن الصيد قبل الإحراز لا قيمة له؛ لأنه مباح والمباح لا يتقوم إلا بالإحراز، فإذا وجب باعتبار الجناية كان كفارة كالمحرم فيجزئه الصوم رمز الحقائق (۱۷۹/۱] قلنا: إن الحرمة في المحرم باعتبار معنى فيه وهو إحرامه فيكون جزاء الفعل وهو الكفارة، والحرمة في صيد الحرم باعتبار معنى في الصيد، فصار بدل المحل، والصوم يصلح جزاء الأفعال لا ضمان المحال. واختلفوا في الذبح، فقيل: لا يجزئه الذبح إلا أن تكون قيمته مذبوحاً مثل قيمة الصيد المقتول فيجزئه عن الإطعام وفي ظاهر الرواية يجزئه؛ لأنه فعل مثل ما جنى. (فتح) الحرم بصيد : أي من دخل الحرم بصيد وهو حلال؛ لأن المحرم يجب عليه الإرسال في الحال، ولا يتوقف وجوبه على دخول الحرم. وقوله: "أرسله ليس المراد من الإرسال تسييبه؛ لأن تسييب الدابة حرام بل يطلقه على وجه لا يضيع، ولا يخرج عن ملكه بهذا الإرسال حتى لو خرج إلى الحل فله أن يمسكه، ولو أخذه إنسان يسترده، وأطلق في الصيد] فشمل ما إذا كان من الجوارح، فلو دخل الحرم ومعه باز فأرسله فقتل حماماً من الحرم لا شيء عليه، وعند الشافعي: ليس عليه إرسال وهو قول مالك؛ لأن حق الشرع لا يظهر في مملوك العبد لحاجة العبد، ولنا: أنه بدخول الحرم صار من صيد الحرم، فصار كما لو دخل بنفسه فلا يجوز التعرض له، ولأنه بدخول الحرم استحق الأمن؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَنْ دَخَلَهُ كَانَ آمِنًا﴾ (آل عمران: ۹۷)، وهذا إذا كان الصيد في يده حقيقة، وإن كان في رحله أو قفصه لا يجب إرساله. (فتح، مستخلص) فإن باعه أي الحلال أو الحرام وقد أخذه حلالاً حتى لو كان حراما وقت الأخذ لا يملكه بالأخذ فيكون بيعه باطلا لا فاسدا و قوله: "رد" البيع أي يجب رد بيعه إن كان الصيد باقيا؛ لأن البيع فاسد لمكان النهي، ولا فرق بين ما باعه في الحرم أو بعد ما أخرجه؛ لأنه صار بالإدخال من صيد الحرم، فلا يحل إخراجه بعد ذلك، ولو تبايع الحلالان وهما في الحرم، والصيد في الحل، جاز عند أبي حنيفة، وقال محمد: لا يجوز؛ لأنه ممنوع عن التعرض له بالرمي، فكذا بالبيع؛ ولأنه ليس بمتعرض له حساً. وقوله: "وإن فات" عبر بالفوات ليشمل ما لو كان بالهلاك أو بغيبة المشتري، ووجوب الجزاء في هذه الصورة؛ لأن رد البيع تعذر بالموت فنزل منزلة الإتلاف. (فتح، مستخلص)
The penalty for killing and wounding game: he gives charity with it, and no fasting. And whoever enters the sanctuary with game and releases it, then if he sells it, the sale is revoked if the game remains, and if it perishes, then upon him is the penalty. [Commentary:] Meaning by its value upon the poor, meaning with the game, meaning the game, meaning the game due to the corruption of the sale, if it perishes then upon him is the penalty. And whoever enters into ihram and in his house or his cage is game, he does not release it. And if a non-muhrim takes game, meaning the game, meaning the seller, and he is the guarantor, he gives in charity its value while it is that there is no fasting. [I.e., fasting does not suffice him in this issue, i.e., fasting is not permissible, because the obligation is the guarantee by killing and not an expiation, and fasting does not suffice as a guarantee. And Zufar said: fasting is permissible in it, because the obligation of the penalty is only due to considering the aggression against the game, not as a substitute for the destroyed property, because before acquisition the game has no value, since it is permissible and the permissible is not valued except by acquisition, so when it is obliged due to the aggression, it is an expiation like the muhrim, so fasting suffices him. (Rumuz al-Haqa'iq 1/179) We said: the sanctity in the muhrim is due to a meaning in him, which is his ihram, so it is a penalty for the act, which is the expiation, and the sanctity in the game of the sanctuary is due to a meaning in the game, so it becomes a substitute for the place, and fasting is suitable for penalizing acts, not for guaranteeing places. And they differed regarding slaughter, so it was said: slaughter does not suffice him unless its value slaughtered is like the value of the killed game, then it suffices him for feeding, and in the apparent narration it suffices him, because he did an act similar to what he committed. (Fath) "The sanctuary with game": meaning whoever enters the sanctuary with game while he is non-muhrim, because the muhrim must release it immediately, and its obligation is not dependent on entering the sanctuary. And his saying: "he released it" does not mean setting it free, because setting free an animal is prohibited, but he releases it in a way that it does not get lost, and it does not leave his ownership by this release, such that if it goes out to the non-sanctuary, he may catch it, and if someone takes it, he can reclaim it. And he used the general term "game" to include if it is a bird of prey. So if he enters the sanctuary with a falcon and releases it and it kills a pigeon of the sanctuary, there is nothing upon him. And according to al-Shafi'i: there is no release upon him, and it is the saying of Malik, because the right of the law does not appear in the property of the servant due to the need of the servant. And for us: by entering the sanctuary it becomes part of the game of the sanctuary, so it is as if it entered by itself, so it is not permissible to interfere with it, and because by entering the sanctuary it deserves safety due to His saying: "And whoever enters it is safe" (Al 'Imran 3:97). This is if the game is in his hand actually; if it is in his saddlebag or cage, its release is not obligatory. (Fath, Mustakhlas) "Then if he sells it": meaning the non-muhrim or the muhrim while he took it as non-muhrim, such that if he was muhrim at the time of taking, he does not own it by taking, so his sale is void, not invalid. And his saying: "the sale is revoked" means the sale must be cancelled if the game remains, because the sale is invalid due to the prohibition, and there is no difference whether he sold it in the sanctuary or after taking it out, because by bringing it in it became from the game of the sanctuary, so its removal thereafter is not permissible. If two non-muhrims make a transaction while in the sanctuary and the game is in the non-sanctuary, it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa, and Muhammad said: it is not permissible, because he is prohibited from interfering with it by shooting, so also by sale, and because it is not sensory interference. And his saying: "and if it perishes" he used 'perish' to include if it is by destruction or by the buyer's absence, and the obligation of the penalty in this case because the cancellation of the sale was impossible due to death, so it is treated as destruction. (Fath, Mustakhlas)
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage addresses the penalty for killing or wounding game in the Haram. It begins by stating that one must give in charity the value of the game, and fasting is not acceptable as a penalty. It then discusses the case of a person who enters the Haram with game and releases it; if he later sells it, the sale is invalid if the game still exists, otherwise he owes the penalty. The commentary explains the details. The provision for fasting is debated: Zufar allowed it, but the Hanafi school rejects it because the penalty here is a form of compensation (daman) for the game, not a kaffarah (expiation). The compensation must be monetary or equivalent, and fasting cannot substitute for that because fasting is only valid for expiating acts, not for compensating lost property. The text also discusses slaughtering: the preferred view (zahir al-riwaya) is that slaughtering the animal (as compensation) is valid because it is an act similar to the offense (i.e., killing). Then it explains the meaning of 'release': it does not mean abandoning the animal to perish, but releasing it in a way that it is not lost, and the owner retains ownership. Disagreeing with Shafi'i and Malik, the commentary holds that entering the Haram with game makes it part of the Haram's game, so it must be released. If a person sells it, the sale is invalid, and he must recover it if possible; if not, he owes the penalty.

Key Terms
جزاء (jaza): The penalty or compensation for killing or wounding game in the Haram.
صيد الحرم (sayd al-haram): Game that is within the sanctuary (Haram) of Mecca.
ضمان (daman): Compensation or guarantee for a lost or damaged property.
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation for an act, such as breaking an oath or violating ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, the penalty for killing game in the Haram is considered:
A) Kaffarah
B) Daman
C) Charity
D) Fasting

Key Takeaway
The penalty for killing game in the Haram is compensation for property (daman), not expiation, so fasting does not suffice.

Muhrim Not Required to Release Game in House or Cage
Ruling on a Muhrim who has game in his house or cage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on keeping game in a cage during ihram and explain the proof from the Sahaba's practice as a binding consensus.

Core Idea
A Muhrim may keep game in his cage – the Sahaba's practice forms a binding consensus.

This lesson examines a dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools over whether a Muhrim must release game that is in his house or cage. The key point is whether keeping the game constitutes interference (ta'arruḍ) that must be ended by release. The Hanafi school holds that release is not required, relying on the established practice of the Companions and the continuous practice of the Ummah as a form of practical consensus (ijma' fi'li).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Muhrim is not required to release game that is in his house or cage, whether the game is in his hand or in his saddlebag (according to the most correct view).
This applies to game kept in a confined space like a cage or house, not to game hunted in the wild.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the Muhrim must release the game because keeping it in possession is interference (ta'arruḍ), which is prohibited during ihram.
The Shafi'i school analogizes it to game held in the hand, where release is wajib to remove the prohibition.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Shafi'i: Keeping game in one's possession while in ihram constitutes interference, and the prohibition can only be lifted by release. The same ruling applies whether the game is in hand, cage, or house.
They use qiyas (analogy) to the clear case of game in hand.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is based on the practice of the Companions (Sahaba). They used to enter ihram while having domestic fowl (dawājin) in their homes and did not release them. This practice continued without objection, forming an ijma' fi'li (practical consensus) that overrides the qiyas.
The consensus (ijma') is a stronger source of law than qiyas in Hanafi usul.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Hanafi law, a Muhrim may keep game in his cage or house without any obligation to release it. Under Shafi'i law, he must release it or incur a penalty.
This practical difference affects many pilgrims who own pets or keep animals at home.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا يرسله [ أي لا يلزمه ذلك سواء كان في يده أو في رحله في الأصح. (ط) أي لو كان في قفصه صيد لا يلزمه مطلقاً، سواء كان في يده أو رحله وقال الشافعي يلزمه إرساله؛ لأنه متعرض للصيد بإمساكه في ملكه، وذلك حرام بإحرامه ووجب تركه بإرساله كما إذا كان في يده ولنا أن الصحابة كانوا يحرمون وفي بيوتهم دواجن أي غير السوائم، و لم ينقل أنهم أو جبوا إرسالها ، وبذلك جرت أفعال الأمة إلى يومنا هذا، فصار إجماعا فعلا؛
He does not release it. [Commentary:] Meaning it is not obligatory upon him, whether it is in his hand or in his saddlebag in the most correct view. (T) Meaning if there is game in his cage, it is not obligatory upon him absolutely, whether it is in his hand or his saddlebag. And al-Shafi'i said: It is obligatory upon him to release it, because he is interfering with the game by keeping it in his possession, and that is prohibited by his ihram, and its abandonment is obligatory by release, just as if it were in his hand. And for us: the Companions used to enter ihram while they had domestic fowl (i.e., non-grazing animals) in their houses, and it is not narrated that they obliged their release, and by that the practices of the Ummah have continued until our day, so it became a practical consensus.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage discusses the rule that a Muhrim who has game in his house or cage is not required to release it. The commentary explains that this applies whether the game is in his hand or in his saddlebag, though if it were in his hand, some scholars might argue otherwise. The Shafi'i school holds that the Muhrim must release the game because keeping it constitutes interference. However, the Hanafi school argues based on the practice of the Companions, who had domestic animals in their homes while in ihram and were not required to release them. This continuous practice has become a binding consensus (ijma' fi'li). Therefore, the Hanafi position is that no release is obligatory.

Key Terms
إرسال (irsal): The act of releasing or setting free game.
دواجن (dawajin): Domestic fowl or animals that are not grazing livestock.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling regarding a Muhrim who has game in a cage in his house?
A) He must release it immediately.
B) He is not required to release it.
C) He must slaughter it.
D) He must pay a penalty.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school, relying on the Sahaba's practice and continuous Ummah consensus, rules that a Muhrim need not release game from his cage or house.

Liability for Muhrim's Game When Released or Killed by Another
Cases of liability when a Muhrim's game is released or killed by another person.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability for game in the hands of a Muhrim when it is released or killed by another, and identify the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
A Muhrim does not own game, so releasing it incurs no liability, but killing it by another Muhrim creates joint liability.

This lesson examines several scenarios involving a Muhrim and game. The key principle is that a Muhrim cannot own game due to the Quranic prohibition. Therefore, if a Muhrim takes game, he has no property right, and releasing or killing it by another does not trigger liability for him in the same way as for a non-Muhrim. However, if a non-Muhrim catches game and then becomes Muhrim, a dispute arises about whether a releaser is liable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenarios
List the four scenarios: (1) Halal catches, becomes Muhrim, then another releases. (2) Muhrim catches, another releases. (3) Muhrim catches, another Muhrim kills. (4) Halal kills while Muhrim holds.
2
Determine the ruling for each
For each scenario, state the Hanafi ruling: (1) Abu Hanifa says releaser liable, Sahibayn say no. (2) Consensus: no liability. (3) Both liable, captor can recover. (4) Muhrim liable, recovers from halal killer.
Note the disagreement in scenario 1.
3
Locate the dalil
The Quranic verse 5:96 prohibits hunting for Muhrim, establishing that Muhrim cannot own game. This is used to argue no liability when a Muhrim's game is released.
Zanni dalala because the verse does not directly address liability.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
In scenario 1, Abu Hanifa views the game as owned property before ihram, so releasing is destruction. The Sahibayn view the releaser as a deputy of the law, so no liability.
Thamarah: who pays compensation.
5
Note the recovery rule
If two Muhrims are liable, the captor can recover from the killer if the latter expiates with property, not fasting. Zufar disagrees with recovery entirely.
This shows further intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأحرَم ضمن مرسله، ولا يضمن لو أخذه محرم، فإن قتله محرم آخر ضمنا، ورجع قاتله. آخذه على فإن قطع . أي لو أخذ صيدا ثم أحرم فأرسله من يده غيره. (مسكين) ضمن مرسله عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأنه ملكه بالأخذ وقت كونه حلالاً ملكاً . ولا يبطل احترامه بإحرامه وقد أتلفه المرسل فيضمن قيمته وعندهما لا يضمن؛ لأن المرسل محترماً، آمر بالمعروف ناه عن المنكر فكان نائبا عن الشرع، فصار كما إذا أخذه المحرم حالة الإحرام. (فتح، مستخلص) لو أخذه محرم: أي لو أخذ الصيد محرم، فأرسله آخر من يده، لا يضمن بالإجماع؛ لأن المحرم بالأخذ لم يملكه؛ لأن المحرم لا يملك الصيد بسبب ما؛ إذ هو محرم عليه ؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَحُرِّمَ عَلَيْكُمْ صَيْدُ الْبَرِّ مَا دُمْتُمْ حُرُمان (المائدة: ٩٦)، فصار الصيد في حقه كالخمر والخنزير بخلاف ما إذا أخذه وهو حلال ثم أحرم؛ لأنه ملكه بالأخذ قبل الإحرام، فيكون المرسل متلفاً عليه ملكه. [رمز الحقائق: ۱۸۰/۱] فإن قتله محرم آخر: أي إن أخذ محرم صيداً فقتله محرم آخر ، ضمن كل واحد منهما جزاءاً تاماً بشرط أن يكون القاتل بالغاً مسلماً عاقلاً، فلو صبياً أو مجنوناً فلا ضمان عليه، يعني لا يجب عليه الجزاء، ووجوب الضمان عليهما؛ لوجود الجناية منهما ؛ لأن الآخذ متعرض للصيد بالأخذ والآخر بالقتل، وقيل: لأن الآخذ متعرض للصيد بتفويت الأمن، والقاتل مقرر لذلك، والتقرير كالابتداء في حق التضمين. وقوله: "ورجع آخذه" لأن القاتل قرر عليه ما كان على شرف السقوط، يعني أن الآخذ لو ترك الصيد سقط عنه الجزاء، والقاتل صار متعرضاً لذلك وقرره، وللتقرير حكم الابتداء في التضمين، ثم الرجوع على القاتل إذا كفر بالمال، أما إذا كفر بالصوم لم يرجع؛ لأنه لم يغرم شيئاً، وقال زفر لا يرجع؛ لأن الآخذ مؤاخذ بصنعه فلا يرجع به على غيره؛ لأنه لم يملك الصيد لا قبل الضمان ولا بعده : ولا كانت له فيه يد محترمة، ووجوب الضمان بتفويت يد أو ملك و لم يوجد ولنا أن يده على هذا الصيد كانت معتبرة لتمكنه إرساله وإسقاط الضمان نفسه، والقاتل فوت عليه هذه اليد فيضمن أما لو قتله حلال ضمن عن المحرم فقط، ورجع به على القاتل عندنا خلافاً للشافعي. (فتح، مسكين) ضمنا : أي القاتل والآخذ في حالة الإحرام جميعاً؛ لوجود الجناية منهما . (ع) قاتله: بما ضمن، ولو قتله حلال ضمن المحرم ورجع به على القاتل. (ط) فإن قطع : ليس المقام مقام التفريع؛ لعدم المفرع عليه، فحق الكلام أن يصدر بالواو؛ ولهذا جعل بعضهم الفاء للاستئناف، والمراد بالحشيش ما لا ساق له ولا حاجة إلى التقييد بكونه غير مملوك؛ إذ لا دخل له في وجوب الجزاء على القاطع لوجوب القيمة مع الملك أيضاً، والشجرة التي بعض أصلها في الحرم كالتي جميع أصلها فيه.
Then he enters ihram, then the releaser is liable, and if a muhrim takes it, he is not liable, and if another muhrim kills it, both are liable, and the captor recovers from the killer. [Commentary:] Meaning if he took game then entered ihram and someone else released it from his hand. (Miskin) The releaser is liable according to Abu Hanifa, because he owned it by taking while he was non-muhrim property. His sanctity is not nullified by his ihram, and the releaser destroyed it, so he is liable for its value. According to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], he is not liable, because the releaser is a respectful person, commanding good and forbidding evil, so he is a deputy of the law, thus it becomes as if a muhrim took it in the state of ihram. (Fath, Mustakhlas) If a muhrim takes it: meaning if a muhrim takes game and another releases it from his hand, he is not liable by consensus, because the muhrim by taking did not own it, because the muhrim does not own game by any means, since it is prohibited for him, due to His saying: "And forbidden to you is game of the land as long as you are in ihram" (Al-Ma'idah 5:96), so the game becomes for him like wine and pork, unlike the case where he took it while non-muhrim then entered ihram, because he owned it by taking before ihram, so the releaser destroys his property. (Rumuz al-Haqa'iq 1/180) If another muhrim kills it: meaning if a muhrim takes game and another muhrim kills it, each of them is liable for a complete penalty, on condition that the killer is adult, Muslim, and sane; if a child or insane, there is no liability on him, meaning the penalty is not obligatory on him. And the obligation of liability on both is due to the existence of aggression from both, because the taker interferes with the game by taking and the other by killing. And it is said: because the taker interferes with the game by removing safety, and the killer confirms that, and confirmation is like initiation in terms of liability. And his saying: "and the captor recovers" because the killer confirmed upon him what was on the verge of falling, meaning that if the captor had released the game, the penalty would have fallen from him, and the killer became interfering with that and confirmed it, and confirmation has the ruling of initiation in liability. Then the recovery from the killer if he expiates with property; if he expiates with fasting, he does not recover, because he did not pay anything. And Zufar said: he does not recover, because the captor is held accountable for his own act, so he cannot recover it from another, because he did not own the game before liability nor after it, nor did he have a respected hand over it. And the obligation of liability is due to the loss of a hand or property, and that was not found. And for us: his hand over this game was considered because of his ability to release it and drop the liability himself, and the killer caused him to lose this hand, so he is liable. But if a non-muhrim kills it, the muhrim is liable only, and he recovers from the killer according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i. (Fath, Miskin) "Both are liable" means the killer and the taker in the state of ihram both, due to the existence of aggression from both. (A) "His killer" means by what he is liable. And if a non-muhrim kills it, the muhrim is liable and recovers from the killer. (T) "If he cuts" means this is not a place for branch, because there is no principal; thus the word 'fa' is for resumption. The meaning of hashish is what has no stem, and there is no need to restrict it to being non-owned, since that has no bearing on the obligation of the penalty on the cutter, because the value is obligatory even with ownership. And the tree part of whose root is in the sanctuary is like the tree all of whose root is in it.
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage covers several scenarios regarding a Muhrim and game. First, if a person catches game while halal, then becomes Muhrim, and another person releases the game from his hand, the releaser is liable to pay its value according to Abu Hanifa, but the two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say he is not liable because the releaser is acting as a representative of the law (commanding right and forbidding wrong). Second, if a Muhrim catches game and someone else releases it, there is consensus that no liability arises because the Muhrim does not own the game, citing the Quranic verse (5:96) which forbids hunting for the Muhrim. Third, if a Muhrim catches game and another Muhrim kills it, both are liable for a full penalty each, provided the killer is an adult, sane Muslim. The captor can recover the penalty from the killer if the killer pays with money; if he expiates by fasting, he cannot recover. Zufar disagrees with recovery. Fourth, if a non-Muhrim kills the game while a Muhrim has it, the Muhrim is liable and can recover from the killer, contrary to Shafi'i. Finally, the passage briefly discusses cutting grass (hashish) and trees in the Haram: the penalty is based on value, and even if the tree has only part of its root in the Haram, the same rule applies.

Key Terms
ضمان (daman): Liability or guarantee for the value of the game when it is destroyed or lost.
إتلاف (itlaf): Destruction or causing loss of property.
محرم (muhrim): A person in the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah.
حلال (halal): A person not in ihram; permissible to hunt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where a Muhrim takes game and another Muhrim kills it, what is the Hanafi ruling on recovery?
A) The captor can always recover from the killer.
B) The captor can recover only if the killer expiates with property.
C) The captor cannot recover because he had no valid hand.
D) The killer can recover from the captor.

Key Takeaway
A Muhrim does not own game, so releasing it incurs no liability for the releaser; but if another Muhrim kills it, both are liable, and the captor can recover from the killer if the latter pays compensation in property.

Liability for Game Taken by a Muhrim: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on liability for game taken by a muhrim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi positions on liability for game taken by a muhrim and apply the rule of recourse when another muhrim kills it.

Core Idea
Ownership established while halal is not nullified by ihram; thus the sender who destroys that property is liable.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the liability for game (sayd) that was lawfully taken by a person while halal, but who later enters ihram, and then another person releases or kills the game. The key issue is whether the sender (mursil) is liable for the value of the game or not. The passage also covers the scenario where two muhrims are involved: one takes the game, and another kills it. Understanding the reasoning behind each position strengthens your ability to analyze property rights and liability in sacred contexts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
First, note the two main cases: (1) A halal person takes game, becomes muhrim, then another sends the game away. (2) A muhrim takes game, then another muhrim kills it. Each has its own ruling and dispute.
2
Analyze the first scenario: halal-turns-muhrim with sender
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the sender is liable because the taker owned the game fully while halal, and ihram does not void that ownership. The sender destroyed the property. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree: the sender is a deputy of the Shari'ah (commanding good), so it is as if a muhrim took it, hence no liability.
Focus on the legal reasoning: ownership vs. representation of the Law.
3
Examine the second scenario: both muhrims
When a muhrim takes game and another muhrim kills it, both are liable for a full penalty. The taker can seek recourse (ruju') from the killer if the penalty is paid in wealth. This is because the taker had a protected hand over the game (could have released it to drop liability), and the killer destroyed that hand.
Note the minority view of Zufar who denies recourse.
4
Understand the cross-madhhab difference
The passage ends with a reference to al-Shafi'i: if a halal kills the game, the muhrim alone is liable and cannot seek recourse from the killer. This contrasts with the Hanafi view where the muhrim can seek recourse.
This is a separate ikhtilaf from the main dispute.
5
Synthesize the ruling and its practical application
The mufta bihi position is not explicitly stated, but the text implies that Abu Hanifa's view is stronger because ownership is a fundamental right. In practice, a friend who releases a bird caught by someone who later entered ihram would have to pay compensation according to Abu Hanifa, but not according to the Sahibayn.
Consult later Hanafi fatwa works for the relied-upon view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأحرَم ضمن مرسله، ولا يضمن لو أخذه محرم، فإن قتله محرم آخر ضمنا، ورجع آخذه على قاتله. فإن أخذ صيداً وهو حلال ثم أحرم ثم أرسله من يده غيره ضمن مرسله عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأنه ملكه بالأخذ وقت كونه حلالاً ملكاً تاماً، ولا يبطل احترامه بإحرامه وقد أتلفه المرسل فيضمن قيمته وعندهما لا يضمن؛ لأن المرسل آمر بالمعروف ناه عن المنكر فكان نائبا عن الشرع، فصار كما إذا أخذه المحرم حالة الإحرام. (فتح، مستخلص) لو أخذه محرم: أي لو أخذ الصيد محرم، فأرسله آخر من يده، لا يضمن بالإجماع؛ لأن المحرم بالأخذ لم يملكه؛ لأن المحرم لا يملك الصيد بسبب ما؛ إذ هو محرم عليه ؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَحُرِّمَ عَلَيْكُمْ صَيْدُ الْبَرِّ مَا دُمْتُمْ حُرُمان (المائدة: ٩٦)، فصار الصيد في حقه كالخمر والخنزير بخلاف ما إذا أخذه وهو حلال ثم أحرم؛ لأنه ملكه بالأخذ قبل الإحرام، فيكون المرسل متلفاً عليه ملكه. فإن قتله محرم آخر: أي إن أخذ محرم صيداً فقتله محرم آخر، ضمن كل واحد منهما جزاءاً تاماً بشرط أن يكون القاتل بالغاً مسلماً عاقلاً، فلو صبياً أو مجنوناً فلا ضمان عليه، يعني لا يجب عليه الجزاء، ووجوب الضمان عليهما؛ لوجود الجناية منهما ؛ لأن الآخذ متعرض للصيد بالأخذ والآخر بالقتل، وقيل: لأن الآخذ متعرض للصيد بتفويت الأمن، والقاتل مقرر لذلك، والتقرير كالابتداء في حق التضمين. وقوله: "ورجع آخذه" لأن القاتل قرر عليه ما كان على شرف السقوط، يعني أن الآخذ لو ترك الصيد سقط عنه الجزاء، والقاتل صار متعرضاً لذلك وقرره، وللتقرير حكم الابتداء في التضمين، ثم الرجوع على القاتل إذا كفر بالمال، أما إذا كفر بالصوم لم يرجع؛ لأنه لم يغرم شيئاً، وقال زفر لا يرجع؛ لأن الآخذ مؤاخذ بصنعه فلا يرجع به على غيره؛ لأنه لم يملك الصيد لا قبل الضمان ولا بعده : ولا كانت له فيه يد محترمة، ووجوب الضمان بتفويت يد أو ملك و لم يوجد ولنا أن يده على هذا الصيد كانت معتبرة لتمكنه إرساله وإسقاط الضمان نفسه، والقاتل فوت عليه هذه اليد فيضمن أما لو قتله حلال ضمن عن المحرم فقط، ورجع به على القاتل عندنا خلافاً للشافعي.
If a muhrim takes game, he is liable for its release; but if a muhrim takes it, he is not liable. If another muhrim kills it, both are liable, and the taker can seek recourse from the killer. If a person takes game while halal, then becomes muhrim, and then another person sends it away from his hand, according to Abu Hanifa the sender is liable; because the taker owned it fully by taking it while halal, and his ownership does not become void by his ihram, and the sender has destroyed his property, so he must pay its value. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he is not liable; because the sender is commanding good and forbidding evil, so he is a deputy of the Law, and thus it is as if a muhrim had taken it while in ihram. (Fath, Mustakhlas) If a muhrim takes game: i.e., if a muhrim takes game and another sends it away from his hand, there is no liability by consensus; because the muhrim by taking did not own it; because a muhrim cannot own game by any means, as it is prohibited for him; due to His saying: {And prohibited to you is game of the land as long as you are in ihram} (al-Ma'idah: 96), so game in his regard is like wine and pork, unlike the case where he takes it while halal and then becomes muhrim; because he owned it by taking before ihram, so the sender destroys his property. If another muhrim kills it: i.e., if a muhrim takes game and another muhrim kills it, each of them is liable for a complete penalty, provided that the killer is an adult, Muslim, and sane. If a child or insane, no liability on him, meaning the penalty is not obligatory. Liability is obligatory on both due to the offense from both; because the taker exposes the game by taking, and the other by killing. It is said: because the taker exposes the game by causing loss of security, and the killer confirms it, and confirmation is like initiation in liability. His statement "and the taker seeks recourse" because the killer has confirmed what was on the verge of falling, meaning that if the taker had left the game, liability would have fallen from him, and the killer has exposed himself to that and confirmed it, and confirmation has the ruling of initiation in liability. Then recourse against the killer if he expiates with wealth; if he expiates with fasting, he does not have recourse because he did not pay anything. Zufar said: he does not have recourse because the taker is accountable for his own action, so he cannot seek recourse from others; because he did not own the game neither before liability nor after it, nor did he have a protected hand over it, and liability is due to destroying a hand or property, and none existed. For us: his hand over this game was considered because he was able to release it and drop the liability from himself, and the killer has destroyed this hand, so the killer is liable. As for if a halal kills it, the muhrim is liable and then seeks recourse from the killer according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i.

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, regarding the liability for game taken by a person who later becomes muhrim and then another person releases or kills the game. The passage also covers the case where a muhrim takes game and another muhrim kills it. The commentary explains the reasoning and the positions of each imam. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is not explicitly stated but based on the structure, Abu Hanifa's view is often preferred in such matters of ownership. Key concepts: muhrim (one in ihram), mursal (the sender), liability (daman). The text also includes a minority view of Zufar. The passage ends with a brief cross-madhhab reference to al-Shafi'i.

Key Terms
مُحْرِم (muhrim): A person in the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah, which prohibits certain actions including hunting game.
مُرْسِل (mursil): The person who releases or sends away the game from the hand of the taker.
ضَمِن (damin): Liable for compensation (the value or penalty).
جَزَاء (jaza'): The penalty for killing game while in ihram, which can be offering a similar animal, feeding the poor, or fasting.
آمر بالمعروف (aamir bil ma'ruf): One who commands good; used by Sahibayn to characterize the sender as acting in accordance with Shari'ah.

B) Both are liable, and the taker can seek recourse from the killer.

D) Neither is liable.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, property rights established while halal survive ihram, so a person who destroys such property is liable, but this is disputed by the Sahibayn who prioritize the principle of commanding good.
