Penalty for Cutting Plants of the Haram: Ruling, Exceptions, and Proof
Ruling with proof on cutting plants in the Haram, with exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on cutting fresh plants in the Haram, identify the exceptions (dry plants and idhkhir), and explain the dalil (hadith) and its authoritative weight.

Core Idea
Cutting fresh, uncultivated plants in the Haram is haram and requires compensation; dry plants and idhkhir are excepted.

The sanctity of the Haram extends beyond animals to its vegetation. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling on cutting plants and trees in the Haram, exploring the general prohibition, the exceptions for dry plants and idhkhir, and the textual proof that anchors the ruling. We will also examine an intra-Hanafi dispute raised by Abu Yusuf and why the relied-upon position adheres to the clear hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Read the opening text to determine what act is being ruled upon (cutting herbage/trees) and the initial ruling (prohibition with compensation). Note that the ruling applies to both muhrim and non-muhrim (halal).
The act is cutting fresh, uncultivated plants; the ruling is haram and requires payment of value.
2
Trace the exceptions
Locate the two exceptions: dry plants and idhkhir. Understand the rationale: dryness removes 'growing' status, and idhkhir is explicitly exempted by the Prophet's hadith.
Dry plants are like firewood; idhkhir is a fragrant grass used for roofing and graves.
3
Examine the proof (dalil)
Identify the hadith cited ('la yukhtala khallaha wa la yu'adad shawkaha') and the exception for idhkhir. Note how this hadith is a 'prompted exception' (istithna talqini). Understand the wajh al-dalalah: the imperative prohibition indicates haram, and the exception confirms the specific exemption.
The hadith is a sunnah ahad (zanni al-thubut) but clear in meaning (qati al-dalala).
4
Understand the four-type classification
Read the passage that classifies trees into four types based on whether they are planted by people or grow naturally. Identify which three are permissible to cut without penalty and which one requires compensation.
The fourth type (wild, not commonly planted) is prohibited to cut without penalty, even if it grows in private property.
5
Address the intra-Hanafi dispute
Review Abu Yusuf's opinion allowing grazing due to hardship. Note the refutation: the clear text overrides consideration of hardship, and alternative provision of herbage from outside the Haram is available.
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) follows Abu Hanifa and the majority of the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حشيش الحرم أو شجراً غير مملوك، وهو مما لا ينبته الناس ضمن قيمته إلا فيما جف، وحرم رعي حشيش الحرم وقطعه إلا الإذخر. المراد به ههنا مطلق الكلاً رطبا كان أو يابسا وفي الأصل الحشيش: ما يبس من الكلا. (فتح) ضمن قيمته: سواء كان القاطع محرماً أو حلالاً، ثم إذا أدى القيمة ملكه غير أنه يكره له بيعه والانتفاع به، أما الصيد الذي أدى جزاءه فلا يجوز بيعه؛ لأن الصيد محظور إحرامه بالنص القطعي، وأما شجر الحرم وحشيشه فلا تعلق للإحرام به والقارن في ذلك كالمفرد لا يجب عليه إلا قيمة واحدة والقلع كالقطع، ولا مدخل للصوم في هذه والحاصل أن شجر الحرم وحشيشه أربعة أنواع: ثلاثة منها يحل قطعها والانتفاع بها بلا جزاء، وواحدة منها لا يحل قطعها والانتفاع بها بدون الجزاء، أما الثلاثة الأول : فكل شجر أنبته الناس وهو من جنس ما ينبته الناس، وكل شجر أنبته الناس وهو ليس من جنس ما ينبته الناس وكل شجر نبت بنفسه وهو من جنس ما ينبته الناس وهذه يحل قطعها؛ لأن ما ينبته الناس عادة غير مستحق الأمن بالإجماع، وما لا ينبت عادة إذا أنبته الناس التحق بما ينبت عادةً، وأما الواحدة التي لا يحل قطعها فهي كل شجر نبت بنفسه وهو ليس من جنس ما ينبته الناس ولو نبت بنفسه ما لا ينبت عادة في ملك رجل بأن نبت في ملكه أم غيلان وهو نوع من شجر السواك ينعقد عليه الصمغ العربي، يجب على قاطعه قيمته لمالكه، وقيمته لحق الشرع كما لو قتل صيداً مملوكاً في الحرم. (فتح) إلا فيما جف أي ضمن قيمته إلا في شجر الحرم الذي يبس فإنه لا يضمن ويحل الانتفاع به؛ لأنه حطب وليس بنام ولهذا جاز أخذ الكمأة منه لعدم نموها وثبوت الحرمة بسبب الحرم لما يكون نامياً، والشجر المنكسر کالیابس والمذكور في الكتب أن قطع الكلأ مطلقاً يوجب الجزاء، والفرق بينه وبين الشجر غير ظاهر، ولو جعل الاستثناء من الحشيش والشجر كان مقتضى القياس. (فتح) إلا الإذخر: أي يحرم رعي حشيش الحرم وقطعه إلا الإذخر فإنه يجوز قطعه ورعيه، وهو ما ينبت في السهل والجبل، وله أصل دقيق وقضبان دقاق يطيب ريحه والذي بمكة أجوده يسقفون به البيوت بين الخشبات ويسدون به في القبور الخلل بين اللبنات، والأصل في ذلك أنه عليها لما قال: "لا يختلى خلاها ولا يعضد شوكها"، قال ابن عباس: يا رسول الله ! إلا الإذخر، فإنه لرعي دوابنا وقبورنا، فقال: "إلا الإذخر"، ومثله يسمى بالاستثناء التلقيني، ولهم عطف تلقيني أيضاً، ومنه قالوا: "والمقصرين" الحديث، وقال أبو يوسف: لا بأس برعي الحشيش؛ لمكان الحرج في حق الزائرين والمقيمين والحجة عليه ما روينا والقطع بالمشافر كالقطع بالمناجل، وحمل الحشيش من الحل متيسر فلا حرج ولئن كان فيه حرج فلا يعتبر؛ لأن الحرج إنما يعتبر في موضع لا نص فيه، وأما مع النص بخلافه فلا.
or a tree not owned, and which is not planted by people, he is liable for its value except what is dried. And grazing the herbage of the Haram and cutting it is prohibited except idhkhir. What is meant here is absolute herbage, fresh or dry. In origin, hashish is what is dried of herbage. (Fath) He is liable for its value: whether the cutter is muhrim or halal. Then if he pays the value, he owns it, but it is disliked for him to sell it or benefit from it. As for game for which he paid the penalty, it is not permissible to sell it, because game is prohibited by a definitive text. As for trees and herbage of the Haram, there is no connection with ihram. And the qarin (one performing Hajj and Umrah together) is like the mufrid (one performing Hajj only); only one value is obligatory. Uprooting is like cutting. Fasting has no place in these. The conclusion is that the trees and herbage of the Haram are of four types: three of them are permissible to cut and benefit from without penalty, and one is not permissible to cut and benefit from without penalty. As for the first three: every tree planted by people and is of the kind that people plant; every tree planted by people and is not of the kind that people plant; and every tree that grows by itself and is of the kind that people plant – these are permissible to cut, because what people plant is normally not entitled to inviolability by consensus, and what does not normally grow, if planted by people, becomes like what grows normally. As for the one that is not permissible to cut: every tree that grows by itself and is not of the kind that people plant. Even if something that does not normally grow grows by itself in a man's property, like a gum arabic tree (umm ghilan) – which is a type of siwak tree from which gum arabic forms – the cutter must pay its value to its owner, and its value is for the right of the Law, just as if he killed owned game in the Haram. (Fath) Except what is dried: i.e., he is liable for its value except for the tree of the Haram that has dried, then he is not liable and it is permissible to benefit from it, because it is firewood and not growing. For this reason, it is permissible to take truffles from it because they do not grow. The inviolability due to the Haram applies only to what is growing. And broken trees are like dry ones. It is mentioned in the books that cutting herbage absolutely requires a penalty, and the difference between it and trees is not apparent. If the exception were from herbage and trees, it would be in accordance with analogy. (Fath) Except idhkhir: i.e., grazing the herbage of the Haram and cutting it is prohibited except idhkhir, for which cutting and grazing are permitted. It grows in plains and mountains, has a fine root and slender twigs, and is fragrant. The best quality is in Mecca; they use it to roof houses between the beams and to fill gaps in graves between the bricks. The basis for this is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: “Its fresh grass is not to be cut, nor its thorns to be broken.” Ibn Abbas said: O Messenger of Allah, except idhkhir, for it is for grazing our animals and for our graves. He said: “Except idhkhir.” This is called a prompted exception. They also have a prompted conjunction. From it they said: “and the ones who shorten” in the hadith. Abu Yusuf said: there is no harm in grazing the herbage due to hardship for visitors and residents. The proof against him is what we narrated. Cutting with lips is like cutting with sickles. Bringing herbage from outside the Haram is easy, so there is no hardship. Even if there is hardship, it is not considered, because hardship is only considered where there is no text; but when the text is contrary, it is not considered.
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (dalil naqli) concerning the penalty for cutting plants and trees in the Haram of Mecca. It distinguishes between fresh and dry plants, and also specifies an exception for idhkhir (a fragrant grass). The text also includes a classification of four types of trees based on their origin and whether they are typically planted by humans. The main ruling is that cutting fresh, uncultivated plants requires payment of value, while dry plants are exempt. The proof is the hadith where the Prophet prohibited cutting the fresh grass of Mecca but made an exception for idhkhir upon Ibn Abbas' request. The passage also includes a view of Abu Yusuf allowing grazing due to hardship, but the text refutes this by citing the clear text of the hadith.

Key Terms
حشيش الحرم (hashish al-haram): The herbage (grass, plants) that grows in the Haram of Mecca.
إذخر (idhkhir): A fragrant grass that grows in Mecca, used for roofing and filling grave gaps.
جزاء (jaza'): The penalty/compensation for cutting plants, which is the value in monetary terms.
كلأ (kala'): Herbage, pasture grass.
نامي (nami): Growing, developing. The inviolability of the Haram applies to growing plants only.
استثناء تلقيني (istithna' talqini): A prompted exception, where the listener suggests an exception and the speaker confirms it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which type of tree in the Haram is NOT permissible to cut without penalty?
A) Trees planted by people of a kind people plant.
B) Trees planted by people of a kind not usually planted.
C) Trees that grow by themselves of a kind people plant.
D) Trees that grow by themselves of a kind not usually planted.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that cutting fresh, uncultivated plants in the Haram is haram and requires compensation, with clear exceptions for dried plants and idhkhir, based on a prophetic hadith.
